Current Affairs Commentary

Heng 29

The Future of the Saar Question 30

According to a Berlin dispatch on the 2nd, the German government has issued a notice to the people of the Saar, ordering them to prepare for the "plebiscite" next year in accordance with the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles, in order to determine the ownership of this region. If we are not forgetful, we should remember that Hitler once directly negotiated with France, demanding the immediate return of the Saar, and declaring that if France agreed to his request, Germany would have no further demands. Hitler always vowed to restore lost territories, yet his territorial demands on France were so small, which was beyond the expectations of the world. However, Hitler's request was still rejected by France. Now, judging from Hitler's notice, he has abandoned his original claim and yielded to the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles. The National Socialist Party's attitude has become so docile, not only inconsistent with its usual rhetoric, but also far inferior to that of other political parties. Although the foreign policy stances of other political parties are not very strong, they can still achieve the goal of reducing reparations and make considerable revisions to the Treaty of Versailles. Since coming to power, Hitler has been harsh and arrogant, regarding the world as nothing, thinking that diplomacy can also be achieved through threats, just like seizing domestic power. As a result, he has alienated various countries and become isolated and helpless. Although his attitude has gradually become silent and softened, he still cannot gain people's trust and sympathy. Whether the Saar region can be returned to Germany in the future is greatly related to Hitler's policies. Let me venture to offer my humble opinion.

According to the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles, after the Saar region has been governed by the Governing Commission organized by the League of Nations for fifteen years, the local people can hold a vote to decide on three issues: (1) Maintaining the status quo, that is, continuing to be governed by the League of Nations. (2) Merging with France. (3) Returning to Germany. When these three issues are put to a vote next year, the truth will naturally come out and a final solution will be obtained. However, judging from the various current situations, there are great problems as to whether this region can be returned to Germany. If Germany did not have a person like Hitler, I dare to predict that the return of the Saar to Germany next year would not be much of a problem. But in today's Hitler's dictatorship, it is very unpredictable. The difficulties that can be pointed out are: First, France's attitude. Since the Nazi Party has been carrying out large-scale activities in the Saar region, France has used its influence in the Saar Governing Commission to actively suppress them. At the same time, it advocates preventing the Nazi Party from manipulating the voting movement of Saar residents next year. According to a Geneva dispatch on the 2nd of this month, this issue has been included in the agenda of the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting that will open in the middle of this month. It can be seen that France has already prepared to manipulate the voting movement in the Saar next year. This is one of the difficulties for the Saar to return to Germany.

Second, although the 800,000 residents of the Saar are all Germans, most of them are Catholics. The power of the German Centre Party accounts for half of the entire population and can be said to be the only major party in the Saar region. However, this political party represents the Catholic Church, and its nature is the same as that of the Christian Social Party led by Dollfuss in Austria (now merged with the Austrian Home Guard and has become a fascist political party). It was this Christian Social Party, which represents Catholics, that opposed Hitler's movement to merge Germany and Austria in Austria. The reason why Catholics rejected the Nazi Party was that they did not want to be controlled by the Nazi Party. If the Nazi Party gains power, not only will other political parties have no room for existence, but even the Catholic Church will be controlled by it. This fact has already been performed in Germany and it is difficult to guarantee that it will not affect other German regions. The Germans in Austria know this, so they would rather cooperate with the Latin-speaking Italy than merge with the German-speaking Germany. Now, using the example of Austria to speculate on the Saar, even if it is not exactly the same, it is not far off. On the one hand, the Catholics in Germany still have disputes with the Nazi Party. On the other hand, the Centre Party, which represents German Catholics, has been eliminated by the Nazi Party since Hitler came to power. It is not as good as the Saar Centre Party under the rule of the League of Nations, which can still operate freely. From this point of view, the Catholics and the Centre Party in the Saar, learning from the past, will inevitably be wary and do not want the Saar to return to Germany. This is the second difficulty.

Third, the workers in the Saar mining area are mostly guided by the Social Democratic Party and the Communist Party. These political parties have been wiped out by the Nazi Party in Germany. Their resentment towards the Nazi Party must be far greater than before Hitler came to power. Recently, it has been heard that France has tried to accommodate these political parties, ordering their party newspapers to step up their propaganda against the return of the Saar to Germany. This is the third difficulty for the Saar to return to Germany. Moreover, since Hitler came to power, many people who are not tolerated in Germany have gathered in the Saar. These exiles will inevitably oppose Hitler's success. This can be asserted.

Based on these points, even if a vote is held in the Saar region next year, it may be difficult to return to Germany. The result may be to maintain the status quo and continue to be governed by the League of Nations. If so, Germany's diplomacy will suffer another failure.

US and Japan Compete to Expand Air Force; First Batch of 110 Aircraft; US Army Department Invites Bids; Japan Actively Proceeding with Expansion Plan 31

(Washington) The Army Department announced today that, in order to proceed with the three-year air force program, it will soon invite bids for the construction of eighty bombers and thirty attack aircraft, a total of one hundred and ten aircraft, costing approximately $7.5 million. The second bidding will be held before July. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

Comparison of Air Power Among Various Countries 32

Hualian News Agency, Tokyo Dispatch According to the Asahi Shimbun, the Ministry of the Army has decided to greatly expand the air force from next year. Currently, various agencies under its jurisdiction are actively preparing and investigating the current air force situation of various countries. The following is a record: (Naval Air Force excluded) Japan: 26 air squadrons, 2 balloon squadrons, with a total of 1,000 aircraft. The aviation budget for this year is approximately 26 million yuan.

England: Air squadrons: 75 in England itself, 23 in British colonies. Domestically: 13 fighter squadrons, 10 army cooperation squadrons, 34 light bomber squadrons, 50 heavy bomber squadrons, 1 communication squadron, 7 flying boat squadrons. Each squadron has approximately 1,500 aircraft. The budget for 1933 was 19,638,600 pounds. Air force personnel: 3,150 officers, 25,042 non-commissioned officers and below. Future plans: Increase squadrons to 89, aircraft to 2,072, and personnel to 40,000. United States: 21 fighter squadrons, 14 attack squadrons, 14 reconnaissance squadrons, 12 bomber squadrons, totaling 51 squadrons, 1 aviation school training squadron, 1 balloon squadron, 2 airship squadrons, 16 flight service squadrons. Total number of aircraft: 1,760. The budget for 1933-34 is $27,042,337. Number of officers: 1,615, number of non-commissioned officers: 14,000. Future five-year plan: 2,800 aircraft. France: 35 fighter squadrons, 46 reconnaissance and observation squadrons, 9 light bomber squadrons, 18 heavy bomber squadrons, 2 protection squadrons, totaling 110 squadrons. Others: 18 balloon squadrons, 24 squadrons in French colonies. Total number of aircraft: 3,000. The budget for 1933 was 1,694,130,000 French francs. Number of officers: 2,900, number of non-commissioned officers: 30,412. Future plans: 201 squadrons. Italy: 36 fighter squadrons, 28 reconnaissance squadrons, 31 bomber squadrons, 14 training squadrons, other (type unknown)

14 squadrons, totaling 123 squadrons, 2 balloon squadrons. Recently changed organization: 42 main force battalions, 4 army cooperation regiments, Italian colonial forces separately designated. Current total number of aircraft: 1,500. Budget for 1933-34: 695,948,000 Italian lire. Number of officers: 2,437, number of non-commissioned officers: 4,188, number of soldiers: 25,029.

Russia: Russia is extremely secretive. Roughly as follows: 46 fighter squadrons, 87 reconnaissance squadrons, 46 bomber squadrons, 31 attack squadrons and others, totaling 210 squadrons, 13 balloon squadrons, 32 naval aircraft squadrons, totaling approximately 2,500 aircraft.

US Navy on the East Coast of Panama

Exercises for Unit; Defending the West Indies as the Goal; Determining Future Naval Policy 33

(Washington) After the US fleet departs from the Panama Canal

Zone tomorrow, it will conduct combat exercises against a hypothetical enemy, who is believed to have challenged the US naval hegemony in the Caribbean Sea. Fleet No. 15 of the Question Mark will demonstrate how to defend the Panama Canal and the US East Coast after a battle fleet suffers a defeat at the start of a war. This will give the peaceful US Marine Corps a taste of hardship. According to the simulated combat program, the hypothetical enemy fleet will occupy the US naval base in the West Indies and concentrate strong naval forces on the sea there, creating a wartime situation. Representing the United States is a battle fleet, commanded by Admiral Reeves. The hypothetical enemy is represented by a reconnaissance fleet,

led by Vice Admiral Blumbe. The commander-in-chief of the US fleet

is Admiral Sello, who will supervise the battle from the flagship Pennsylvania. Both sides are equipped with equal air forces and one aircraft carrier each. The Marine Corps is concentrated in the Canal Zone, serving as the attacking force, landing under the cover of the fleet's heavy artillery, and occupying the forward base. Marine Corps Commander Lehman is the former commander of the US Marine Corps in Shanghai. All ships will turn off their lights at night, guarding against enemy attacks. Officers and soldiers will practice at the combat location from time to time, and will open fire and bombard as soon as they encounter the hypothetical enemy. The only difference from a real war is that live ammunition will not be used. According to the US Navy's previous exercise, it was conducted in February 1933 by Fleet No. 14 of the Question Mark between the Hawaiian Islands and the Pacific coast. According to the official report, various fleets and aircraft carriers have made significant progress in that exercise. Secretary of the Navy Swanson declared in his last annual report: "The annual concentration and occasional tactical exercises of the fleet have great effects on the training of naval personnel and will continue to be held." The results of the Caribbean Sea exercise this time will have a significant relationship to the US policy and naval shipbuilding plan in the future naval

conference. (National Telegram on the 4th)

Soviet Russia's Plan

Opening a Grand Canal; From Moscow via the Volga River; Directly to the Black Sea, 700 Miles Long; Most of the Project Funds Come from the United States 34

(Moscow) The Soviet Russian authorities today approved the construction of a huge canal, 700 miles long, from Moscow via the Volga River to the Black Sea, capable of accommodating 10,000-ton ships. Once this plan is completed, Moscow will be transformed into an artificial seaport. This project is being prepared by American engineers, and most of the funding is also

coming from the United States. Construction will begin next month. The motivation for this major project is that railway transportation is inconvenient and the industrialization of Moscow has been greatly affected. The Moscow Government Labor Corps has specially used a large number of cement to build a large ground, so that Moscow has a small-scale military port. The Military Commission will also propose building new-style pocket battleships for navigation on inland rivers. (National Telegram on the 4th)

Australia and Finland

Order Aircraft from England 35

(London) The Finnish government has ordered a large number of 640-horsepower bombers from England, with a speed of 320 kilometers per hour, which is equivalent to that used by the British Royal Air Force. The State of Australia has also ordered 24 military aircraft from the British Vickers factory, worth a total of 345,000 pounds. (National Telegram on the 5th)

Between Paris and Tokyo

Attempt to Fly Non-Stop; Depart from Paris on the 23rd of this Month; Another Feat by Two French Aviators 36

(Paris) Two famous French aviators, Codoss and Rossi, departed from New York in August last year and flew across the Atlantic Ocean, directly reaching the city of Layak in Syria, covering a distance of 5,900 miles without stopping, setting a world record for long-distance straight-line flight. They now intend to abandon their original plan to fly to South America and Indochina, and will depart from the Bourget Airport on May 23 and fly to Tokyo, Japan. The two aviators' aircraft is currently parked at the Port of Ille-de-France in southern France and will be transported in a few days. The long-distance flight between Paris and Tokyo is approximately 6,030 miles. The aviator Tolais once tried to fly this route but failed. Now Codoss and Rossi also intend to take the same route. (Havas dispatch on the 5th)

Paris City Government

Receives Japanese Naval Students 37

(Paris) Representatives of the Paris City Government received officers and trainees of the Japanese Imperial Naval Academy and fleet at the City Hall this morning. Sato, the Japanese ambassador to France, also participated in the ceremony. The President of the Paris City Council, Fiquet, delivered a welcome speech, which Sato thanked. The ceremony of playing the national anthems of France and Japan then concluded. (Havas dispatch on the 5th)

Response to the US Memorandum

Japan is Unwilling to Remain Silent and Weak; Plans to Issue Another Statement at an Appropriate Opportunity; US Plans to Unite with England to Punish Japanese Goods 38

(Tokyo) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a memorandum regarding the unofficial statement made by the United States on April 30 regarding Japan's policy towards China. As a result of deliberations on how Japan should deal with this, it was generally agreed that although there is no need to issue a statement against the United States at the moment, failing to express any intention would lead the United States to misunderstand that the Japanese government acquiesces in the US memorandum and fully acknowledges the US point of view. Therefore, in order to eliminate future misunderstandings, it is necessary to clearly express Japan's beliefs at an appropriate opportunity through statements and other methods. This view is generally consistent. (Dentsu dispatch on the 5th)

(Washington) State Department officials today expressed satisfaction with the current trend of the Far Eastern situation. The attitude taken by French Foreign Minister Barthou in replying to the Japanese note was particularly pleasing to the State Department. Officials here believe that France's note upholding the Nine-Power Treaty is a full endorsement of Secretary of State Hull's firm opposition to Japan's Asian Monroe Doctrine. An Associated Press reporter also learned that State Department officials were also very satisfied with the warning issued by British Minister of Commerce Runciman to Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira in London yesterday. It is said that if the United States has a way, it will also take the same action as England to deal with the cheap sale of Japanese goods. State Department officials said that the British-Japanese trade war does not affect American commerce. Regarding the difficult situation of British-Japanese cotton industry competition, the Federal Tariff Commission announced that the President has approved the implementation of a tax increase on Japanese-branded canned food from May 31, which has attracted attention from all parties. The tax increase method is based on the US sales price, not the foreign price, and is 35% ad valorem. At the same time, the ad valorem tax on Canadian-branded canned food will be reduced from 35% to 23%. (National Telegram on the 4th)

League of Nations Assists Our Construction

Japan Has No Right to Interfere; Minister Hu's Declaration in Geneva 39

(Geneva) Hu Shih-tse, the Chinese Minister to Switzerland, spoke to an Associated Press reporter today, pointing out that Japan's attempt to create hegemony in the Far East has failed, and it is likely to vent its anger on Rajchman, the liaison officer between the League of Nations and China. Minister Hu declared, "Japan's declaration has aroused public outrage around the world. The Japanese are eager to save this matter, so they do not hesitate to turn Rajchman into their target of attack. The Japanese have no right to arbitrarily approve or disapprove of the League of Nations' assistance to China's construction. There are many reasons for this. The Japanese have withdrawn from the League of Nations and have no intention of returning, which is one. The tenth provision of the League of Nations General Assembly's report on the Sino-Japanese incident on February 24, 1933, suggested cooperation between China and the League of Nations, which is the second. The Japanese opposed this report at that time, which is the third reason. Because the Japanese do not trust this plan, it is absurd for the Japanese to oppose this major issue if it is unfavorable to them." (National Telegram on the 4th)

Technical Cooperation with Us

League of Nations Has Not Changed; Report on Avenueol's Conversation with Yokoyama is Untrue 40

(Geneva) The Secretary-General of the League of Nations issued a communique today stating that the report on the conversation between Yokoyama, the Japanese Consul-General in Geneva, and Avenueol, the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, is untrue. During this conversation, the Secretary-General took the opportunity to inform the Japanese Consul-General of the Administrative Council of the League of Nations' resolution on technical cooperation with China and the specific content under the implementation of this resolution, in order to eliminate possible misunderstandings. He did not say that any changes are being made. (Reuters dispatch on the 5th)

US Newspaper Anti-Japanese Remarks; Account for 75 Percent 41

(New York) A New York newspaper stated that if the comments of US newspapers on the Far Eastern situation are summarized into charts, 75 percent of all newspapers severely criticize the Japanese government, and the comments of the remaining newspapers are more moderate. (TASS dispatch on the 2nd)

Explanation to the Japanese Envoy

French Newspapers Praise and Criticize 42

(Paris) French newspapers today criticized Japanese Ambassador Sato's explanation to French Foreign Minister Barthou regarding Japan's policy towards China, with both praise and criticism. The Paris Times, a semi-official organ, naturally offered many compliments.

Japan May Tear Up the Treaty at Any Time; However, the Paris 43

Evening Post raised questions, saying, "Will Japan seize power by destroying the Nine-Power Treaty when people are unprepared, as it did in the League of Nations?" (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

Internal Political Worries Should Be Stopped; ⊙Paris 44

Japanese Ambassador to France Sato formally visited Foreign Minister Barthou yesterday to explain the declaration made by the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs spokesman on April 17. The Times published an editorial today, stating that the Japanese government automatically explained its views without waiting for the formal inquiry of the French government. This courteous act is enough to eliminate all misunderstandings in principle and in fact. From the statement of the Japanese ambassador, it can be seen that the views officially stated by the Tokyo government are more of a retreat than the views stated in a semi-official form by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs spokesman on April 17, and the threat of all disputes seems to have been avoided at present. Because Japan is currently facing various difficulties in its internal affairs, and various opposing trends are confronting each other, it is not allowed to make a decisive gamble. The French reply also resolutely stated that if Japan believes that a certain interference is sufficient to hinder the order and justice in the Far East, then whether in law or in fact, Japan can only consult the opinions of the signatory countries in accordance with the procedures stipulated in the Washington Nine-Power Treaty. As for other methods, they are not recognized by France. (Havas dispatch on the 4th)

Provoking the United States is Tantamount to Insulting; ⊙Paris 45

Several newspapers this morning commented on the Far Eastern issue. This complex and serious situation will cause a reaction in Geneva. At that time, Japan will treat the rights of the powers in China in a generous manner in order to ease the hearts of the powers.

British Government

Preparing to Implement a Trade War Against Japan: Banning the Import of Cotton Goods and Artificial Silk; Japan to Request Britain to Postpone Implementation 49

(Tokyo) A Reuters correspondent today visited the spokesperson of the Japanese Foreign Ministry to inquire whether the memorandum issued by British Trade Secretary Runciman was in the nature of an ultimatum. The spokesperson replied that the memorandum had just been completely translated and needed further study before any comments could be made. The drafting of a reply would also take several days, as it was necessary to consult with business leaders. At the same time, various newspapers expressed the opinion that the quota system would not seriously affect Japanese trade in the British territories, as Japanese goods sales had continued to increase despite repeated tax increases in the various British territories. It was also doubtful whether the quota system would affect Japanese trade with the British Dominions, as Japan's exports were currently continuing to increase. In April of this year, the increase amounted to 33 million Japanese yen compared to April of last year. The world orders received by Osaka have already extended to August of this year. Therefore, it seems difficult to agree with Britain's opinion. According to the prediction of a certain Japanese newspaper, the Japanese government will adopt a tough attitude, even if trade negotiations break down as a result. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

(Tokyo) Japanese Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira sent a telegram to the Foreign Ministry on the 5th, reporting the contents of the memorandum delivered by British Trade Secretary Runciman. According to the telegram, the British government limited the types of goods to be discussed in the Anglo-Japanese talks to cotton cloth and artificial silk, and the agreed-upon region was mainland Britain and its directly administered colonies. The measure to be taken this time was an import allocation system, applied to cotton cloth and artificial silk. For Japanese silk, it was planned to increase tariffs. If Japan did not express a compromising attitude in the Anglo-Japanese talks, it was planned to start an Anglo-Japanese economic war. After receiving this telegram, the Japanese Foreign Ministry studied countermeasures. Because confrontation with Britain would be unfavorable to Japan, it was planned to avoid an economic war and request Britain to postpone the implementation of the allocation system, or to present a Japanese proposal to Britain. (Japan United Press dispatch, 5th)

(Tokyo) According to a telegram received by the Foreign Ministry on the 4th from Ambassador Matsudaira in Britain, British Trade Secretary Runciman met with Ambassador Matsudaira on the 3rd and personally handed over a memorandum regarding Anglo-Japanese trade. He also told Matsudaira that the contents of the memorandum would be announced in the British Parliament on the 7th. Matsudaira immediately asked the Trade Secretary whether it was true that the British government planned to implement an import allocation system for Japanese goods, as reported in the newspapers. The Trade Secretary replied that the import allocation system was still under consideration and had not yet been decided. Furthermore, the Japanese goods to which the system would be applied were limited to special commercial goods such as cotton cloth and artificial silk, and would not be applied to general merchandise. According to the Trade Secretary's reply, the British government seemed to intend to implement an import allocation system for Japanese goods, and the Japanese government attached great importance to its future. (Japan United Press dispatch, 5th)

(Washington) The State Department and the Commerce Department are currently studying the extent to which the low prices of Japanese goods in the Philippines, Hawaii, Panama, Puerto Rico, and Alaska are damaging American goods. Officials from both departments believe that Britain and its colonies have agreed to boycott Japanese goods, but it is difficult for the United States to follow suit. The fall in prices of Japanese goods has led to an increasing demand for them in various American territories, but the rate of increase is not of a serious nature compared to the total amount of Japanese trade. For example, in 1931, Japanese goods imported into the United States were valued at 425,330,000 Japanese yen, and in 1933 this had only increased to 492,113,700 yen. Furthermore, in 1911, the Philippine Islands purchased Japanese goods worth a total of 20,425,000 yen, and in 1933 this had only increased to 24,050,000 yen. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese government has decided to allocate 200,000 yen from the second reserve fund for expenses related to the Japanese-Dutch talks. This will be submitted to the regular cabinet meeting on the 8th, requesting the approval of all cabinet members. (Dentsu dispatch, 5th)

Britain to Implement New Taxes

Our Egg Industry Affected 50

(London) According to an official announcement made today, a new tax will be implemented from May 8th, which will affect the Chinese egg industry importing to Britain. Currently, shelled eggs are taxed ad valorem, but in the future, they will be taxed by weight. Liquid or solidified eggs, including those prepared with glycerin, will be taxed at half a penny per pound. Whole dried eggs will be taxed at two pence and twenty-five hundredths per pound, dried egg yolk at one penny and twenty-five hundredths per pound, and dried egg white at two pence and seventy-five hundredths per pound. Furthermore, unground pepper will be taxed at five shillings and six pence per 112 pounds, also effective from May 8th. This new tax is approximately equivalent to 10% of the current average import value of the items listed. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

Germany Restricts Imports 51

(Berlin) According to an announcement by the authorities, German imports will continue to be greatly reduced. Since October 1930, importers have been allowed to purchase foreign currency up to a maximum of 50% of their needs. In April of this year, this was reduced to 17.5%, and now it has been reduced again to 12.5%. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

⊙Simla The Indian government today announced far-reaching proposals to create a unified strategy to seek national economic improvement. United States Proceeding

Plan to Raise Prices: Not Focusing on Currency Devaluation 53

(Washington) According to information obtained from responsible sources, the authorities are currently implementing a plan to raise prices. The plan intends to start with stimulating commercial activities through indirect methods, and does not focus on experimental methods of currency devaluation. It is now believed that President Roosevelt still hopes that prices can be raised to be equal to those in 1926, but progress is slower than expected. Administrative leaders are still engaged in the price increase movement, and have not expressed impatience due to the slow progress. For example, officials of the Agricultural Adjustment Administration did not express excessive alarm over the recent decline in wheat prices. The authorities are urgently trying to raise prices in order to reduce the national debt and to allow real estate to circulate. For example, the $200 million Exchange Stabilization Fund will be used to devalue the currencies of non-gold standard countries in order to promote the sales of American goods in those countries. This step will also promote the increase of domestic prices. (National News Agency dispatch, 4th)

(Washington) Interior Secretary Ickes told the Associated Press today that big business has already forgotten the lessons of the depression. The Public Works Administration plans to allocate another 500 million US dollars as construction reserves. This amount will be requested from the current Congress, and will be distributed according to the expenditure procedures of the Public Works Administration. Therefore, the reconstruction funds have reached 4 billion US dollars. The previously allocated 3.3 billion was distributed completely in six months. This is the largest expenditure in peacetime, and has not been seen in any country or any place. The 500 million dollars now allocated is a part of President Roosevelt's 2.2 billion dollar budget, which has been designated by President Roosevelt for the next fiscal year. Roosevelt's allocation procedures are as follows: 600 million for relief, 500 million for public works, and 100 million for the Agricultural Credit Administration and domestic public debt. (National News Agency dispatch, 4th)

US House Passes

Securities Exchange Management Act 55

(Washington) The Securities Exchange Management Act was passed in the House today by a vote of 280 to 84. There was a great deal of support for the bill, so amendments that would weaken its effectiveness were all defeated. The bill has now been sent to the Senate, and debate is expected to begin in the middle of next week. Although the Senate also has a similar plan, it differs greatly from the one passed by the House. The key points of the bill passed by the House are: (1) all securities exchanges must register with the Federal Trade Commission; (2) the Federal Reserve Board has the power to determine the maximum amount of margin, with the normal margin being 45%; (3) various manipulative acts to raise prices are prohibited. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

American Bandit Still Not Captured

Causing a City-Wide Uproar; Wabash, Indiana Bank Robbed Again; Dillinger Suspected of Being Involved 56

(New York) A bank in Fort Recovery, Ohio, was robbed by two armed bandits today, and five people were injured. It is generally believed that the notorious bandit Dillinger must be one of the two bandits. The two bandits were neatly dressed, looking like ordinary customers. They entered the bank without arousing suspicion that they were carrying weapons. However, after entering, they immediately brandished their submachine guns. The employees of the bank could not resist, and cash and securities worth 18,000 dollars were stolen. When leaving, the bandits forced one male and one female employee to walk in front of them as shields. At this time, the bank employee had already sent out a warning signal. The bandits knew that the situation was urgent, so they quickly took the loot into a car parked on the side of the road, and made the two employees stand on either side of the car's fenders. They drove off quickly. The bank employees chased them to the outside of the bank, firing shots remotely. However, it was too late. The police heard the alarm but did not chase them either, but they were all afraid of accidentally injuring the innocent employees next to the car, so they did not dare to shoot freely. When the chasers and the two bandits exchanged gunfire, five of the chasers were injured. The bandits finally escaped. After the car had gone a long distance, the bandits ordered the two employees to get out of the car. After this case occurred, 10,000 central soldiers and police immediately engaged in a large-scale search in Ohio and Indiana, hoping to capture the fugitives. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

(London) The United States Department of Justice has requested the China Hsing Steamship Company to investigate the report that the notorious American bandit Dillinger took the Duchess of York from Halifax on Monday to England. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

(New York) The police heard that two bandits were trying to set fire to something in a certain area, and rushed to arrest them. But the bandits opened fire to resist arrest, causing two police officers to be injured. The bandits escaped in a car. Later, a street policeman saw suspicious people sitting in a car and intended to stop them from proceeding, but was shot and killed by the people in the car. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

Creditors' Meeting

Difficult to Reach a Compromise with Germany; Creditors Criticize Germany's Reserve Report as Inconsistent 63

Germany May Unilaterally Announce Suspension of Debt Payments (Berlin) Meetings continue between the German Central Bank and representatives of various creditor nations, with the Central Bank reporting that the ongoing meetings are a fortune, though representatives of both parties are still arguing. Creditors believe that Germany has not reported true figures of its currency reserves, with recent official announcements being too bleak and inconsistent with reality. The Central Bank remains firm that there are no secret stores of currency, though admitted that there are 149 million marks worth of 15 and 3 month promissory notes not included in formal announcements. Additionally, the "Gold Discount Bank" has 60 million marks worth of promissory notes that can be collected. Germany also has long-term accounts receivable such as Soviet payment notes for purchases, again not reported by the Central Bank. In the year alone, the Soviet Union has transferred 680 million golden marks to Germany for payment of goods, revealing the inconsistencies of Germany's reporting. Certain individuals have claimed that it is difficult for the creditor nations and the Central Bank to come to an agreement, and that as a result, Germany may unilaterally announce suspension of debt payments. Japan's New Diplomatic Strategy (Japan Communication) Arita First Returns Home Hirota's Statement Intended 86

Foreign Minister Hirota's so-called "moral diplomacy" and a new diplomatic lineup have, in practice, achieved considerable success in diplomacy towards the United States. Now, he intends to gradually summon ambassadors and ministers stationed abroad back to Japan to discuss new strategies. The first to be summoned back is Ambassador to China, Ariyoshi Akira. From the steps and timing of his return, one can glean the importance of Ariyoshi's return. According to Hirota's intentions, Japan's diplomacy towards China is planning to take advantage of this opportunity to shift away from its previous fierce image and adopt a relatively moderate approach.

Attempted Economic Alliance

Focus on Dealing with the Soviet Union

However, the military still strongly advocates a hardline stance, believing that Japan should at least obtain a so-called special position in China, and that this special position must be recognized by all countries in the world, requiring at least the understanding of Britain and the United States. Therefore, Director of the Foreign Ministry's Intelligence Department, Amau Eiji, turned Foreign Minister Hirota's words into an informal conversation and used it as a form of propaganda material to publicize to the world. While stating Japan's position, it also sought the understanding of the military. Unexpectedly, this aroused reactions from world opinion and prompted serious attention from Britain and the United States. As a result, Hirota ordered ambassadors and ministers stationed abroad to explain everywhere, especially to Britain and the United States, providing more detailed explanations, clarifying that Japan does not intend to close off the East's door, meaning that even the door of Manchuria could be opened, as a strategy.

The important event of Ariyoshi's return home is to report the true situation in China. However, one particularly important aspect is to promote the so-called Sino-Japanese economic alliance. Because of this matter, among the general economic circles in China, there are naturally few supporters and many opponents, making it difficult to achieve appropriate and satisfactory results. On the international front, everyone wants to obtain preferential benefits and is unwilling to let Japan monopolize them, especially in the Pacific region, where the stakes are high. Japan must carefully handle it. Ariyoshi's mission in returning home is to discuss these kinds of countermeasures, to see what kind of tactics to use so as not to provoke the resentment of the great powers, to allow the United States and Britain to adopt a bystander's attitude, and at the same time, how to restrain China from silently obeying its arrangements. The specific details are not yet very clear, but the general principles have been decided.

Japan's preparation for war against the Soviet Union has almost become an open secret. However, when and how this war will be launched is still unknown. Currently, or in the near future, Japan does not yet have the determination to attack the Soviet Union. The biggest reason is that international relations have not been handled well. Various projects in the Northeast have just begun, and Japan's own military preparations have not been completed, especially the expansion of the air force and tank corps, which are not yet fully equipped. The economic situation in its own country, apart from the military industry, is still struggling in a recession. Therefore, it is unwilling to immediately challenge. Therefore, its first priority is to complete its so-called "Japan-Manchuria Economic Alliance," which goes without saying that it is to bring all the economic power of the four northeastern provinces under the control of Japan, and under the sole management of the military. Even the Mitsui and Mitsubishi Zaibatsu must listen to the military's command. According to the military's view, the so-called "Japan-Manchuria Economic Alliance" is primarily for national defense. This national defense, needless to say, refers to the projects in the Greater Khingan Range area, as well as the military installations in the Muling area, and the new planned seven major railway lines within the borders of the four northeastern provinces, as well as the steel industry, nitrogen industry, etc. The military construction in the Greater Khingan Range has already been implemented step by step, to be completed no later than the summer of next year. Several important railways, especially the Jehol railway, will be completed this year.

What the Japanese militarists lack confidence in now is still international diplomatic relations. It still has vigilance towards China, wanting to have a reliable solution as soon as possible. It is even more anxious about Britain and the United States. If serious problems arise between Japan and the Soviet Union, and if Britain and the United States maintain a strict neutral attitude and do not provide Japan with material assistance, its steel raw materials and petroleum and other important resources will have no source, and the result will inevitably be to fall into a tragic situation. Therefore, Hirota's diplomacy, on the one hand, seeks understanding from Britain and the United States, finding factors of reconciliation, and on the other hand, wants to monopolize the Far East market without revealing traces. This is to discuss with Ariyoshi how to play this set of tricks. (April 30th, Tokyo)

Japanese Troops in Jidong

Military Telephones Extensively Installed Already Erected in More Than Two Counties Military Exercises Daily 87

Tianjin Communication: The Japanese troops stationed in North China have been very active recently. The troops stationed east of Tangshan and at various passes along the Great Wall conduct combat exercises every few days. The Asami Battalion of the Tangshan Japanese Army has conducted field exercises at the local Western Hills shooting range five times in the past month alone. Sometimes they notify our side before the exercises, and sometimes they conduct live-fire exercises late at night. Residents are awakened in their sleep, fleeing in panic. By the time the truth is understood, the Japanese army's exercises have already ended. Afterwards, the Japanese army informs our local authorities by telephone, explaining the course of the exercises, but by then the incident has already passed, the people's panic has subsided, and notification and explanation are too late. Similar incidents occur wherever Japanese troops are stationed in Jidong, causing deep disturbance. The Japanese troops stationed at various passes along the Great Wall form teams, enter various counties by car to survey the terrain, and photograph strategic locations, in countless instances. It is not known what the Japanese army's intentions are with such busyness. The Japanese troops stationed in various places have freely erected military telephone lines in ten locations, including Xinglong, Malan峪, Gubeikou, Tangshan, Zunhua, Linyu, Qian'an, Fengrun, Funing, and Luanxian. Their telephone lines are all hung on our long-distance telephone poles. The long-distance telephone bureau has telegraphed the provincial government in detail, requesting that the matter be included in the case for negotiations. The province has instructed Tao Shangming and Yin Rugeng to negotiate with the Japanese to remove the lines, but it is not certain whether this will be effective. The Japanese troops stationed in Beijing and Tangshan conducted a long-distance military vehicle exercise again on the 30th of last month. A heavy truck departed from Beiping, driven by 25 Japanese soldiers, passed through the Ping-Sui Line, and drove to Nankou, planning to camp overnight in Nankou. On April 2nd, it returned to Beiping along the original route. Three military vehicles departed from Tangshan, driven by a Japanese squad, and drove along the Beining Line to Tianjin. They departed on April 30th, camped in Hanzhuang on the first day, arrived in Tianjin at noon on the second day, went to Yixingbu south of Tianjin on the third day, and returned to Tangshan in the afternoon. In addition, on April 29th, two squads of Japanese troops, about 70 soldiers, arrived in Ninghe County from Bin Di County. After arriving in the county, they divided into two teams, one team went to the suburbs to survey, and the other team erected telephone lines and tried to communicate with Japanese troops in various places. On the morning of the 30th, they conducted street fighting exercises in the streets, disturbing the entire county's merchants, who closed their doors and stopped business, daring not go out. In the evening, the Japanese troops began to head towards Fengrun, and the area returned to peace. The Japanese troops stationed in Malanyu conducted field artillery exercises near the Qing Tombs on the morning of April 1st, firing dozens of cannons. Nearby residents all thought a major war was coming and fled in panic. By noon, the Japanese army's exercises stopped, and the people realized the truth and gradually returned to their original residences. These are all recent shows of force by the Japanese army, and we have no way to protest to stop them. (May 3rd)

Northwest Inspection Notes Special Correspondent Geng Ya's Miscellaneous News from Baotou 88

Mr. Li Yunyu, editor of the Baotou Daily, sends a copy of the newspaper to me daily, which I appreciate. To report on the local conditions and customs, I was guided to visit the only scenic spot in Baotou, the "Zhuanlongzang." Stepping out of the eastern suburbs, a slope faces you, with a low-lying middle section. The majestic temple corners tower high among the forests. This is the Zhuanlongzang. Climbing the slope northward, one sees the ruins of a radio station, which was built and then destroyed by Feng Yuxiang. Passing a stage on flat ground, one enters the "Longquan Temple" gate. In the courtyard, a spring gushes from the ground, its force almost enough to turn a millstone. The taste is sweet and the color is clear, and it is the drinking water for the entire city. Ascending the steps to the "Little South Sea" gate, a notice is posted: "Women are not allowed to enter the temple without reason." I once visited Yungang in Datong. When female students from a Beiping student tour group occasionally climbed on a stone Buddha, the village women who saw it from afar exclaimed, "That is a woman, how dare she defile the Buddha!" It is evident that the custom of "disparaging women" is still prevalent outside the Great Wall. In the main hall, three Buddha statues are sculpted. Beside the hall stands a stone tablet for famine relief, briefly stating that in the fifteenth year of Baotou, large armies passed through the area, and the local savings were exhausted. In the sixteenth and seventeenth years, a severe drought occurred, spreading throughout the Sui area, coupled with Fu Bu Jing's unrest, causing the people to be displaced. Wang Tingying provided famine relief for three months, spending over four thousand yuan in silver, etc. The abbot is a "Western monk," who is said to have a good understanding of Buddhist scriptures. I briefly talked with him and then left. Leaving the mountain gate, gazing at the scenery of the entire Zang, it all comes into view, as elegant as a natural painting, and the Yellow River fish boats ripple, clearly visible. The refreshing atmosphere is beyond comparison.

According to legend, Baotou was a sandy wasteland in the Qing Dynasty, sparsely populated. Five or ten families gathered into a village, and most of the residents were Mongolian, living purely by nomadic life. Trading was rare, only a few people, all using Naobao as a market, where Mongolians and Han Chinese traded, starting from there. At that time, deer from the Daqingshan Mountains often came to "Zhuanlongzang" to drink spring water. The Mongolians admired them, and the scenery touched their feelings, gradually calling the area in the eastern suburbs "Baogutu." Baogutu is the root of the naming of Baotou. At that time, a Tibetan Grand Lama came to Baotou, hung his staff at Zhuanlongzang, and his medical and fortune-telling skills became famous for a time. When Emperor Kangxi conquered Galdan and returned through Naobao, he expressed admiration and built the Guangjue Temple on Wudang Mountain for him to reside in. At the same time, residents, drinking the water and thinking of the source, also built Guangde Temple for the Lama at Zhuanzang. The number of merchants increased daily, gradually evolving, and Baotou was first opened.

Fuzheng Temple is located in the northeast corner of the city, purely a Mongolian Lama temple. The temple door is tightly closed, with the key hidden in the threshold. Opening the door and entering, the hall is short and deep. On the central table are small photos of the Panchen Lama and scriptures, with more than ten copper bowls of water and many kneeling pads placed beside them. Behind the table at an oblique angle, each has scripture shelves, wrapped in yellow silk, seemingly very precious. Buddha statues are sculpted against the walls, all hideous and terrifying, covered with yellow silk, making it difficult to see the details in the dim room. The guiding lamas all bowed to the table, making a sound by touching the table, and turning to look at us, repeatedly saying "Morocco," meaning that we should perform the ritual like them. Leaving the hall, I invited the lamas to take photos together. At first, they firmly declined, but later, seeing the camera being fully unfolded and the copper frame extended, they

each ran to their Zen rooms, re-arranged their clothes and came out. A certain Grand Lama of Wudang Zhao, who was here to welcome the Xuanhua envoy Zhangjia, also spoke Chinese and volunteered to join the photography. Could it be that interacting with the Mongols is like governing the people, "it is difficult to plan the beginning, but easy to enjoy the success"?

Lamaism is originally a type of Buddhism. During the Zhenguan period of the Tang Dynasty, Buddhism was introduced to Tibet and was mixed with gods, ghosts, and heresies. Therefore, the statues in the temples are mostly gods and monsters. Moreover, in order to adapt to the environment, lamas still eat beef and mutton as usual. This is also completely different from Buddhism. The Mongols are superstitious in Lamaism. For lamas, their glory is almost like the imperial examinations in the Qing Dynasty. At least one son must become a lama, otherwise the Living Buddha will send down illness and disaster. Therefore, the birth rate is declining daily. When a son becomes a lama, it is like entering school, and sometimes the family even relies on supplying expenses. Those tens of thousands of lamas do not engage in production, but live by alms and obtain the people's offerings through political and religious means. The American Andrews said, "The demise of the Mongolian nation is entirely due to Lamaism. If Lamaism can be abolished and the Mongols can receive proper education from the government, there is still hope for Mongolia." This statement is quite reasonable. The people of Sui have proposed popularizing education in Mongolia to replace Lamaism. Mongolians such as "Man Tai, the Chief of the Tumet General Administration" and "Rong Xiang, the Secretary-General of the Mongolian Border Command," are said to be scholars with deep learning, and other Mongolian youths who have received school education, why not work hard for this?

The Mongols use brick tea as currency. In addition to directly bartering furs for rice and cloth, the value of everything else is determined by brick tea. This custom has continued to this day and has not been completely changed. There are "39," "27," and "24" teas. The so-called "24" tea is the brick tea that can be placed in 24 pieces per box. Each "24" box is worth about 33 yuan, each piece weighs five and a half catties, worth one yuan and two or three cents. The red-colored leaves, containing twigs, and the "24" tea that has been soaked for a long time are the most preferred by ordinary Mongols. Holding it to exchange for furs and other items, it can be used as a two-yuan currency. The 39 tea is worth about six cents and can also be used as a one-yuan circulating currency. In addition, there is also Qianliang tea, which seems to be molded from willow trees, so the shape is very similar to willow trunks. When sold, it is sawn horizontally like a cutting board and sells well in Ningxia, Gansu, and other places.

Among the schools in Baotou, there is the Suiyuan Provincial Second Middle School (only offering junior high school), with four classes of co-educational students, about five hundred and sixty students. There are five county-run primary schools, but there are no schools in the villages. Teachers are lacking, mostly hired from outside. Classical scripture private schools are more numerous than schools. Slips of paper saying "So-and-so School will open on the sixteenth day of the first month" are everywhere, but those willing to send their children to school (whether new or old)

are few in number. School-age children do not know how to read and mostly take mud on the streets and alleys, knead it into bowl shapes, throw it on the ground to make a bang, startling passersby, which is a great pity.

The houses here are all single-story. Entering the door, one sees a screen wall, and a small temple is made in the cave wall to worship the local god. Entering another door, four rooms form a courtyard, and the courtyard is very wide. The roofs are mostly flat earthen platforms, easy to go up and down, and can be used for drying things. I once saw a courtyard where mother-in-law and daughter-in-law were quarreling. The neighbors heard it and climbed on the roofs to look down. They were all small-footed women. Hearing loud voices on the road also often comes from high places.

The shop signs in the city mostly use both Han and Mongolian characters. Those setting up stalls on the ground must either sell chivalrous Four Books or smoking utensils. Paper lanterns with "Opening a Lamp Smoking House" and "Buying Harmful Ash" are especially scattered everywhere, actually many times more than restaurants. In the open space in the southwest corner of the city, poppies have been sown. Every summer, when the red and white flowers bloom, tourists flock there. No wonder nearly half of the more than 20,000 residents of the city are opium addicts.

People gather in the streets to gamble at Xiangqi, with large wins and losses. I envied the liveliness, squeezed in to watch. A certain soldier took out a gold coin, wanting to gamble with a man wearing sheepskin. The "owner" politely advised him, saying, "It is either win or lose, it is not easy for soldiers to earn money, please don't." The soldier insisted, but unfortunately lost. He then snatched the gold coin back and left. The winner dared not say anything. A few days ago, Mr. Liu Shengwu invited me to a dinner. At the table, guests talked about "the reclamation army borrowing farmers' farming tools, employing farmers to cultivate for them, not only wasting the farmers' cultivation time, but also exploiting them with high interest," etc. At first, I dared not believe it, but now, watching Xiangqi, I began to believe it.

Agricultural products in Hetao, in addition to rice, include many kinds of grains and vegetables. Among them, the cabbage, with each seedling weighing thirty or forty catties, and the melon seeds, with the famous name of "Dingxin Bai," are especially popular. It is a pity that the land is vast and the population is sparse, with a total population of less than 100,000. On average, each person can obtain two qing of land. No wonder many people just sit and watch it lie fallow. In the old days, prices were very cheap. One yuan for white flour could buy forty catties, more than thirty catties of millet, fifty or sixty catties of oats, four or five chickens, more than one hundred eggs, and more than ten catties of beef, mutton, pork, and fish. Vegetables were even cheaper, not to mention. Therefore, even villagers eat meat, flour, and vegetables as common food. Now, due to military chaos, it is greatly different from the past. Cattle, horses, camels, pigs, and sheep have all been slaughtered and eaten. Bone piles are like mountains, unbearable to look at. Meat is very difficult to obtain, and flour is also surprisingly expensive, only seven or eight catties per yuan. The rest can be inferred by analogy. Idle soldiers along the way sell goods to the people. Camels are five or six jiao each, mules and horses are two or three yuan. Some even use their guns to exchange for a full meal or five or six eggs.

From Baotou to Ningxia, passing through Wuyuan and Linhe, you can reach it by car in as little as four days. However, recently, due to ice melting and rising water levels, cars cannot pass. Moreover, the war in Ningxia has just ended, and there are often illegal acts by roaming bandits and scattered soldiers along the way. Therefore, travelers are cautious and mostly detour elsewhere, or take the Ping-Sui Road to Datong and transfer to the Longhai

Road westward, which takes about ten days, or hire a small Yellow River boat, dragged upstream by manpower, which takes two or thirty days, or ride a camel, go through the Hexi grasslands, which also takes twenty days. There are mostly deserts along the way, rarely populated, and the people you encounter are not kind, hence the saying "Rather encounter a camel than a person." The reporter is unwilling to retrace the same route and detour through Shaanxi, and wants to appreciate the desert scenery. What is the true picture? I have already prepared for the journey, joined a camel transport merchant group, and decided to depart tomorrow (21st), which will take about twenty days to reach Ningxia, and then I will see the readers again. (20th)

Page 9

Japanese Army Eager to Complete

Changda Road Has Started Construction Facilitates Military Transport Absorbs Freight Transport from Northern Manchuria Creates Industrial Center 89

Changchun Communication: The five roads in our Northeast planned by the Japanese were repeatedly requested to be built by the Northeast authorities before the September 18th Incident, but ultimately failed due to popular opposition. Now that they have occupied our Northeast, they can do whatever they want. Therefore, they completed the other four roads last year, with only the Changda Road remaining unfinished. However, in mid-March of this year, they started construction again. The entire road is approximately 800 Chinese miles long. Because there are no mountains or rivers along the line, the progress is quite rapid. The roadbed has now been laid, and it is expected to be open to traffic in September. The intentions and passing points of the Japanese's active construction of this road are also very noteworthy.

Although the Japanese army occupies our Northeast, the Soviet Union, because of the talisman of the Chinese Eastern Railway, causes inconvenience to the Japanese in every way. Although the Japanese tried to buy it, the Russians played along and refused to give up easily. The Japanese, in view of this, spared no effort to destroy the road. Daan is also an important town in northern Manchuria, located at the junction of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang provinces. Once the Changda Road is built, the Japanese can go straight from Dalian to northern Manchuria, cutting off the Russians' return route, making it impossible for the Russians to dare to easily leave the country and drive straight to Harbin, then the value of the Chinese Eastern Railway will be completely lost. This shows the importance of Changda Road.

The abundance of soybean production in the Northeast is world-renowned, especially in northern Manchuria. Exports rely entirely on the transportation of the Chinese Eastern Railway, so the road's income is astonishing. The Japanese are unwilling to have the Soviet Union obtain such a large profit, so they are determined to build the Changda Road. In the future, after the road is completed, the Chinese Eastern Railway will not only lose its military value, but also its freight transport will probably be unattended. At that time, even if the Russians do not want to sell, they will not be able to.

Daan is located in the Songhua River Basin, with a suitable climate and abundant production of various crops. Because water transportation is also very convenient, commerce is very developed. There are also many fish produced there, with cheap prices, sometimes selling for one cent per catty. Therefore, Japanese industrialists have raised funds to set up a large-scale fish canning company, which is now being prepared and can begin production in May. The fish produced in the Moon Lake accounts for 70% of the total. The lake has now been bought by the Japanese at a low price. At the same time, according to the measurement results of the South Manchuria Railway Company, the lake can generate 800,000 horsepower of hydroelectric power. A hydroelectric power plant is currently being funded. The Japanese are so active in operating because they want to turn the area into an important town in northern Manchuria and an industrial center.

The road starts from Changchun County in Jilin, passes through Nong'an and Fuyu counties, and ends at Daan County in Heilongjiang. It then connects to the Baichengzi Station of the Taoang Road in the north (now changed to Taoan County). After the completion of this road, Japan's railway network plan in the Northeast will also be fully realized.

Lu Muting, Director of the Hebei Provincial Department of Finance, will attend the meeting at that time. This conference is related to the overall plan for national financial reorganization. Since the war in Tangdong, Hebei Province last year, the finances have long been full of holes. The province is suffering from a lack of solutions. Having this conference opportunity, it is determined to submit a detailed report on the situation, so that the central government has a plan. At that time, I met with the Director of the Henan Finance Department. During our conversation, I learned that the central government was convening a national financial conference. Upon returning to the province, the order from the ministry had already arrived. After reading it, I learned that the conference was scheduled for May 21st. The materials requested from our province include the collection status of land taxes in each county and the budget books of each county in the province. However, our province is vast, with 131 counties under its jurisdiction. A single order would take at least six or seven days to reach all of them, and the preparation of budget books is no small task. Therefore, whether they can be completed and sent to this department before the conference is also a question. The department has issued multiple telegrams in recent days, ordering all counties to expedite the process. The conference is scheduled to be held on May 21st, and I plan to arrive on the 17th or 18th. I am preparing several proposals regarding the issues of our province to be submitted to the conference for discussion. Although we dare not expect any assistance from the central government in the current situation of our province's finances, this is a rare opportunity to present our province's predicament. Currently, the tax revenue in our province is the same as last year, with only a slight recovery in the war zones. However, due to special circumstances, there are obstacles to collection. The total annual revenue budget for the province before the war was 18 million. After the war, with the exemption of land taxes in the war-affected counties, it decreased by more than 4 million. The total annual expenditure for the province is more than 18 million, excluding temporary expenditures. Therefore, not counting temporary expenses, there is a shortage of more than 4 million. Temporary expenditures, such as the disbandment of various teams in the war zones and the recent expenses for the disbandment of the special police in Yutian, are all urgently needed, and their amounts are difficult to predict. The provincial treasury bears the most burden of these expenses, with an average monthly deficit of more than 300,000, which is being covered by scraping together funds. Chairman Yu Shu admonished me, saying, "When living in poverty, one must grit one's teeth and work hard." Hebei is now making a living by working hard in this poverty. Therefore, we are taking out loans every month to pay government expenses. For example, the expenses for various agencies in March were paid after obtaining a loan from the Provincial Bank, which will begin to be distributed tomorrow. Such difficult circumstances will be explained in detail at the upcoming national financial conference. (27th)

Military Affairs Commission Dispatches Personnel to

Inspect the Garrison in Xuzhou; Holding a Military Parade and Academic Examinations 98

Xuzhou Dispatch: After suppressing bandits in northern Anhui last year, the 7th Division of the 3rd Army returned to garrison in Xuzhou and Bengbu for reorganization and training, which has lasted for several months. Wang Jun had previously telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to dispatch personnel for inspection. The Military Affairs Commission designated Ye Nanfan as the chief inspector, and the Training Supervision Department dispatched Infantry Supervisors Zhang Gongda and Lin Rifan, the Military Administration Department dispatched Reserve Division Qiu Wenhua, and the Military Medical Division dispatched Xiong Jiping as inspection committee members. They arrived in Xuzhou from Nanjing at the end of last month. On the morning of the 1st, a military parade was held at Jiuli Mountain, with thousands of people from various agencies, organizations, and schools attending to observe the ceremony. The 39th Regiment of the 7th Division stationed in Xuzhou and the 37th and 38th Regiments stationed along the eastern and western routes, as well as the division's directly subordinate units such as the artillery battalion, engineer battalion, cavalry company, and special services, were all gathered for the parade. Division Commander Zeng Wanzhong served as the commander-in-chief. The parade began with Wang Jun accompanying Ye Nanfan and other inspection committee members, as well as representatives from various sectors, inspecting the troops for a week. Then came the marching parade, with each unit passing in front of the command platform in high spirits and with orderly steps. After the parade, technical skills were randomly tested, including bayonet practice, combat training, individual training, squad, platoon, and company training, martial arts, etc., and the results were remarkable. On the morning of the 2nd, internal affairs were inspected, and in the afternoon, academic subjects were tested. On the 3rd, a full roll call was conducted. On the 4th, live ammunition shooting took place, and special forces demonstrated explosions. On the 5th, 6th, and 7th, field exercises were conducted, with plans to form eastern and western detachments. The troops stationed along the eastern route were designated as the eastern detachment, and the troops stationed in Xuzhou and Bengbu were designated as the western detachment. The exercise area extended along the eastern section of the Longhai Railway. After the inspection in Xuzhou is completed, they will proceed to Bengbu to inspect the troops stationed there. (3rd)

Recent Situation in the Bandit Area of Changting; Mao Zedong Recuperating in Ruijin; Zhu De's Whereabouts Highly Secret 99

Xiamen Dispatch: Since a certain division of the Fujian Western Bandit Suppression Army captured Dayang Dam in Yongding on the 21st, a certain 3rd Division of the 4th Column has formed a communication line from Xinquan, Pengkou to Dayang Dam, 60 li from Liancheng and 140 li from Changting. Changting has been a bandit area for several years and has become a bandit nest, along with Ruijin, forming the bandit base. The county town of Changting is only 80 li from the town of Ruijin, and its importance is evident. The target of the Fujian Western Bandit Suppression is Changting. If Changting is recovered, the puppet capital will be difficult to defend, and the suppression of the Jiangxi bandits can be completed. According to those who fled from the Changting bandit area to Zhangzhou, the Central Army has been vigorously suppressing the Red bandits in various counties, and the puppet 3rd and 5th Army Corps have suffered the most losses, with over a thousand killed or wounded. Over two hundred were carried back to Changting for medical treatment. In early April, over two thousand Red bandits were sent from Ruijin to Changting, but only two-thirds had rifles. The next day, they set off for the border between Tinglong, Bian, and Nanyang Dam. Recently, most of the Red bandits in Changting have retreated to Ruijin and Huichang, leaving only a few hundred. In mid-April, a certain division of the Central Army in Longyan launched a two-pronged attack on the Baisha Red bandits from Xiaochi and Dayang Dam. There were several thousand bandits in the area. After two days and nights of fierce fighting, the National Army captured Xiaochi, and the bandits retreated to the Changfang area on the morning of the third day. The National Army sent teams to search and suppress them on one hand and pursue them on the other. Most of the remaining bandits are now gathered near Jiuxian (place name). The bandits have designated Nanyang, Jiuxian, and Baisha in the Fujian Western region as two lines of defense. Now that Baisha has been recovered by the National Army, the first line of defense has been lost. As for the second line of defense, since the recovery of Baisha near Jiuxian, the Longyan garrison has sent personnel to Shanghang to purchase rice and grain. Now the route between Baisha and Shanghang has been opened, and the Central Army has established contact with the Guangdong Army in Shanghang. Mao Zedong, the head of the Red bandit's puppet political department, has recently had a relapse of his lung disease and is recuperating in the Shachou Dam area of Ruijin. He lives in a cave dug in the ground to avoid air raids. The cave is very large and can accommodate a hundred people. Zhu De wears the same uniform as the bandit soldiers, and those who are not familiar with Zhu De's face cannot distinguish him. Recently, with the National Army launching attacks on the bandit nests from all directions, his whereabouts are even more secret. Women in Liancheng between the ages of twenty and forty have all been abducted by the bandits to serve in the women's teams and as scouts. Those who resist slightly are accused of being counter-revolutionaries and executed by shooting. The number of bandits in Liancheng is also large. (April 25th)

Xue Zukang Goes to the United States to Promote Chinese Silk 107

In recent years, the silk market has plummeted, and silk factories have suffered a sharp decline, closing down one after another. The sale of raw silk in the European and American markets is hindered by the dumping of Japanese silk and due to China's adherence to traditional methods, without knowing how to improve. As a result, sales have been stagnant, with almost no foothold. Recently, Xue Shou Xuan, the director of the local Huaxin Silk Factory, in order to rescue the situation, has specially sent Xue Zukang, the director of the silk manufacturing training institute of the factory, to go to the United States to promote Wei silk and to investigate the products of various European and Japanese countries for reference. Now Mr. Xue has gone to Shanghai yesterday to wait for the ship to go abroad.

Jiangyin: Security Expenses Collected Through Land Tax Surcharge 108

The security corps in the county has never had dedicated funding. In the past, the corps in each district collected donations locally, totaling more than 200,000 yuan per year for the entire county. Later, the county government prepared an estimate and submitted it to the Finance Department and Security Office, requesting that starting this year, a surcharge of 5.5 cents per mu be levied under the land price tax item, but the order has not yet been approved. Now that the headquarters has been established, according to the new plan, A and B security companies should be formed. Before the funding is determined, a temporary allocation of 11,700 yuan will be made from the local general reserve fund. Yesterday (3rd), the county government affairs meeting discussed and decided to submit a request to the Finance Department to approve the collection of land tax surcharge.

Changshu: Provincial Order Sets Deadline for Tax Collection 109

The amount of land price tax arrears in the county from the 17th year to the 21st year reached a total of 280,000 yuan. The Provincial Finance Department, in order to clear the arrears, sent Commissioner Chen Nai to reside in the county to clear them. The new tax for the 22nd year, from December 1st to the end of April of this year, has collected 49.8% of the total. The county reported to the provincial department. The province believes that the county has a habitual arrears of grain and taxes. If it is not rectified, it will repeat its past mistakes. Therefore, the county magistrate, Zhou Heng, and the directors of the east and west counters for grain collection are ordered to recover 80% of the amount by the end of June of this year, otherwise the county magistrate and the two directors will be dismissed and punished. In this situation of rural economic bankruptcy, it is quite difficult to collect the arrears. Therefore, the county government has found it difficult to comply with the order.

Nantong: Rugao Smuggled Goods Bribery Case Opened 110

Lu Peixian, secretary of the Rugao County Party Committee, and others opened the county's sealed smuggled goods from various industries. Merchants Yu Hao and others accused them of accepting bribes. The case was transferred to the jurisdiction of the Nantong Court for trial. The criminal court scheduled a public trial on the 21st.

Yang Meimei, a notorious bandit rampant in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, was a subordinate of Tai Bao Ashu and was as famous as Zhuluo Amei. Since Tai Bao Ashu was brought to justice, Yang Meimei led the remaining crowd and became their leader, committing more than 70 cases. A few days ago, they robbed Xiaozheng Town and kidnapped Cao Boming, the mayor of Xiaozheng Town, demanding 1,000 yuan. The meeting was scheduled to take place at Fengjing Town in the county. Yang's bandits were hiding in an opium den in Fengjing, and the matter was learned by Fei Gongxia, the captain of the Songjiang Water Patrol Team, who personally led the ship captain Tang Shuqin, scout Xia Chungen, and other police officers to Fengjing. They saw Yang Meimei on the street and immediately captured him and four other bandits. They were taken to Songjiang that night. After interrogation by the Water Police Headquarters, they confessed that they had been bandits for 19 years. Recently, they robbed Xiaozheng Town, Zhangliantang Town, and Shenjia浜 Yuan厙 and other places. They lived in taverns and enjoyed themselves with prostitutes for nearly four years. Now that they have been captured, they are certain to die. However, there are still long guns and cash hidden in the home of their mistress, Xu Sanniangzi, and with Cao Rongfu, the commander of the Xiaozheng Security Corps. After the Water Police Team Headquarters obtained the confession, in addition to detaining Yang and his gang, they also sent a team to bring Xu Sanniangzi and Cao Rongfu to justice.

Hangzhou: Jiu Hua Silver Shop Robbed in Broad Daylight 112

Yesterday (4th) at around 1:00 PM, the Jiu Hua Silver Shop outside the Drum Tower in Hangzhou was suddenly visited by a robber dressed as a worker, who held a bill of sale and purchased two gold rings weighing two mace each and a pair of earrings weighing two mace each. The shop clerk did not suspect anything and took the goods to the counter for him to choose. The robber took advantage of the clerk's preparation and grabbed the gold jewelry and fled. The clerk shouted for the police to pursue him. He was captured at Wangxian Bridge by police officer Zhou Junjie. In desperation, the robber threw the gold jewelry on the side of the road in an attempt to destroy the evidence. After being detained and interrogated by the First Branch Bureau, he confessed his name as Wang Chunsheng, 44 years old, from Shaoxing, and admitted to planning the robbery. He was sent to the General Bureau and then to the court for trial on charges of robbery in broad daylight.
