Lu Shan, Lu Chuangong, and others from Datang Village in Tiantai, due to a dispute with Xu Qigen, a farmer from the neighboring Shuitang Village, over the cutting of Meng grass, gathered crowds of hundreds of people and engaged in a clan fight. As a result, Xu Qigen was shot and killed by Lu Shanshu and others. The county arrested the murderers Lu Shanshu, Lu Chuangong, Mei Angui, Lu Chuanxu, Mei Shouzai, Mei Shoubao, and others. The county court sentenced Lu Shanshu to life imprisonment and Lu Chuangong and Mei Angui to six years of imprisonment. Lu and others refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Higher Jiang Court. The prisoners were escorted to the province and tried once yesterday, and were ordered to be remanded in custody for further trial.

Special Article

On the Issue of Promulgating the Constitution (Continued) – A Reply to Mr. Wu Jingxiong – 114

— Zhang Yuanruo

Considering the process of constitutional development in various countries, the promulgation of their constitutions is also tailored to the times. The Magna Carta, initially promulgated in England, only restricted the power of the monarch to tax. Later, in 1679, 1688, 1911, 1918, and 1928, it was gradually supplemented. France initially promulgated only the Organic Law of the Senate and the Government, which was also incomplete. Since then, it has been amended over the years. Similarly, the implementation of the Finnish Constitution is determined by law (Article 95 of the Finnish Constitution). The promulgation of the Prussian Constitution only put Articles 31-43 and 86 into effect. The remaining articles were implemented after the new elections of the state council according to Article 74 (Article 88 of the Prussian Constitution). The Polish Constitution came into effect from the date of promulgation, and some of its articles, which need to be implemented by other laws, came into effect from the date of implementation of those laws (Article 126 of the Polish Constitution). The Lithuanian Constitution came into effect from the date of promulgation, but must be approved by national referendum within ten years at the latest (Article 107 of the Lithuanian Constitution). The Siamese Constitution came into effect from the date of promulgation, but is still subject to the restrictions of temporary provisions (Articles 64-65 of Chapter 7 of the Siamese Constitution). From this, it can be seen that the promulgation and implementation of a constitution must be tailored to the special requirements and environment of the nation, with the necessary discretion and flexibility.

The difficulty of China's constitutional problem does not lie in the creation of a good legal system, but in the promotion of the rule of law. The spirit of the rule of law is not only limited to the written legal code, but also values the implementation, protection, observance, and popularization of the law. The drafting of laws is easy and temporary, but the implementation, protection, observance, and popularization of laws depend on the development of the spirit of the rule of law and the cultivation of public habits. It is difficult, time-consuming, and difficult to achieve results. The Chinese people have long lacked the spirit of the rule of law. Therefore, the result of the reform and change was that new laws and old habits initially had no relationship or influence. The new laws were new, but the people remained old, accustomed to their old habits. After the change of era, the Chinese people were still eager for success without considering the fundamentals. The constitution they made was still not consistent with the habits of the people. Therefore, if we want to achieve constitutional success today, we should strive to cultivate the spirit of governance and consolidate the foundation of the rule of law during the crucial period of tutelage, so that the future laws can be integrated with the people and consistent with the people's spirit and habits, and no longer depart from the people and run counter to them. The success or failure of this tutelage work is the key to the social order and the success or failure of the constitution in our country (see my book "Politics and the Rule of Law in Twenty Years" 3.2. Central Daily News). Therefore, when the provisional constitution was drafted a few years ago, I wrote an article explaining that the main purposes of the provisional constitution were: 1. To complete revolutionary doctrine; 2. To promote the development of civil rights; 3. To build local autonomy; 4. To cultivate the spirit of the rule of law (see my book "The True Meaning of the Provisional Constitution" May 7, Ta Kung Pao). Now that the period of tutelage is not yet complete and local autonomy has not been achieved, the spirit of the constitution at this time should still be based on these four purposes, and its practical use should be limited to "trying out the five-power government" (as stipulated in Article 19 of the Founding Program). Before the constitution is promulgated, "the presidents of all institutes shall be appointed and dismissed by the President and supervise them" (Article 21 of the Founding Program). The draft constitution should be based on the Founding Program and the achievements of the tutelage and constitutional periods, and should be deliberated by the Legislative Yuan and publicized to the people at any time (Article 22 of the Founding Program). It must not be hastily set a two-month period for public comment, and as for its promulgation and implementation, it should be in accordance with Article 23 of the Founding Program, which stipulates that the National Assembly should be convened to decide on the promulgation after more than half of the provinces in the country have reached the period of constitutional start-up, that is, the complete establishment of local autonomy in the entire province.

Dai Jitao said in a letter to Sun Zhesheng, the president of the Legislative Yuan, "If our comrades do not legislate for the long-term plan of the country and for the benefit of the people, or arbitrarily enforce the law, or enact it without implementing it, it will not complete the people's way. Therefore, for two years, I have repeatedly said that the provisional constitution should be implemented. Now, the convening of the National Assembly to create a constitution is of greater significance than the provisional constitution, but if the attitude of the Chinese people remains the same as their attitude towards the provisional constitution, then its constitution will only lead to political stagnation, and the chaos and the demise of the country may arise from it. The Chinese people today still have a ray of hope in the future, thinking that the National Assembly has not yet been convened, and the constitution has not yet been formulated. After the constitution is promulgated, the task of revolution and nation-building of the Kuomintang will reach its final stage. If it cannot be implemented, or if it is implemented with major defects, then the hope of the people will be exhausted, and unexpected changes may occur." His words are serious and profound, and I truly agree with them.

In short, the great cause of constitution-making is everlasting, and the order and chaos of the country depend on it. It should not be arbitrarily written or hastily done. My humble opinion is self-examined and sincere. I hope that those who are experienced and plan for the country will deeply consider it (The End).

Local News Yesterday

Anniversary of the Establishment of the Revolutionary Government: The Whole City Hangs Flags in Celebration, All Government Offices Are Closed; Municipal Party Headquarters Convened a Representative Assembly of All Circles 115

Yesterday was the 13th anniversary of the establishment of the Revolutionary Government. More than 300 representatives from all walks of life attended, and the atmosphere was quite enthusiastic. The details are recorded as follows:

Party, government, and military organizations such as the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, and the Garrison Headquarters, as well as the Jianghai Customs, the Central Bank, various groups, and schools, all took a day off and sent representatives to attend the commemorative meeting of all circles. Tong Xingbai, Chen Kecheng, Zhang Jintang, Zhou Feicheng, and Zhou Xuexiang formed the presidium.

Chairman's Report 119

First, Chairman Tong Xingbai gave a report, saying in brief: "Today is the 13th anniversary of the establishment of the Revolutionary Government. Why should we commemorate the establishment of the Revolutionary Government thirteen years ago? Because this was the day when the Prime Minister took office as the Extraordinary Grand President, which has a significant relationship with the future of our nation and country. During this commemorative period, we recall the history from the founding of the Republic to the tenth year of the Republic, during which many difficulties occurred in politics, and the political organizations and forms underwent abnormal changes. The government was often manipulated by ambitious people. Therefore, in order to promote the revolution, the Prime Minister had to change the sluggish situation. At that time, some people believed that the revolution was successful when the Republic was established and the Manchu Qing Dynasty was overthrown. However, the Prime Minister thought otherwise. He felt that the revolution would not be successful unless the Three Principles of the People were realized and the will of the whole country was unified. Therefore, he would rather resign from the position of Provisional Grand President and organize a revolutionary government in Guangzhou, using the power of the Party to destroy the remnants of feudalism, such as Yuan Shikai, who proclaimed himself emperor, and Zhang Xun, who restored the monarchy, and other rebellious acts, which made the principles of Chinese politics disappear. The Prime Minister fought with all his strength, so the Guangzhou Revolutionary Government was finally established. This is from the perspective of the country. As for the imperialists abroad, they colluded with a group of politicians and warlords to carve up China. As a result, most of the unequal treaties were signed at that time, which is really heartbreaking. In order to fulfill his aspiration to save the country and the people, the Prime Minister tried his best to promote the Extraordinary National Assembly and the Revolutionary Government in Guangzhou. Therefore, the Revolutionary Government in the tenth year of the Republic was of great significance in the history of the Republic. This is the first point. Secondly, after the establishment of the Revolutionary Government, the Prime Minister never used the power of the Guangdong border to seize power. He wanted to use Guangzhou as a base to unify the whole country. Therefore, the first thing after the establishment of the Revolutionary Government was the Northern Expedition. After capturing parts of Hunan and Jiangxi, Chen Jiongming rebelled in Guangzhou, so he returned to suppress it. After destroying Chen's rebellion, there was a second Northern Expedition, which laid a very solid foundation for our Party. In the fifteenth year of the Republic, Commander-in-Chief Chiang's third Northern Expedition followed the Prime Minister's last will, and the country was mostly unified by the seventeenth year. If we trace the origin, it was based on the establishment of the Revolutionary Government in the tenth year of the Republic. In the future, our comrades who die later must continue the Prime Minister's last will and support our current leader to complete the unification. If there are rebels who want to disturb the unification of China, we must all rise up and attack them. Thirdly, the Prime Minister, during his lifetime, adhered to the spirit of unyielding and fought against the powers, and would never give an inch of China's land to foreigners. In Guangdong, he fought with foreigners over the tariff issue. No matter how the imperialists used their power to threaten, the Prime Minister would never lose a bit of the country's interests. Therefore, the establishment of the Revolutionary Government was also to deal with imperialism. Even today, although the three northeastern provinces have been taken away by violent Japan by force, in law, we have never signed or recognized it. Japan uses the issues of through trains and through mail to lure us, but the government has not been tempted so far. Japan's recent statement that Japan has a special status in China and that Western countries cannot interfere has been severely refuted by our government. The outside world does not understand and has doubts, but it does not know that the government's strategy has never changed. However, because the current strength is still insufficient, there is hope to recover the lost land in the future when the domestic strength is sufficient. This depends on our efforts."

Chen's Speech 120

Next, Mayor Wu's representative Chen Kecheng gave a speech, saying, "Today is the anniversary of the May 5th Revolutionary Government, which is also the anniversary of the Prime Minister's assumption of the office of Extraordinary Grand President. Mayor Wu is one of the members of the presidium of this meeting and was scheduled to attend on time. However, because there is also a workers' movement conference in the city at the same time, and the municipal government is also holding a commemorative meeting, the time conflicted, and he could not arrive in time. Therefore, he specially sent my brother to represent him. Today's commemoration, in today's situation of both internal and external troubles, we recall the great spirit of the Prime Minister leading our Party to fight against evil forces in difficult and arduous times, which makes us feel infinite admiration and emotion. In the ten years from the Prime Minister's death to the present, our Party vowed to launch the Northern Expedition and eventually unified the country. The initial cause of the revolution is about to be completed, but what follows is the invasion of foreign enemies and the harassment of red bandits. The invasion of foreign enemies is to cut off our revolutionary path, and the harassment of red bandits has disrupted our construction progress. At the same time, in the midst of external aggression and internal unrest, it has given some ambitious people the opportunity to harm the Party and the country. The Fujian Incident in the past was an example. Even though a huge price was spent to quell the Fujian Incident, the vitality of the entire country and nation was once again weakened. Wanting to resist foreign aggression without internal stability, and talking about resisting foreign aggression with other intentions, this is the general phenomenon in China today. Therefore, those who seek internal stability cannot do so freely, but foreign troubles continue to oppress them even more. If this situation does not change, China will be incurable. It is like trying to force a person whose thoughts are not correct to take a path that does not lead to heresy. Where does one start? I have already said that the invasion of foreign enemies is to cut off the revolutionary path. Then, will the way out for our country and nation be cut off because of this? Here, we have a very big premise, which is what method we should use to avoid being cut off, and what method we should use to make ourselves stronger. This kind of rational self-strengthening theory has been rarely paid attention to since the outbreak of national disasters. The enemy's planes and cannons can never be resisted by our empty talk on paper. Therefore, our only preparation is how to follow others to manufacture planes and cannons. To manufacture planes and cannons, we must put the strength of the entire country into it. Similarly, to gather the strength of the entire country, we must unify the country. The conclusion is to stabilize the internal situation first and then resist foreign aggression. Especially to stabilize the internal situation, we must quell the rebellion and exterminate the red bandits. Under this conclusion, we re-examine the general consciousness of the people in the past two years, but we cannot help but be disappointed. But what about our Party's work in the past two years? Even if we cannot be complacent, we cannot help but make us feel the rebellion has been quelled, and the red bandits have been wiped out. Under the leadership of Chairman Chiang, the remarkable achievements are known to all Chinese people, and there is no need to say more. And the progress of various construction undertakings has been praised by British and American public opinion. From this, we can know that only our Party can save the country, and only our Party can fight in the midst of internal and external attacks and revive China. Similarly, the order of stabilizing the internal situation and resisting foreign aggression cannot be reversed, and it has firmly established its foothold in the iron-like facts. Speaking of this, we need to look at it from a higher level. Why is the general national consciousness so depressed? Some people say that this decadence is an inevitable stage in the transition from the old to the new era. Then, why has China's reform for thirty years not made progress in the new stage? Our answer is that the national thinking is not unified, and there are very few correct opinions to guide it. Therefore, what is manifested in the facts is the proof of the past two years since the national disaster. In the future, the work of our Party, in addition to the actual internal stability and construction, must also focus on correcting the general thinking of the people. To correct this decadent thinking and put it into practice in daily life, we must work harder to promote and implement the New Life Movement, to cultivate our great spirit from the New Life Movement of the small self, to shoulder the heavy responsibility of the country and nation in this extraordinary period. This is the significance of our commemoration of the Prime Minister today. Our slogans today are to commemorate the Prime Minister, to eliminate the reactionaries, to implement the New Life Movement, to work hard on construction, and to swear to eliminate national humiliation."

Tan Zhen Guo Chuntao

Representative of the Anti-Drug Association to Hankou

Huang Jiahu Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 127

Petition Results···The Hankou Anti-Drug Chinese National Anti-Drug Association has been advocating the anti-drug movement for ten years. Although the struggle has never been relaxed due to the harsh environment, it has recently learned that opium, red pills, and other substances are extremely poisonous, and sent representative Huang Jiajun to Hankou last month to investigate. Liu Yaochang, a member of the association in Hankou, Wu Deshi, the Chinese bishop of the Sheng Kung Hui, and Dunn, the adviser to Commander Zhang, accompanied him to visit Zhang Xueliang, the Deputy Commander of the Anti-Banditry of the Three Provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, to request strict prohibition in order to save the country. Huang Chen presented the situation he witnessed and vigorously advocated the advantages and disadvantages. Deputy Commander Zhang was extremely moved, and immediately transferred the petition to Commander-in-Chief Chiang, and asked Huang to draft the regulations and propose a prohibition plan as a basis for implementation. It is said that Huang Junye has returned to Shanghai after finishing his work. It is said that Chiang and Zhang have accepted the petition from the association and ordered the closure of all large and small opium dens in Hankou and Wuchang, and smoking by young people is absolutely prohibited. The order was implemented on April 30th, and there are also records in the special telegrams of various newspapers in recent days. The association was very pleased to receive reports from members in Hankou confirming that the opium dens in the city have been closed. It is said that the association is continuing its efforts to achieve the goal of complete purification. The statement submitted by Mr. Huang to Commanders Chiang and Zhang is excerpted below, "For the sake of regulations, opium is a poisonous substance that destroys the country and the people. All countries in the world have declared it a strict prohibition. At the end of the Qing Dynasty, our country was horrified by the fierce scourge of opium. Prohibition was necessary for survival. We spared no sacrifice and finally achieved the goal of prohibition, which was valued by the international community. In recent years, our country has been in constant chaos, foreign insults have been frequent, bandits have been everywhere, and disasters have continued. The scourge of opium has been rekindled, and it is even worse than at the end of the Qing Dynasty. Until today, the scope and degree of its poisoning has reached a point where it cannot be ignored. The arrogance of warlords, the corruption of politics, the exhaustion of the economy, and the bankruptcy of the countryside are all the steps that this thing has taken to become fierce. Furthermore, the aggression of strong neighbors, the failure of diplomacy, the decline of morality, and the decline of morale are all caused by opium. After the Japanese occupied the three northeastern provinces, they were eager to implement the public sale of opium. The colonial governments of various Nanyang countries wanted to control the overseas Chinese and also used opium to promote their rapid demise. The obvious lessons are all in front of us. Looking back at the domestic situation today, it is even worse than in the Northeast and Nanyang. Judging only by the amount of opium taxed by the Hankou Lianghu Special Tax Office, it was 100,000 dan in the 18th year of the Republic, 117,000 dan in the 19th year, 70,020 dan in the 20th year, 59,860 dan in the 21st year, and 71,756 dan in the 22nd year. The number of morphine, heroin, red pills, white pills, and other poisonous substances that are not taxed by the Hankou Special Tax Office or smuggled is not included. The number is even more alarming when calculated nationwide. Therefore, today, from the central government and military agencies to the local government, land and water military police, no one does not regard this as a source of wealth. Even courts, schools, groups, and newspapers are eager to share the profits equally. Therefore, the opium force is advancing by leaps and bounds, and the traffickers and opium merchants are extremely popular. To talk about prohibition is almost empty talk. However, opium prohibition is the only way to save the country. How can we abandon food because of choking and sit idly by?

From a general point of view, it seems that there is really no way to prohibit it. Therefore, the advocacy of banning in taxation and the provisions for public sale are rampant. Some use scientific opium prohibition as a slogan, or advocate turning private into public to move people. The authorities also believe that since there is no way to prohibit opium, it is better to collect taxes and allow sales to enrich the national treasury, and gradually prohibit it, which is better than letting it all fall into the hands of local military personnel, politicians, traffickers, and merchants. It is really a win-win situation. However, these methods have been tried repeatedly. The result is limited income and endless malpractices, which only make the scourge of opium spread day by day, and only create opportunities for corrupt officials, greedy officials, donation bandits, and upper merchants to make money. It is of no great benefit to the national treasury. What is the achievement of the Lianghu Special Tax and the ten-province opium prohibition today? It can be seen in general. Today, both at home and abroad, the reputation of the country is declining, foreigners are contemptuous, and at home, the officialdom is flooded and public opinion is boiling. All these are the evil consequences of opium taxes, and the losses outweigh the gains. I think it is already in your Excellency's awareness. My colleagues in the association have been refusing drugs for ten years, running around and calling out, and dare not slack off. However, our cotton power is limited and the effectiveness is not obvious. Although the environment is harsh, we still adhere to our long-standing advocacy and continue to struggle. We have presented the advantages and disadvantages to the central government and the governments of various provinces, and requested prohibition no less than dozens of times. However, the gentlemen in charge either regard it as insignificant or think that there is no way to do it. Therefore, we turn a blind eye to the requests of the people. But how can we sit idly by and watch the country perish and the species die out? Your Excellency is well-versed in the world situation and knows the suffering of the people. "For opium poisons, we must adopt the long-standing determination to deeply hate and thoroughly prohibit them, and properly plan a good method of fundamental prohibition, to lift the people out of the water and fire and lay the foundation of the country on a solid foundation. My colleagues should only contribute their years of research and the knowledge gained from domestic and foreign investigations and inspections. Here, we hereby put forward the following outline of recommendations for your Excellency's selection: 1. The government should hire experts from China and abroad on opium agricultural economics and other issues to conduct investigations, and based on the facts of the investigation, study opium prohibition methods that meet the needs of the facts. 2. The government should conduct surveys and provide full protection for opium, and facilitate the implementation according to the planned plan. 3. The central and local governments should compile statistics on the tobacco tax collected by the army and calculate the total amount. Experts should study and compensate for it from other sources. 4. The opening of new tax sources should be based on the principle of not affecting people's livelihoods and not disturbing social tranquility. 5. No matter what method is used to handle opium prohibition, it should be based on the principle of pure prohibition. The government should express its determination to strictly implement it, starting with military and political personnel, so as to restore the people's faith. 6. The government should select people with high moral character who are trusted by the people to take on the heavy responsibility of prohibiting politics, and should give them practical guarantees and necessary privileges to make it easy to achieve results. 7. The fines and any income from opium prohibition must not be used for military and political expenses, and should be allocated to fund drug rehabilitation and anti-drug education. 8. In handling opium prohibition, we should cooperate with the people on the one hand, such as surveying tobacco seedlings, arresting smuggling, prohibiting private sales, and banning smoking, in order to achieve thoroughness and rapid results. This responsibility can be taken over by the Anti-Smoking Supervisory Committee composed of fair people publicly recommended by the local legal groups. 9. The country has a vast territory, and it is not easy to prohibit it once and for all. Several provinces and regions should be designated to take the lead in order to establish a model for the provinces and increase the determination to follow it. 10. In order to ensure opium prohibition, the government should assist the anti-drug movement of the people and prohibit illegal officials from destroying it, so that it can help what the law cannot. At the height of the New Life Movement, opium prohibition should be listed as one of the work outlines. If the above ten outlines are accepted, then tens of thousands of families will be saved, and hundreds of generations will be fragrant. Your Excellency's achievements in saving the country and the people will be as long as the sun and the moon."

German侨 Celebrate National Day; Not to Commemorate International Labor Day; Statement by Mr. Barnick of the German Consulate 128

Mr. Barnick, Acting Consul General of Germany in Shanghai, sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, "To the Editor, I have read in your newspaper's local news column on the 3rd of this month that regarding the German僑 celebrating the National Day, 'International Labor Day has been designated by German Prime Minister Hitler as the Commemorative Day for the German Brown Shirt Labor Vanguard.' In order to avoid misunderstandings, I hereby declare the following: The celebration and commemoration of May 1st in Germany has absolutely no international nature and is completely different from International Labor Day. The German government issued a decree on February 27 this year, stipulating May 1st as the German National Day, and the meaning of the celebration is the expression of the German people's cooperation with their motherland and nation, not the idea of international class struggle, such as the Marxist workers' May Day Labor Day held in other countries. May 1st in Germany is the same as the October 10th Double Tenth Festival in China, both are National Days. I hereby send this letter to your newspaper, and please check it."

The Residents of Peide Lane Had Their Water Turned On Yesterday, Thanks to Mediation by Feng Bingnan and Assistance from He Dekui; Tenants Declare They Will Not Bear the Increased Fees 130

A New Sound Society report states that the residents of Peide Lane on the Great West Road in the New Gate area had their water cut off by the water company at the behest of the landlord, who was unable to increase the water rates. Yesterday morning, Mr. Wang Xiangu, the lawyer representing the lane's residents, accompanied by representatives Wang Jieqing, Liu Chengyong, Huang Yaozu, Chen Silong, and others, went to the water company to negotiate with the Western deputy manager, Mr. Walter. Following mediation by Feng Bingnan, the Western manager's attitude was no longer as rigid as before. However, he still indicated that he needed to consult with the landlord before making a final decision, so no agreement was reached. Subsequently, they went to the Public Works Bureau to request the assistance of He Dekui. Mr. He also expressed considerable sympathy and agreed to negotiate with the water company. As a result, at 2:00 PM yesterday, the water company dispatched personnel to turn the water back on. Upon hearing the news, the residents of the entire lane were overjoyed and set off firecrackers, bringing the water cutoff dispute to a temporary end. However, according to the residents' representatives, although the company has restored the water supply, the residents will not bear the increased water fees if they are still paid by the landlord. If the residents pay themselves, they must deduct one-tenth of the ice money from the rent, in addition to the extra dollar. If this is not done, the more than three thousand tenants will not yield.

The Northbound Plane Was Grounded Yesterday; The Southbound Plane is Scheduled to Return from Tongzhou to Shanghai This Morning 131

Yesterday's weather was overcast, with a light rain in the morning, making air travel inconvenient. Tang Guanyu's Inspection

A Written Report on the Domestic Goods Factories in North China 132

Ms. Tang Guanyu, a member of the Women's Domestic Goods Promotion Association, submitted a written report at the joint meeting of the three committee groups the other day. The report is recorded as follows: "On this trip, I was entrusted by the association to take the opportunity to visit domestic goods factories. It was my responsibility, but due to the limited time and my own limited abilities, I was unable to conduct a thorough investigation, which I regret. I will now provide a brief report based on my recollections. "[Beiping] In Beiping, I visited the following factories under the guidance of Mr. Chen Shiquan and Mr. Zhang Pengcai from the Municipal Party Department: (1) The Beiping Municipal People's Livelihood Carpet Factory, where I was shown around by Director Cheng Kuan. The raw materials used are very loose cotton threads, and the carpets are woven on wooden looms entirely by hand. The patterns are exquisite and artistically meaningful. This factory was established by the municipal government to support the livelihoods of the common people. (2) The Yanjing Carpet Company, where I was guided around by Mr. Ji Mengchun. The manufacturing method is the same as in (1). The patterns use colors, and the work is exquisite and beautiful. The facilities are also quite comprehensive. They pay close attention to worker welfare, such as labor hygiene. (3) The Tianyihe Enamel Factory, which produces the renowned Jingtailan (cloisonné enamelware). The manufacturing process involves first making objects out of copper, then embedding copper wires to create patterns, then coating them with various colors using materials from Boshan in Shandong, baking them, and then carefully polishing them by hand, resulting in an unusually bright and long-lasting finish. They sell a great deal to Western countries. (4) The Renli Industrial Company, where I was guided around by Manager Ling Qijun. The carpet department is on the ground floor, and the Boshan material department is upstairs. They produce various samples that resemble white jade and green jade, including flower vases, bowls, screens, and other items, all of which are bright and very beautiful. Various domestic goods companies in Shanghai often display them, but not very completely. According to a Renli company employee, most of these materials are sold to Western countries. (5) The Hebei No. 1 Prison Workshop, where I was guided around by Mr. Zhou Yuxiu. The building is circular and divided into two parts, each shaped like a fan. The first part is further divided into A, B, C, D, and E, and the second part is further divided into F, G, H, I, and J. The prison cells are connected to the workshops and are quite clean. The men's prison has a printing department, which is quite large. The products of its curtain department are exquisitely painted and are the best in Beiping, which is effective in resisting Japanese curtains. There is also a rattan ware department and a shoe department, which can also be relied upon to generate profits. In addition, there are woodworking and agricultural activities. Therefore, part of the building was built by the prisoners themselves with great skill, which shows the sanctity of labor. (6) Jade shops are located in the small alleys outside Chongwenmen, with numerous workshops. The production is exquisite. Beiping jade is truly a beautiful Chinese product. (7) There are many children's toy stores. The animal models they make are very lifelike and are made of flannel and old leather. The toy departments of the Sincere, Wing On, and Sun Sun department stores often display them. These are Beiping products. "[Tianjin]" In Tianjin, I was able to visit the factories thanks to a letter of introduction from Mr. Song Fei Qing, the manager of the Dongya Woolen Textile Company, who also offered to accompany me to other factories. His enthusiasm was commendable. (1) The Dongya Woolen Textile Company, where I was guided around by Manager Song Fei Qing. The scale is very large, and the facilities are quite well-organized. The raw materials selected can be described as pure. The Di Yang brand wool yarn produced is also quite smooth. The wool produced in China is slightly shorter and harder than that produced abroad, which is related to the breed of sheep (Japan does not produce wool). The dyes used to dye the wool are different from those used to dye yarn. Therefore, if yarn is mixed into the wool yarn, the yarn will not be colored, which shows that the raw materials for the wool yarn are entirely wool. (2) The Sheng Xifu Hat Shop, where I was accompanied by Mr. Song. Manager Zhou Yongze provided a thorough welcome. Most of the shop's work is done by hand, but there are a few small machines used to weave straw braids. The trademark is the Three Hats brand. They have both felt hats and straw hats. One type of thin felt hat has a brim that is woven from a combination of hemp thread, cotton yarn, and wool yarn. (3) The Renli Industrial Company Weaving Factory, which is a branch of the Renli Industrial Company of Beiping, where I was guided around by Deputy Manager Chen Li. The woolen fabrics, carpets, and other items woven are beautiful in color and the selection of yarn is exquisite. The scale is very large. (4) The Shengsheng Workshop, where I was accompanied by Mr. Song and Mr. Chen Xizhi from the YMCA. The workshop specializes in weaving jacquard blankets, which are made by hand on wooden looms. There are many patterns, all of which are considered excellent. They are woven purely from cotton yarn. The guide was Mr. Feng Yueqian. (5) The Yongnian Machine-Woven Cool Mat Factory, where I was guided around by Mr. Wang Fusun. The mat grass is purchased from Ningbo and woven on wooden looms. The printing of patterns has been prone to discoloration, but they now use steam printing and dyeing, which makes them durable and prevents discoloration. (6) The Mohong Magnetic Tile Factory, where I was guided around by Mr. Liu Fuzhai and Mr. Zhang. The raw material stone is produced in Tangshan, Tianjin. They manufacture glazed tiles, mosaic cement bricks, magnetic tiles, earthenware tiles, and ordinary bricks and tiles. The colors are bright, and the patterns are also good. I heard that they are quite durable and can compete with imported products. They can be adopted for new buildings. (7) The Tianjin Soap Company, which was founded nearly thirty years ago, produces Seven Star brand iron anchor soaps, Eight Trigram brand gourd brand medicinal soaps, various scented soaps, floral water, and snowflake cream cosmetics. Because they have chemical experts engaged in research, the colors and shapes can compete with foreign goods. (8) The North China Leather Company, where I was guided around by technician Zhou Naigeng. The enameled leather, flag leather, shoe upper leather, box leather, book cover leather, clothing leather, etc., made of cowhide are quite popular in the north. They have recently added the production of tire leather (used on various machines). In the past two years, the results have been gradually emerging. The highest quality is the Elephant brand, followed by the brand, which are both durable and long-lasting. The various leathers produced by the company also use the Elephant brand as a trademark. (9) The North Asia Industrial Factory, which specializes in the manufacture of buttons. There are many types, including Roman buttons and horn buttons, and the production is quite abundant. (To be continued)

The County Government Announces a Reduction in the Deed Tax to 6.3% for Sales 135

The Shanghai County Government issued a public notice yesterday, stating that it had received an order from the Jiangsu Provincial Government to reduce the deed tax rate in the province to 6.3% for sales, starting in May, for a three-month trial period. During this trial period, any deeds that are overdue and have not been taxed will be allowed to be taxed leniently, without penalty. In accordance with this order, the county must comply. All deed taxes in the county will be collected at a rate of 6.3% for sales, starting this month. The attached taxes will also be reduced proportionally. In addition to issuing notices to the district, township, and town offices to notify each household, the public notice is issued to all the people of the county, so that everyone is aware. All unregistered deeds under public or private names must be taxed in the county during the period of reduced taxes and exemptions from penalties. If the deadline is still not met, once discovered or reported, the original tax rate will still be collected, and severe penalties will be imposed.

Shanghai County Government

Levying the Yingdou River Dredging Fee 136

The Yingdou River in the first district of Shanghai County has recently become silted up, which is detrimental to agricultural irrigation. The local people in the area have planned to dredge it and immediately reported it to the county government to request funding. The county government then forwarded it to the provincial government, which approved a temporary levy of one dime per mu on the benefited fields on both sides of the river, which will be collected with the first installment of the land price tax in the 23rd year. The county government has now verified that the actual taxable mature fields benefited by the river are 2,664 mu, 1 fen, 8 li, and 9 hao in the 21st bao and 1st tu; 4,374 mu and 1 li and 2 hao in the 69th tu; 4,756 mu, 2 fen, and 4 li and 1 hao in the 54th and 55th tu; 961 mu, 7 fen, and 6 hao in the 42nd tu; 5,000 mu and 9 fen and 8 li in the 7th tu; and 3,312 mu, 3 fen, and 1 li and 1 hao in the 10th tu, for a total of 25,069 mu, 4 fen, 3 li, and 9 hao. Yesterday, the collection office was ordered to comply with the levy.

Lü Yuequan Appointed as Chinese Consultant to American Insurance Institute - An Honor for China's Life Insurance Industry 143

Mr. Lü Yuequan, General Manager of China United Assurance Society, has served in the life insurance business for over thirty years and is a pioneer in the life insurance industry. He initially worked for Yongnian Life Insurance Company and later resigned from his original position in the first year of the Republic of China to personally found China United Assurance Society. Through diligent management, he has built a solid foundation and an outstanding reputation to this day. Today, when people in society discuss Chinese life insurance companies, they all regard China United Assurance Society as the leader. This is because Mr. Lü's vision is far-reaching, his character is noble, and he handles affairs diligently, making him the foremost figure in China's life insurance industry. His reputation is widely known and has spread overseas. Now, the American College of Life Underwriters in Philadelphia, USA, having long heard of Mr. Lü's great reputation, has sent a joint letter from the President, Dean, and Secretary-General of the College, formally inviting Mr. Lü to be the Chinese Life Insurance Consultant to the College. It is noted that the College is the most prestigious life insurance management college in the United States. The authorities of the College are all well-known figures in the life insurance industry. Only those who have specialized in life insurance, passed the College's examinations, and been granted certificates can be qualified life insurance managers. The College widely seeks advice and recruits talented individuals to provide support, which is more than sufficient. It is heard that Mr. Lü, considering the College's earnest invitation, could not refuse and has already agreed to take on the position of Consultant. In the future, he will surely make significant contributions to the College. Enclosed below is a translation of the letter of appointment: By order of the Board of Directors of this College, we hereby appoint Mr. Lü Yuequan, General Manager of China United Assurance Society, as Chinese Life Insurance Consultant. Mr. Lü possesses both talent and virtue, and his reputation is outstanding. The Executive Department and Academic Department of this College hereby authorize and trust Mr. Lü to fully utilize his grand plans for the aforementioned position of Consultant. This is our deep hope. Dated this twenty-seventh day of February, 1934, in the City of Philadelphia, State of Pennsylvania, USA. Signed: Clark, President of the American College of Life Underwriters; Hübner, Dean; Macfarlane, Secretary-General.

Chunming Bookstore

Fined for Selling Pirated Books 147

Chunming Bookstore on Fuzhou Road was reported to the Laozha Police Station by Sanyou Bookstore and Shenghuo Bookstore for selling pirated copies of "啼笑因緣" (Tixiao Yinyuan, A Story of Laughter and Tears) and "字辨" (Zi Bian, Character Discrimination), which they had published. Detective Zhang Yuanjing and Detective Pang Ruiqing investigated and confirmed the report. Subsequently, the police lawyer Qian Xunjiu filed a public prosecution against Chen Zhaochun, the manager of Chunming Bookstore, who is from Haimen, with the First Special District Court, based on Articles 234, 267, and 44 of the Criminal Law. The Special Court has concluded the interrogation, and yesterday, Judge Deng Baosun held a court session and announced the verdict. Chen Zhaochun was fined 800 yuan for continuously selling goods known to be counterfeited trademarks. If he could not pay the fine, he would be imprisoned, with two yuan equivalent to one day. Eight pirated copies of "啼笑因緣" were confiscated. He was found not guilty on other charges. The related civil lawsuit will be transferred to the Civil Division of this Court for trial.

Customs Officer

Memorial Service Held for Zhuang Zexin, Tax Official Who Died in the Line of Duty; Request for Compensation Filed 148

Zhuang Zexin, a field officer of the Zhifu Customs, at 3:00 AM on the first of last month, accompanied by inspectors and patrol teams, boarded a sampan to meet the Litong steamship arriving from Dalian. Unexpectedly, after the ship dropped anchor, it suddenly reversed, nearly colliding with the sampan. In a moment of urgency, Zhuang jumped into the water. At that time, the waves caused by the ship's propeller created a strong suction that pulled Zhuang into the bottom of the ship, causing him to drown. He left behind a wife and daughter, a truly tragic situation. Zhuang's brother, Zhuang Zezhong, currently the Deputy Commissioner of the Anti-Smuggling Department of the General Administration of Customs, went to Zhifu to handle the affairs upon hearing the news. All officers of the local customs and the General Administration of Customs, considering Zhuang's death in the line of duty, have not only sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance requesting compensation but have also scheduled a memorial service at the Customs Club on Jing'an Temple Road at 2:00 PM on the 20th of this month to express their condolences.

Shengming Factory Manager

Shengming Factory Manager Accused of Counterfeiting Trademark; Defendant Files Appeal with the Executive Yuan; Second Special Court Suspends Trial 149

Chen Fukang, a native of Ningbo, 37 years old, opened the Shengming Gauze Factory at No. 7, Deyi Lane, Annakin Road in the French Concession many years ago. Chen serves as the manager, and his products are gauze mantles used for gasoline lamps, which are widely sold. He had registered with the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government and obtained a license. His business was very prosperous. Recently, the German firm Qianxin Foreign Firm discovered that the gauze mantles produced by Shengming Factory had counterfeited trademarks and hired lawyer Wei Wei to report to the French Concession Police. The police sent detectives to Shengming Factory and confiscated gauze mantles worth 3,000 yuan, along with the manager Chen Fukang, and transferred them to the Second Special District Court. The police lawyer filed a lawsuit for the crime of counterfeiting trademarks. Judge Wu Fanglian held a court session for trial. The defendant hired lawyer Jiang Baoli for defense. The court ordered the defendant to pay a 1,000-yuan deposit for bail and await further investigation. After Chen was released on bail, he filed an appeal with the Executive Yuan based on the Trademark Law. Yesterday, the Second Special Court held a continued trial. First, the police lawyer stated that the police investigation had been completed. According to the defendant's lawyer, the defendant's trademark had already been registered, and an appeal had been filed with the Executive Yuan, requesting a postponement. The court then ruled that since the defendant had filed an appeal with the Executive Yuan, the trial should be suspended.

Tobacco Exchange Association

Notice Regarding the Rectification of Market Prices 150

The Shanghai North and South Branch Office of the Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Association, in accordance with the resolution of the 23rd Executive and Supervisory Committee meeting on the 3rd of this month, instructed all branch offices to promptly rectify matters in accordance with the regulations to maintain association affairs and to set new price lists for retail sales, which were distributed to all stores along with the notice. It is heard that the Shanghai South Branch Office, in order to protect the rights and interests of the industry and its reputation, has specially hired lawyers Gong Tongyuan and Shen Guozhang as legal advisors. Yesterday, a notice was issued stating that the profit margin for the sale of cigarettes by the industry is already very thin. Due to the increase in foreign prices, the retail stores are suffering significant losses and finding it difficult to maintain business. In order to protect the industry, the association has specially revised the retail prices for various items, submitted them to the Party and government authorities for approval and record-keeping, and issued them to all stores for compliance. Any violations will result in the association requesting legal advisors to take action in accordance with the association's articles of association and business regulations, and submitting a request for punishment, without any leniency, so as not to hinder the overall business. The following price list will take effect on the 10th of this month. All stores must comply with the sales prices to protect their capital and livelihood. This notice is hereby issued.

Business of Japanese Prostitutes in This City Declining 153

According to yesterday's Japanese-language Shanghai Daily, the situation in Shanghai's pleasure quarters has been quite bleak recently. In April, 82,500 tickets for Japanese prostitutes were sold, a decrease of 100 tickets compared to the previous month. Only eight prostitutes were able to sell more than 1,000 tickets. After the Shanghai Incident, during the era of rampant sexual desire, the number of restaurants in the city increased to more than 160, with over 700 female waitresses. After reorganization, this number was reduced to 138, of which 47 were purely coffee shops, with a total of more than 430 female waitresses. Now, whether it is coffee shops or restaurants, the business situation has plummeted.

Candle Shop Employee

Impersonates to Obtain Large Sums of Money; Impersonates to Call Money Exchange to Exchange Cash; Flees with 4,000 Yuan 154

Chen Jinquan, a 20-year-old native of Ningbo who works as an employee at Dacheng Candle Shop at the corner of Dongjiadu inside the Limalu in Nanshi, impersonated Hu Gensheng, a rice merchant residing upstairs in the shop, at around 1:30 PM yesterday. He secretly called the Tongxing Money Exchange in Beishi, falsely claiming that he urgently needed to exchange 6,000 yuan. The money exchange, having previously had transactions with Hu, sent someone with the cash to exchange it. However, Hu Gensheng, realizing that he had not made the call, suspected an error and told the messenger that he did not need the money. Unexpectedly, Chen Jinquan then went upstairs and told the Tongxing messenger that his shop had borrowed Hu Gensheng's name to call for 6,000 yuan. The Tongxing messenger, knowing that the shop had also had transactions in the past, did not suspect anything and told Chen that they had sent 4,000 yuan first, and the remaining 2,000 yuan would be sent later. One party then handed over 4,000 yuan to Chen Jinquan. After Chen counted the money, he hid it in his pocket and told the Tongxing messenger to wait a moment while he went downstairs to get the exchange money. After saying this, he went downstairs and left. However, after half an hour, Chen had not returned, causing great alarm. They hurried downstairs to inquire and realized they had been deceived. However, Chen Jinquan had disappeared without a trace. Afterwards, the Tongxing messenger reported to the store, which in turn reported to the First District One Precinct, and the police ordered Hu Gensheng and the manager of Dacheng to be taken to the precinct for questioning.

Using Theft to Create

Large-Scale Iron Factory; A Bizarre and Shocking Theft Case; Secret Construction in Suzhou 155

The North American Match Factory on Xichenjiadu Creek, Zhoujiaqiao, West Shanghai, has been in operation for more than ten years since its establishment. The factory site occupies a vast area, and its capital is quite substantial. The internal layout and scale are also very grand and complete. The manager is an American named Blanc, and there are a total of four to five hundred workers. Unexpectedly, the factory recently experienced an unprecedented theft of a large quantity of important machinery, which was secretly transported to Suzhou to rebuild another factory. The details of the incident are recorded below. It turns out that Wang Jisong, a foreman at the factory, secretly contacted Wang Liangyu, a former foreman who had stopped working, and starting this year, continuously stole important machinery and large and small steel knives from the factory and transported them to Suzhou to imitate and build another factory. The factory building has been completed, and the machinery has also been installed. In early last month, Wang and others began raising capital and were in the process of recruiting when, unexpectedly, the matter was discovered by Blanc, the factory manager, who immediately began investigating. As expected, he discovered that many important machines were missing and also found a letter outlining all the plans for stealing and building the factory. The planned steps were to steal the machinery and transport it to Suzhou to imitate and build a factory as the first step, to complete the factory site and raise capital as the second step, to have all the original factory workers go on strike at a specific time and then transport them to Suzhou to start working as the third step. With conclusive evidence, Manager Blanc reported to the Sixth District on the 18th of last month. After receiving the report, District Chief Tan, considering the seriousness of the case, immediately sent Officer Wei to lead the police to the factory and arrested the five thieves, Wang Jisong, Gu Xishan, Lu Afu, Lu Ayou, and Su Asan. After separate interrogations by the criminal officers of the district, they confessed to stealing machinery and building a factory called Tianyuan Iron Factory outside the Changmen Gate of Suzhou. After obtaining the confession, the district officers immediately prepared a document and transferred it to the General Bureau for investigation. Meanwhile, District Chief Tan ordered Detective Team Leader Wu Kezhong to supervise detectives Cao Chu, Yang Qing, and others to accompany Blanc to Suzhou to locate the factory and arrest the thieves Wang Liangyu and Chao Bingrong. They confiscated twenty pieces of stolen goods, including large and small important machines, fifty-two large and small steel knives, seals, letters, and other evidence, and escorted them back to Shanghai early yesterday morning, detaining them in the Sixth District. They then prepared a document and transferred it to the General Bureau for joint investigation.

Birthday Celebrations to Aid in Hospital Construction; Funds Transferred to Build the Muxin Hospital to Benefit the Residents of Zhabei 157

The day before yesterday was the sixtieth birthday of Mr. Lu Bohong, a philanthropist in this city. Guest List 158

The attendees on that day included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Secretary of the Municipal Government Geng Jizhi, Director of the Bureau of Public Utilities Xu Peihuang, Director of the Bureau of Public Health Li Ting'an, Bishop of the Shanghai Diocese Haouisée, as well as Huang Jinrong, Du Yuesheng, He Dekui, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Yiting, Shi Shengzhi, Yu Qiaqing, Shi Liangcai, Gu Xinyi, Yao Mulian, Fang Jiaobo, Wang Boqi, Xu Shiying, Feng Bingnan, Qian Xinzhi, Yao Ziruo, Wu Yunzhai, Zhang Xiaoliang, Le Zhenbao, Zhu Shouchang, Zhu Xuefan, and Lu Jingshi, totaling over two thousand guests from Chinese and Western communities, gathered together, making it a very grand occasion.

Mayor's Speech 159

During the banquet, Mayor Wu Tiecheng stood up to give a speech, which stated in brief: "Today is the sixtieth birthday of Mr. Lu Bohong of Shanghai. I and everyone here are very happy to participate in this event. Mr. Lu's industries and various charitable causes in this city are well known. This time, he plans to establish the Muxin Hospital in Zhabei to benefit the residents of Zhabei. I and everyone here should congratulate Mr. Lu even more. Today, the Pope of Rome has sent a telegram of congratulations and Bishop Haouisée has offered blessings, which is not only an honor for Mr. Lu but also an honor for the citizens of Shanghai. Mr. Lu's undertakings are always based on the spirit of 'the greatest joy comes from doing good.' Therefore, Mr. Lu is happy in body and mind and in good health. At the age of sixty, he looks like he is in his forties. The reason why Mr. Lu enjoys doing various charitable causes is to follow the spirit of Jesus's universal love and embrace the purpose of saving the world and helping people. His established institutions, such as the Xin Puyu Hall and the Sacred Heart Hospital, have excellent results, which are known to all citizens. Recently, there has been the planning of the Pushan Sanatorium and the establishment of the Muxin Hospital. One charitable cause is completed, and another follows. His spirit of never giving up and his perseverance in moving forward are all derived from his faith in God. We congratulate Mr. Lu on the success of his undertakings and even more congratulate Mr. Lu on becoming healthier as he does charitable causes. I, Tiecheng, respectfully offer a toast and, on behalf of the citizens of this city, wish Mr. Lu a long life and thank him on behalf of the residents of Zhabei."

Bishop's Speech 160

Following this, Bishop Haouisée gave a speech, stating in brief: "I am here to perform the Holy Communion blessing ceremony to express gratitude to God for bestowing various graces upon Mr. Lu. All of Mr. Lu's undertakings are bestowed by God and cannot be achieved by human power alone. However, the graces bestowed by God are available to everyone, but those who receive the graces must use them well; then, everything they do will be good. If they do not use them well, they will surely fail. Mr. Lu is one who uses his graces well, so none of his undertakings fail, and none are not good. Moreover, Mr. Lu is selfless and impartial in everything he does. Whether they are poor or in trouble, those who ask Mr. Lu for help are always given assistance. The success of the various charitable causes he has undertaken today is due to God's protection. This is the secret to Mr. Lu's success in everything he does. Moreover, he seeks cooperation in everything, does not seek personal gain, and is willing to seek happiness for the public. Therefore, he has gained the trust of people from all walks of life. As a result, he has repeatedly received awards from the Pope. This time, he has even received a blessing by telegram. Cardinal Costantini, the Apostolic Delegate to China, and others have also sent telegrams of congratulations."

Mr. Lu's Reply 161

Finally, Mr. Lu gave a reply, saying, "Today is Bohong's sixtieth birthday, and I am honored to receive the kindness of friends from all walks of life, as well as the Mayor's gracious presence and Bishop Haouisée's blessings and exhortations. I, Bohong, am deeply grateful and apprehensive. I have made very few contributions to the country and society, and my age has only increased in vain. How can I dare to speak of longevity? However, the various industrial companies that I, Bohong, am responsible for have received guidance from the Mayor at all times, which has prevented them from failing. The charitable institutions that I have traveled around to raise donations for, such as the Xin Puyu Hall in Nanshi, now care for over two thousand poor and disabled patients. The Sacred Heart Hospital in Yangshupu also has over a hundred patients. The medical clinics in various places provide medical treatment and medicine free of charge. In total, about four to five thousand people are rescued every day. The maintenance of the city government and the generous donations from people from all walks of life are essential. Such a large-scale relief effort cannot be accomplished by one person alone. It is truly due to God's protection that we have today's results. This is what I, Bohong, can be somewhat comforted by. What I would like to inform people from all walks of life is that recently, I have observed that the Zhabei area has thriving factories and shops, a large population, and is gradually recovering to the state before the January 28 Incident. There are not many hospitals that seek health for the public, which has caused me concern. Therefore, I plan to build the Muxin Hospital to benefit the residents of Zhabei. Now that I have received the kindness of everyone and the generous gifts on my humble birthday, I will use them all to fund the construction of the hospital, which is tantamount to asking for donations from all the great philanthropists to accomplish this good deed. In the future, the establishment of the hospital will all be thanks to the gifts of people from all walks of life. The book says, 'The family that accumulates good deeds will surely have blessings to spare.' I only hope that the Mayor, the Bishop, and all the great philanthropists will have much happiness and many plans, and I will bow nine times on behalf of the residents of Zhabei to thank you." The guests did not disperse until about 10:00 PM that evening.

On Wasteland on Xiaoshadu Road

Male Corpse Found Strangled; A Hemp Rope Around the Neck 163

At around 6:00 AM yesterday, a male corpse was found on the wasteland near Macau Road, Xiaoshadu Road, in West Shanghai. The man was about thirty to forty years old, wearing a blue cotton short shirt and black cloth pants. His hands were tied behind his back, and a hemp rope was wrapped around his neck, suggesting that he had been strangled to death. The relevant Putuo Road Police Station was notified and immediately sent detectives to investigate and take photographs and fingerprints for record. The hemp rope was also taken back to the police station to trace the clues of the case. The corpse was transported to the morgue for examination and will be coffined after a report is made to the court for inspection tomorrow morning.

Shops Near Jing'an Temple

Please Widen the Sidewalk: Booths Obstruct Business During the Bathing Buddha Festival; the Municipal Council Widens It from Two to Five Feet 166

The 34th District Branch of the Citizens' Federation recently received a joint letter from more than a hundred member stores near Jing'an Temple, stating that during the Jing'an Temple Bathing Buddha Festival, the nearby stalls were crowded, and the sidewalk was only three feet wide, which not only hindered business but also posed a danger. They requested the Federation to send personnel to negotiate with the Municipal Council to widen the sidewalk. After learning about the situation, the Federation immediately appointed Zhang Yichen, Qin Linxian, Cai Jiugao, Feng Guangjia, and others to negotiate. The Municipal Council then sent He Dekui to conduct an on-site survey. Upon reporting back to Superintendent Zhong Si, Zhong immediately dispatched Assistant Mian Shi to instruct the Public Works Department to re-plan and widen the sidewalk by two feet to five feet. However, many store members insisted that a distance of one zhang (approximately 10 feet) was necessary, so the negotiation remained unresolved.

Japanese Consulate Cracks Down on Dine-and-Dashers 167

According to yesterday's Japanese-language Shanghai Daily News, Zhongtian Zhenyilang, a textile supplies peddler at No. 16, Derun Lane, Xihua Road, and Zhiye Suiwang at No. 62, Labourson Road, incurred dining expenses of 16 yuan at the Linglan Cafe at No. 10, East Qiu Jiang Road, on the first of this month. After they finished eating, they claimed they did not have money on them and requested a one-day delay. By the next day, Zhongtian was unable to raise the funds and made various excuses to evade payment. The cafe owner, Murakami, then accompanied Zhongtian to the Consulate General to request their intervention. However, the consulate was powerless since the men were penniless. It was found that the men were known for their dine-and-dash schemes. On April 30th, they had previously dined and dashed at the Songwu restaurant on Xing Road. The Japanese Consulate Police Department, concerned about the repeated instances of shameless dine-and-dash behavior by Japanese residents in Shanghai, has resolved to thoroughly crack down on such incidents.

Yesterday's Heavy Fog Affected Various Ships

Ships Blocked Outside Wusong Estuary: Only Two Ningbo Ships Arrived; Ningxing Damaged in the Fog 168

Yesterday, the weather in Shanghai was overcast, and heavy fog occurred both at the Wusong Estuary and in the Yangtze River. Many incoming ships did not arrive in Shanghai. The Ningxing, a Shanghai-Ningbo liner from the Sanbei Shipping Company, collided with a warship in the Huangpu River while entering the port, causing slight damage to the stern. It was repaired that day and departed as scheduled in the afternoon. The situation of ships being blocked by the fog is described in detail below.

Temple Fog Hinders Navigation 169

Yesterday morning, heavy fog descended on the sea outside the Wusong Estuary. The shipping companies’ liners from the south and north returning to Shanghai included Swire's Hubei from Yingkou, Suzhou from Nanhua, Shiyo’s Haosheng from India, China Merchants' Kunxing from Hong Kong and Guangdong, Xinfeng from Beiyang, Haixiang from Guangzhou, and Gongping from Qingdao. In addition, foreign ships included Great Britain’s Mengtou from Hong Kong, and Ting’s Luoer from Europe from Europe. These ships encountered fog in the ocean outside the Wusong Estuary. Due to the obscured sea routes and poor visibility, they anchored at sea to avoid the danger of running aground or colliding in the heavy fog. Therefore, they were unable to enter the port.

River Ships Not Arriving 170

The Yangtze River liners of various companies have fixed dates for entering and leaving the port, and these cannot be easily changed. Yesterday, the Yangtze River ships that were supposed to arrive in Shanghai included China Merchants' Jiangshun and Jardine Matheson's Ruihe, as well as several smaller Yangtze River ships. However, due to the extremely heavy fog downstream of the Yangtze River, which persisted throughout the day, the river ships were unable to see anything on the river surface due to the obscured waterways. They had to anchor temporarily and wait for the fog to dissipate before sailing to Shanghai. After anchoring, the ships sounded foghorns as usual as signals to avoid collisions with other ships.

Yongxing Slightly Damaged 171

Yesterday, not a single Yangtze River or sea-going ship arrived in Shanghai, except for the Ningbo liners Xinjingtian and Ningxing, which braved the fog to enter the port. When the Ningxing sailed into Wusong and reached the Huangpu River, the fog had not yet cleared, making it difficult to see clearly on the river surface. As a result, when the Ningxing was entering the Huangpu River, it rubbed against a British ship and a warship of an unspecified country anchored on the river surface while trying to avoid them. The stern of the Ningxing rubbed against the hull of the warship, causing minor damage. It then sailed to the Nanshi pier, where it unloaded cargo and passengers and underwent minor repairs. It departed from Shanghai for Ningbo as scheduled at 5:00 PM. The incident of the collision has been reported to the company, but the damage was minimal.

Publishing Industry 174

"Strikes and Shutdowns in Shanghai in the Past Fifteen Years," A Special Publication on Labor Statistics by the Shanghai Municipal Government's Social Bureau: "Strikes and Shutdowns in Shanghai in the Past Fifteen Years," published by the Zhonghua Book Company, December 1933, first edition. The book has 306 pages, with 14 statistical charts, 16 tables, and 7 appendices, priced at five yuan. This compilation, "Strikes and Shutdowns in Shanghai in the Past Fifteen Years," is not only a revision of the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau's previous special publications and a continuation of its previous reports but also a systematic compilation of strike and shutdown events in the city from 1918 to the present, a continuous statistical record, and a comprehensive exploration. The Bureau mediated in eighty to ninety percent of strike and shutdown events in the city. In addition to contacting both labor and management, statistical materials include investigations, records, and documented cases. The ins and outs of these events are thoroughly understood, accurate, and reliable. Moreover, the Bureau places great emphasis on statistical methods. The strike and shutdown statistical method is based on the framework established by the International Labour Office, while also taking into account the domestic situation. This compilation re-edits past cases to ensure consistency, and the charts and indexes facilitate comparison and reference. Finally, beyond the statistical data, this compilation analyzes the historical background, such as the Chinese labor movement, legal changes, and the waxing and waning of influence between labor and management, how it transformed from a quiet past through an eventful process to the current situation. This analysis is insightful and concise. Statistics without historical and environmental context lack clear and definite meaning.

Publication of "A Social History of China": This book is divided into three parts. The first part, "Introduction," elucidates the basic consciousness of Chinese society, the significance of Chinese social history, ethnic struggles, and development. The second part, "The Essence of Chinese Society," analyzes the Chinese social system. The third part, "The Evolution of Chinese Society," narrates the evolution of material life, such as clothing, food, housing, and other aspects. The entire book is based on rigorous argumentation and reliable textual research, representing a unique contribution to Chinese sociology. It is published by the World Book Company, originally priced at 75 cents, now available at a special price of 45 cents.

Special Feature

A History of the Revision of the Shen Bao Yearbook 181

The Shen Bao Yearbook was originally created to commemorate the 60th anniversary of the Shen Bao. The work began in July of the 21st year and was completed in April of the following year. After its publication, it received widespread praise, which was beyond the expectations of the colleagues involved. However, in China, due to the difficulty in collecting statistics and the challenge of preparing accurate materials, it was inevitable that there would be errors and omissions in the completion of such a large work within a short period of several months. After the completion of the first editorial work, the colleagues thoroughly reviewed it and felt deeply ashamed. Grateful for the criticisms and corrections from enthusiastic supporters, the colleagues gained a clearer understanding of the shortcomings and the goals for improvement. Mr. Shi Liangcai, the general manager of the Shen Bao, and Mr. Zhang Yunhe, the chief editor, also believed that since the first yearbook was popular throughout the country, the content should be further refined to meet the expectations of readers both at home and abroad. Therefore, a thorough revision was undertaken. The noteworthy aspects of the revision process are:

1. Collaboration with Experts and Various Sectors: The Shen Bao Yearbook is of a general nature and covers a wide range of areas. To obtain comprehensive materials in each category, it was not sufficient to rely on ordinary solicitation. At the beginning of this revision, special efforts were made to seek the practical cooperation of domestic experts, professionals, institutions, and organizations to complete a more comprehensive general yearbook. Fortunately, various sectors generously provided valuable advice, either by undertaking the drafting of special articles, pointing out key areas for improvement, or providing materials that were not easily obtained. As can be seen from the separately listed "Specially Invited Editors" and "Material Providers" tables, this two-million-word work was the result of the collective wisdom and efforts of scholars and experts throughout the country, and not something that the colleagues involved dared to claim credit for on their own.

2. Implementation of a Communication Investigation: According to the established rules for editing yearbooks, the principle is to solicit and collect various published statistics. However, the completion of a comprehensive statistic takes a long time, and by the time it is published, those who are not familiar with the actual situation of statistical compilation may find it outdated. During the first edition, considerable effort was made to solicit and collect materials, but there were still those who criticized the materials for being too old. For this revision, a communication investigation was conducted in the areas of "Population," "Agriculture and Forestry," and "Cooperation." The results are as follows: In the population category, data was quickly obtained from the civil affairs departments of more than a dozen provinces and various municipal governments, allowing for the compilation of a "Trial Compilation of National Household Population Table" with reference to population tables in various publications. The total population was 477,353,7335, which is close to the results of Mr. Wang Shida's survey at the Institute of Social Research, suggesting that the investigation was not a complete failure. In the agriculture and forestry category, experts provided important statistics that had not been obtained during the previous solicitation. In the cooperation category, the survey materials were more reliable than the previous ones due to the cooperation association issuing announcements and conducting the investigation. Although the communication investigation did not yield a large amount of data, it cannot be said that there was no progress. Therefore, it is planned to continue this practice in the future to achieve perfection. If various institutions and organizations provide active assistance, allowing for gradual updates, the benefits will extend far beyond the colleagues involved.

After this thorough revision of the Shen Bao Yearbook, the colleagues are not yet ready to definitively say how many parts can be considered to have a solid foundation. However, the experience gained from this revision has made them realize the difficulty of the task. During the revision period, in order to ensure accuracy, the specially invited authors and internal colleagues repeatedly withdrew and revised the drafts that had already been issued. As a result, the amount of material increased compared to the original plan, and the publication was delayed. After the review was completed, there was still a sense that many aspects were not satisfactory. As for the changes to the previously listed categories, the intention was to eliminate unimportant independent sections and merge them into related sections to avoid duplication and facilitate checking. However, whether this is appropriate and whether it will be convenient for reviewing remains to be seen and is subject to the guidance of experts.

Grateful to the enthusiastic teachers who corrected and supplied materials, to those who undertook the writing of the drafts, and to the various institutions and organizations that provided assistance, we hereby express our gratitude. Zhang Zishen, March 4, 5.
