Special document

The National Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration 23 184

First Quarter Work Overview (2)

Regulations for Publication of Periodic Reports 185

Our bureau's external reports have only included accounting and statistical annual reports, limited to the year and primarily in English. This is detailed in economics but lacking in substance and insufficient to represent the overall business situation of our railway. Another publication each year, "An Overview" and "Quarterly Work Summaries," are also limited to the year and are in Chinese. The style of the "Overview" is mostly tables, while the "Work Summaries" are narrative and can supplement the accounting and statistical annual reports. Therefore, it was decided to make these three types the bureau's annual periodic reports and to formulate publication methods, which were submitted to the bureau's business meeting for approval and implementation.

3. Development and Expansion of Business: Promote business offices, promote combined water, land, and air transportation, sell fourth-class tickets for Weiting to Guandu Li, add temporary inter-city trains, promote spring travel, relax restrictions on the types of mixed-loaded goods in a whole car, reduce freight rates for pigs and grain, extend the storage period for goods at the Maigen Road warehouse, establish regulations for the custody of boats and vehicles, establish a sample display room for goods, and investigate the economic situation along the railway line.

Promoting Business Offices 186

Our bureau, adhering to the principle of proactively attracting passenger and freight transportation, first established a business office on Jing'an Temple Road in Shanghai in August of last year. This office piloted services such as answering inquiries, selling passenger tickets, and handling luggage. Later, it also began to handle freight transportation. This year, we also established a cooperative arrangement with China Travel Service. All goods or packages shipped to railway stations with business offices by the various branch offices of China Travel Service will be picked up and delivered by our business offices. For locations without business offices, the business offices will act as agents, handling the pick-up, delivery, shipment, loading, unloading, and collection of payments for goods. Since then, business operations have gradually developed, with daily receipts averaging around 1,500 yuan. Answering inquiries also occurs no less than 140-150 times per day, indicating that the office meets the needs of the public. Therefore, on January 1st of this year, we rented a residential building at No. 10, South Outer Ma Road in Shanghai to establish a business branch (later, due to the small size of the premises, we re-rented No. 18 Outer Ma Road and moved in on March 20th). At the same time, we actively prepared for a Nanjing branch, renting No. 372 Taiping Road as the location, which opened on February 10th.

Promoting Combined Water, Land, and Air Transportation 187

Combined transportation between railways and other water and land routes not only increases convenience for travelers but is also very beneficial to the railway's own business. Our railway has been steadily progressing in this area in recent years, achieving good results. The Zhejiang Province's Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway originally handled combined passenger and freight transportation with our railway. Since the completion and opening of the Jinyu section at the end of last December, it was proposed to add the Huzhen, Longyou, Anren, Zhangshutan, Quzhou, Jiangshan, Hecun, Yushan, and eight stations to the combined transportation network. Our bureau immediately agreed and implemented this on March 1st of this year. In January, the Yangtze River was shallow, hindering navigation. Following the orders of the Ministry of Railways, we jointly arranged combined Shanghai-Hankou transportation with the Pinghan, Longhai, and Jinpu Railways. Starting from February 5th, daily round-trip services operated between Shanghai North Station and Hankou. The Shanghai-Xuzhou section temporarily utilized the Shanghai-Ping service. Passengers from Shanghai could take the 302 express train at 12:00 every night (changed to 4:05 PM daily starting April 1st) to Xuzhou, then transfer to Hankou via Zhengzhou. As the transportation of parcels between Shanghai and Hankou increased daily, we also discussed opening direct combined parcel service between Shanghai North Station and Dazhimen in Hankou. The Pinghan Railway provided three cars, and the Longhai, Jinpu, and Jinghu Railways each provided two cars, forming a total of nine cars. Each week, three round trips operated between Shanghai and Hankou, attached to the 11th and 12th trains of the Pinghan Railway, the 13th and 14th trains of the Longhai Railway, the 5th and 6th trains of the Jinpu Railway, and the 9th, 22nd, and 24th trains of the Jinghu Railway, directly crossing the river. The Joint Transportation Office of the Ministry of Railways also, in response to the increasing development of combined parcel transportation and to meet the needs of society, submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval and publication of regulations for the payment of combined parcel transportation fees upon arrival. Our railway implemented this starting April. As for the LCL (less-than-carload) freight cars between Shanghai and Xuzhou, we had previously agreed with the Jinpu Railway to send personnel to directly escort the goods. However, due to a lack of escort personnel, this was delayed. We have now selected eight luggage porters from Shanghai North Station for training and have agreed with the Jinpu Railway to implement the combined transportation method starting April 1st. In addition, regarding the Jinghu Railway, in addition to adding the Dahongqiao stop to the combined Qingyanggang-Hupu ferry service, we have been handling combined passenger, luggage, and parcel transportation with long-distance buses from Zhenjiang to Yangzhou since January 21st, and with long-distance buses from Zhenjiang via Danyang to Jintan since March 1st. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway also started handling combined passenger transportation with the Sanqingji steamboat, which operates from Zhouzhuang in Wujiang County via Lili and Luxu to Jiashan, starting March 1st. Our bureau believes that this cooperative method is beneficial to all parties and is considering extending it to air transportation, planning to hold separate combined transportation events with China and Eurasia Airlines in order to create a national water, land, and air transportation network, which is currently under negotiation.

Selling Fourth-Class Tickets from Weiting to Guandu Li 188

The Jinghu Railway began selling fourth-class tickets from Weiting to Suzhou in June of last year. Based on observations over the past six months, most of these passengers were Weiting weavers traveling between Weiting and Guandu Li, with very few going to Suzhou. Therefore, we changed to selling fourth-class tickets from Weiting to Guandu Li, tentatively priced at one dime to assist the common people. At the same time, we canceled the fourth-class tickets from Weiting to Suzhou to avoid unnecessary losses.

Adding Temporary Inter-city Trains 189

In the early part of this quarter, during the winter season, there were particularly many passengers, especially those taking the Jinghu Line via Zhenjiang to Jiangbei. Therefore, starting February 8th, we temporarily added a Shanghai-Wuxi inter-city train, departing at 2:50 AM, with ten third- and fourth-class cars, so that passengers between Wuxi and Shanghai would not be crowded on the Shanghai-Zhenjiang train. At the same time, we added cars to the Shanghai-Wuxi third- and fourth-class inter-city train departing at 5:00 AM and attached it to the Yangzhou-Wuxi-Nanjing inter-city train after arriving in Wuxi to facilitate traffic.

Promoting Spring Travel 190

As winter ended and spring returned, with pleasant scenery, the areas along our railway, such as Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Suzhou, and Hangzhou, were all famous scenic spots in Jiangnan. Every year, travel to these places is very popular. Therefore, we formulated methods to promote travel, such as arranging accommodations and transportation, and published promotional brochures to encourage interest. We also selected capable staff to handle recruitment and guidance, increasing convenience. We also stipulated that starting March 30th, special tour trains to Hangzhou would run for five days, with one extra round-trip express train between Shanghai North Station and Hangzhou each day to facilitate travel.

Continuing to Relax Restrictions on the Types of Mixed-Loaded Goods in a Whole Car 191

Railway freight transportation regulations stipulate that a maximum of five different types of goods can be mixed in one car. However, our railway's average proportion of transported goods is mostly foreign general merchandise. Passengers mostly ship mixed items. This was clarified to the Ministry of Railways last year, and approval was granted to relax the restrictions on the types of goods in a whole car to ten on our railway. This was piloted for six months starting July 1st. After implementation, both the railway and merchants found it convenient. Therefore, before the expiration date, we submitted an application for approval to continue for another six months, starting January 1st of this year. (To be continued)

Letter to the Editor

To the Esteemed Editor,

I am writing to you concerning the news item in your newspaper's local news column on May 5th, regarding a large shipment of Taiwanese longan, which stated, "Our company recently sent people to Taiwan to purchase a large quantity of longan and dried longan, and it is rumored that more than a thousand pieces will arrive soon." This information is inaccurate. Our company is merely an agent that buys and sells goods on behalf of customers, earning commission. We have never sent anyone to purchase goods from various locations. Although fifteen pieces of dried longan and twelve pieces of dried meat were shipped to us in April, these were sent by the cargo owner without our company's prior consent and entrusted to us for exchange. We have already informed the sender of our position, requesting that they transfer the goods to another company or have them shipped back. We have not yet received a reply. The statement in the report that our company sent people to Taiwan to purchase the goods is completely unfounded. As for the claim that a large shipment of Taiwanese goods will arrive soon, this is even more groundless and based on pure conjecture. We are concerned that the public will be misled by this false information. Therefore, we are writing to request that you publish this letter in your letters to the editor column and issue a correction. We would be most grateful.

Sincerely,

Dalaehua Company

May 5th

Q&A on Reading – Doubts after Reading "Source Material on the History of the New Chinese Literature Movement" (Continued II) – Reply to Mr. Wang Renkan – 192

The growth of a new kind of literature depends on the substance of a prosperous class life. Let us look at those neutral figures who linger in the "Palace of Art," how they support the facade of their literature on their shallow and soft life foundation! They either completely Europeanize, using the pleasure of the expiration period of capitalism as the content of their literary works, or they fall into metaphysics. Here, we can cite several works as examples. Bing Xin's "Stars" and "Letters to Young Readers" were widely circulated at the time, but when we further examine them, what else do these things express besides the so-called superficial individualistic love? Liu Dabai's "Old Dreams" can be said to be a variant of the Mao Poetry, full of metaphysical tones in content. Others, such as Wang Jingzhi's "The Wind of Hui" and Yu Pingbo's "Winter Night," are all spinning around in such a small world. As for Xu Zhimo, he is merely "integrating their great achievements." According to the general historical process of literary development, the initial stage of the emergence of a new kind of literature should be aggressive and revolutionary; it should be content over form. However, the literature of China's emerging bourgeoisie has taken the completely opposite form. What does this show? This shows that the national bourgeoisie, as soon as it raises its head, embarks on a path of collapse, losing its fighting power and unable to enrich the content of its class life. Therefore, in literature, the general intellectuals only pick up the dregs of the life of the European and American bourgeoisie in the period of decline. They can only use tricks of form to embellish their own superficiality. Even in the use of language, what they have achieved, besides Europeanized sentences, is new-style classical Chinese, because the completion of a language movement is also subject to great limitations of social conditions.

Speaking of this, we should especially remind the reader that, in the process of our new literary movement, when we are completely disappointed with the upper-class intellectuals of the national bourgeoisie, when we examine that although the "May Fourth Movement" launched a new literary movement, it did not complete any tasks in the literary movement, do we think that the new literary movement has stopped its operation? No, we must pay attention to one thing! The "May Fourth Movement" has enabled the new literary movement to penetrate into the petty-bourgeois student and small-citizen strata, then, inevitably, this broader group will rise up to demand their own literature. At a certain period, they were more active than the upper-class bourgeois intellectuals. Although they are the easiest to waver, they stand in the middle from the bourgeoisie to the masses. They can easily see the powerlessness of the bourgeoisie, and at the same time, they can easily discover the undercurrents among the lower masses. Therefore, when the bourgeois intellectuals have lost their power in the literary movement, and the lower masses have not yet reached the maturity to bear this responsibility, the petty bourgeoisie just happens to be the bridge of this transitional era. While denying the achievements of bourgeois intellectuals in the new literary movement, we should also recognize the various groups representing the petty bourgeoisie who supported this movement after "May Fourth." Then, we cannot but fall on the Zhou brothers, the Creation Society and the Literary Research Society.

On the whole, they—these advanced representatives of the petty bourgeoisie—gave this new literary movement a specific content. They put forward the slogan "Art for Life," which seems nothing special at present, but at that time, for those feudal literati who were artists for "fame" or for "interest," for those bourgeois literati who were breaking ranks for art, we cannot ignore its practical combat meaning. In terms of creation, some progressive things have also been produced. First of all, we should mention the unforgettable Lu Xun, whose works, from "Diary of a Madman" to "The True Story of Ah Q," are full of active anti-feudal significance. Secondly, Guo Moruo's poems and his "Three Rebellious Women," both in content and form, are also brand-new works, works with new life. If we want to raise the issue of accepting literary heritage, only these little bits of heritage are worth accepting.

Then, on this unified single line, why are so many different barriers formed? Why did the Literary Research Society and the Creation Society stand against each other at this time? Obviously, this is because of the imbalance of social development and the defects of their class itself, which are reflected in literature, so that various stages of literary thought that have undergone a long period of development in Europe appear in China in a complex and simultaneous manner. When we recognize this problem, we must not think that this is a bad phenomenon. We must not be afraid of struggle. Their struggle is no longer a matter of form like the debate on vernacular literature, but a more practical matter of content. To be sure, the Literary Research Society is conservative and tends to naturalism, and the Creation Society is progressive and tends to romanticism. But our understanding should be limited to this point, and we should not further defend anyone. Their struggle has a considerable effect in promoting the growth of another stage of the new literary movement; at the same time, they are all limited by their own stage, but no one has the courage to enter that new stage. When society progresses rapidly, after the waves of the "February 8th," "May 30th," and even the great revolution of 1925-1927, when the lower masses rise up to demand their own literature and consciously take on the task of this new literary movement, even the Creation Society, which was the first to put forward the call for "revolutionary literature," has changed its face from the previous Creation Society. (To be continued)

Weather Report 193

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: Shandong and surrounding areas are cloudy with easterly winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River and this area are overcast with fog and intermittent drizzle. Winds are from southeast to northeast. There are cyclonic winds, thunderstorms, or showers south of Ma'an Island and in the East China Sea, caused by low pressure moving slowly northeastward. There is low pressure in the northern part of China. Furthermore, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city was a high of 68.2 and a low of 59.0. On the same day last year, the high was 77.4 and the low was 52.7.

The First Workers Games Organized by the General Labor Union

Grand Opening Ceremony Held Yesterday Morning. Mayor Wu Attended and Spoke to Encourage Workers' Organizations to Save the Country. Various Labor Unions Performed Group Exercises in the Rain with a Solemn Formation. Competitions Began in the Track and Field in the Afternoon with Excellent Results. The Games Will Continue for One Day Today. 201

In order to promote mass sports and improve workers' health, the Shanghai General Labor Union specially organized the First Shanghai Workers Games. The opening ceremony was held at the West Gate City Sports Field at 9:00 AM yesterday. Honorary President Wu Tiecheng attended and delivered a speech. Despite the rain during the opening ceremony yesterday morning, all the competitors and members of the military training classes of various labor unions were full of energy and marched around the field in the rain. The order was strict and the ceremony was grand. The Lianhua and Mingxing film companies took footage. From 2:00 PM, various competitions began at the China Track and Field. The audience was very enthusiastic, creating a new era for the sports community. The details are recorded separately below.

Opening Ceremony

Venue Arrangement: The opening ceremony of the Games was held at the City No. 1 Sports Field. The party and national flags were crossed outside the gate, and a white cloth banner with the words "The First Shanghai Workers Games of the Shanghai General Labor Union" was hung above it. The platform was set up in the north of the field, with a portrait of the Prime Minister in the center. The party and national flags were placed on both sides of the portrait. The front of the platform was filled with more than one hundred prizes donated by government officials, various agencies, and various sectors. They were dazzling and beautiful. The venue was also equipped with a generator for making reports. The order of the entire venue was maintained by members of the military training class of various labor unions, as well as more than one hundred boy scouts from Junyi, Shangzhong, Shixiao, and Post Office workers. The Shanghai Public Security Bureau dispatched inspectors and detectives to assist. The post office workers' military band played music, and the order was quite orderly and solemn.

Participating Figures: Those who attended the opening ceremony yesterday included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director of the Social Bureau Wu Xingya, Director of the Education Bureau Pan Gongzhan, City Party Representative Tao Baichuan, Legislative Member Wu Kaixian, Public Security Bureau Director Wen Hongen, City Councilor Lu Jingshi, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau Xu Peihuang, Postal Director Qu Peilin of the Postal Administration, Ma Shaoquan of the City Chamber of Commerce, and guests Hong Yanbin, Ren Jinping, Xu Yefu, Tang Jiazong, Li Jing, as well as the President and Vice President of the Games Zhu Xuefan and Zhou Xuexiang, Preparation Director Li Mengnan, Secretary-General Zhao Shusheng, Shao Xubai, staff members Ye Xianggao, Long Peiyun, Fan Yifeng, and Lu Junyun, as well as more than 10,000 spectators from all walks of life. Opening Ceremony: The music played at 9:00 AM. After the opening ceremony, the flag-raising ceremony was held first. Then, the officials of the Games, referees, members of the military training class of various labor unions, and all the athletes marched around the field for one week in the rain led by the music team. After the ceremony was performed as usual, Chairman Zhu Xuefan delivered the opening speech, and Preparation Director Li Mengnan reported on the preparations. Then, Honorary Presidents and Vice Presidents Wu Tiecheng, Wu Xingya, Tao Baichuan, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Kaixian, and Lu Jingshi delivered speeches one after another. Finally, the music played and announced the end of the ceremony, and everyone took a group photo (Datong Photo Studio). Then, more than 300 members of the military training class of various labor unions performed military exercises and group exercises, and also performed obstacle course competitions. From 2:00 PM, various competitions began at the China Track and Field Stadium.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Zhu Xuefan said in his opening speech, "Representatives of Party and government agencies, guests from all walks of life, and all the athletic heroes of the Workers Games, today is the opening of the First Shanghai Workers Games. I am grateful for the guidance of the representatives of the higher-level agencies and guests from all walks of life, and for the enthusiastic participation of workers' organizations and male and female workers throughout Shanghai. Although the Workers Games in Shanghai, or perhaps in China, this Games is still an unprecedented initiative every time. However, seeing the full spirit and tense atmosphere in today's Games, we can prove that the bright future of the Chinese labor movement will be opened vigorously after the opening of the Games. Then, how worthy is today's Games for us to celebrate! At the same time, we are grateful to the higher-level agencies and fellow countrymen from all walks of life who have guided us and helped us to hold this Games."

Mayor Wu's Address (Photo by Xu Tianzhang) 202

The Shanghai Municipal Workers' Union First All...The intention should be how grateful ah! Revolutionary workers participating in the conference, when holding the conference here, we must understand that the revival of the Chinese revolutionary movement, the salvation of China's difficulties, and the success of the Chinese revolutionary movement are all urgently awaiting our revolutionary workers to work together. This conference is a review of our revolutionary forces, and it is also the beginning of our responsibilities. The strong men participating in the conference today will be the worker soldiers standing on the front line of the revolution in the future. Therefore, I believe that the significance and mission of this Shanghai Municipal Workers' Movement Conference are beyond the significance of general sports meets, and it has a more significant meaning and a more difficult task. China's social and economic class is transitioning from an agricultural and handicraft economy to an industrial and scientific arena. People living in an agricultural and handicraft economic society have a slow, scattered, unstrict, and unregulated life. Therefore, others often scold us Chinese as a pile of loose sand. We examine ourselves and we are indeed like a plate of loose sand. How can we survive in this world surrounded by organized and tense powerful countries? Moreover, due to the objective environment, we know that various reactionary forces are hindering us. China's national revolution and economic construction have not yet been completed. It is because of this uncompleted and abnormal situation that the economic life of the people is becoming increasingly depressed and difficult, the people's situation is becoming increasingly passive and pessimistic, and social morality is becoming increasingly corrupt and declining. Only cruel and ruthless competition for private interests is seen between society and individuals. Other active and just activities are nowhere to be seen. Due to the objective environmental reasons mentioned above and the abnormal subjective weaknesses, our group life and mass life are affected. It can be said that the lives of ordinary people have very little discipline and are extremely unstrict, resulting in the lack of energy in the national spirit and the lack of tension in revolutionary emotions. We can know these facts as long as we think about them and take a look at them. Let's not talk about the facts of aggression and oppression that the imperialists have imposed on us in the past. Now, let's just talk about the cruel bloody lessons that the Japanese imperialists have given us since the September 18th Incident, the January 28th Incident, and the Battle of Rehe. The Japanese imperialists destroyed our prosperous Southeast market and completely occupied our Northeast Four Provinces. They also used warships and airplanes to intimidate our coastal areas and vainly attempted to create puppet forces in the North China provinces. As long as they can create chaos in China and oppose the central government, the Japanese imperialists do not hesitate to provide huge amounts of money and weapons to fund their activities. In North China, the Japanese imperialists disregarded treaty constraints and acted recklessly, which has become a very open fact. Compatriots, in fact, we are already complete slaves of a fallen nation. Are we still waiting to be ghosts of a fallen nation? "An eye for an eye, a tooth for a tooth!" Today, we only have to prepare to shed blood and shed the last drop of blood. This is our plan to save the country, our aspiration to save the country, our plan for revolution, and our aspiration for revolution. However, preparing to shed blood is not easy to do, and it requires technology. The first step is to transform the revolutionary environment. We must create a large number of revolutionary fighters to enrich the foundation of the revolution. The second step is to organize ourselves and train ourselves so that we know how to go and fight desperately, instead of being slaughtered and treated as food. That is to say, we must know how to value every drop of our own blood, instead of letting others suck it without any resistance. Compatriots, a nation of loose sand, a corrupt and weak nation that only knows how to covet private interests, they do not know how to love and cherish their own blood and let it flow to the glorious road. We must bear the mission of revolution, we must have subjective cultivation conditions and personal fighting skills, and to go a step further, we must sweep away the weakness, looseness, corruption, stubbornness, indiscipline, disregard for order, and all aspects of life that are not suitable for today's world stage of life and struggle, and make our actions organized and disciplined, and our spirit solemn and active. For the specific methods of cultivation and training required for this, it is what Chairman Chiang recently announced, "to militarize the national life of the whole country." We must use the spirit and methods of militarization to change and save the weaknesses in our previous lives and make ourselves a team that is brave, knowledgeable, able to speak, and able to act. The significance of this first Shanghai Municipal Workers' Movement Conference, I believe, is not the significance of a general sports meet, but that the working masses of Shanghai will start to eliminate the weaknesses in the national life of the past, follow the announcement of the supreme leader, rectify themselves, train themselves, and embark on the leading position of the revolution. The establishment of new moral standards and the cultivation of new forces of the Chinese nation can all be recognized from this sports meet.

Preparation Report: Li Mengnan, Director of the Conference Preparation Committee, reported on the preparation process, saying briefly that today, the first Workers' Games are held here at the opening ceremony, preparing to use sports to train the body and revive the Chinese nation. Regarding the preparation process of this conference, it is divided into three steps. The first step is to propagate to various factories after the resolution of the General Labor Union's full committee meeting. The second step is to actively do internal work, such as soliciting prizes. The third step is to plan the order of sports, the venue, hire instructors, etc. Thanks to the help and guidance of Mr. Ling Xitao and Mr. Xu Duo, I would like to express my gratitude.

Mayor's Address: Mayor Wu Tiecheng gave an address, saying briefly that today is the opening of the city's first Workers' Movement Conference. We see the spirit of all the athletes, and we have infinite hope for the future of the country and the nation. We must know that workers occupy an important place in the organization of a modern country. Since workers bear a great responsibility for organizing a modern country, increasing production and enriching national strength are mostly on the workers. Of course, only when workers are organized, disciplined, and have a national system can they bear great responsibilities. This workers' physical exercise movement is to train workers' physique, so that workers have a group, have organization, and have discipline, so that they can generate strength, and only with strength can they enrich national strength and increase national production. Today, seeing the Workers' Games, there is already a new spirit full of hope for the revival of the Chinese nation. This hope really started from the Workers' Games. It occupies a very important page in the history of the revolution. In the memorial meeting, holding the city's Workers' Games fully shows that most of the workers are revolutionary elements. The success of the workers' movement is popularized to the people, and military training is used to perform sports, which is even more worth commemorating. Rabbit and the Moon 216

— Bing Yu

In a certain mountain, there lived a mother rabbit and two baby rabbits. The mother rabbit went to the forest alone to find something good to eat for the baby rabbits. Unexpectedly, she fell into a stone cave. The stone cave was five or six feet deep, and she couldn't climb out. The mother rabbit wept incessantly in the cave. After a while, a deer passed by the cave. The mother rabbit cried out for help. The deer looked at the deep stone cave and, seeing no way to help, raised its head and went its way. At this time, the two baby rabbits were very anxious because their mother had not returned for a long time. They left their burrow and went everywhere to look for her. Later, they walked to the side of the stone cave and heard their mother's mournful voice. They ran around the edge of the stone cave, frantic. The mother rabbit hurriedly said, "Now that you've arrived here and seen me trapped in this pit, you should think of a way to save me!" Although the two baby rabbits both wanted to save their mother, they saw that the stone cave was very deep and could only cry in despair.

Suddenly, a beam of moonlight appeared at the cave entrance. A woman descended and said, "Please save my mother, and I will never forget your great kindness. The woman said, "It's easy for me to save your mother's life, but I want the fur of you two." The baby rabbits thought, "I want to make clothes and hats." At this time, the two baby rabbits, seeing that their mother's life was in danger, couldn't care about their own bodies and agreed, "We can't sit by and watch our mother die in the stone cave. If you save our mother's life, we are willing to have our skin and fur stripped off, even if it means being crushed to powder." The woman heard this and immediately jumped into the stone cave and rescued the mother rabbit. She said, "I really don't want your fur. Your filial piety has moved me very much. You don't need to say much; just go back and be with your mother." After speaking, the woman disappeared.

Because they were grateful to the woman who appeared in the moonlight, from then on, every year on the night of the fifteenth day of the month, they invited a group of rabbits, mashed rice to make rice cakes, and offered them to the woman in the moon.

Page 16

Page 17

Women's Garden, Issue 11

League of Nations' Prostitution Prohibition Issue 217

— Tong Hua

The Advisory Committee on Protection of Women and Children of the League of Nations dispatched a fact-finding mission to the Far East last year. As a result, a report was produced, describing the situation of trafficking in women in the Orient. The report listed the countries with the most trafficking in women, with China being first, followed by Japan, then Korea, Malaysia, Annam, Siam, the Philippines, etc., with fewer cases. Trafficking in women also occurred in Asia Minor and the Near East. This trafficking mainly involved selling the victims into prostitution. The fact-finding mission proposed seven methods to prevent trafficking in women in various parts of the Far East. The main points were to abolish the issuance of licenses or publicly recognized brothels, paying special attention to Hong Kong and Shanghai; establishing a general anti-trafficking agency for women, strictly enforcing imprisonment, and closely cooperating with Geneva to exchange information.

According to a report from the Kuomin News Agency on the 11th of last month, the League of Nations also resolved to ban all brothels worldwide, in order to prevent the trafficking of women from recurring. The method was to notify the authorities of various countries not to issue licenses, so that the prostitution industry would lose its legal protection. After the prohibition of prostitution, each prostitute would be given a proper occupation, so that they could become good citizens.

This resolution of the League of Nations is a slight step forward compared to the proposal of last year's Far East Women's Fact-Finding Mission. Although both take the non-issuance of licenses as the first measure to prohibit prostitution, the former noted that "if, after the prohibition of prostitution, each prostitute can be given a proper occupation, then it will not be difficult for them to become good citizens." However, under these two measures of the League of Nations, whether the trafficking of women and the prostitution system can be eliminated immediately following this official document is highly debatable.

Prostitution cannot be eliminated by simply making prostitution less public. Although public prostitution is abolished, private prostitution will inevitably flourish as a result. If private prostitution flourishes, then the trafficking of women will inevitably continue. Why are some people willing to become private prostitutes? Why are some people willing to sell their wives and daughters? These are things that the gentlemen on the shores of Lake Geneva do not understand. Therefore, the methods they decide are naturally bound to be superficial. Now, let me talk about its reasons!

The production of the current system is the reproduction of surplus value. Under this production system, the accumulation of wealth is accompanied by the accumulation of poverty. On the one hand, there are a few extremely happy and idle people; on the other hand, there are many laborers who cannot marry in time, and women who have lost their means of living, are unemployed or without work. In this situation, there are people who enjoy pleasure, people who satisfy sexual desires, and people who are forced to exchange sex for a living. The contradictions of sexual morality, coupled with the contradictions of the economic system, inevitably lead to the existence of the prostitution system, and the trafficking of women into prostitution inevitably occurs. Bebel said, "Marriage is the sexuality of the bourgeois world," and on the other hand, it is prostitution. Marriage is the front of the shield, and prostitution is the back of the shield. Male society cannot be satisfied in marriage, so it usually goes to prostitutes to seek compensation." Therefore, "prostitution is a necessary institution of bourgeois society."

The cruel facts of the Western European bourgeoisie plundering backward nations can be evidenced by the example cited in Luxembourg's Introduction to Economics:

"Due to the lack of food and the sadness of separation from their children, most of the imprisoned natives died on the way to Keemali Port. Among the slaves, those who could not keep up with their companions due to fatigue were stabbed in the back with daggers by the Spaniards, who thought that they would be a threat if left behind, and were cruelly abused. These unfortunate creatures, completely naked, tired and injured, and almost unable to stand due to hunger, the sight of this tragedy was heart-rending. Their hands and feet were bound with iron chains. Not one of the young girls escaped the violence of these robbers (the Spaniards), who indulged in their lewdness and sacrificed them. As a result, most of the young girls had contracted venereal diseases and become permanently crippled... Once the natives became slaves, they were branded with a red-hot iron to mark them. Sometimes, part of the slaves were plundered by the captain and distributed among the soldiers. The soldiers used them as gambling items or sold them to Spanish immigrants. Merchants used them as commodities, exchanging them for wine, flour, sugar, and other daily necessities, and sent them to the parts of the Spanish colonies that needed slaves the most. During transportation, merchants confined the slaves to the bottom of the ship, without giving them seats, fresh air, or water, causing them to die."

This kind of inhumane robbery, although not present on the surface now, has not actually disappeared. The Far East Women's Fact-Finding Mission's claim that China is the country with the most trafficking in women is a good example. International imperialism, in order to maintain China's backwardness, on the one hand, maintains feudal forces, and on the other hand, carries out economic aggression. Especially since this global panic, the dumping of discounted goods by various countries has further accelerated the collapse of China's national economy. In rural areas, due to heavy exploitation, aquatic plants, leaves, wheat seedlings, and tree bark have become the peasants' wonderful foods to fill their stomachs, and selling their children has become their method of drinking poison to quench their thirst. "In Shaanxi, ten-year-old orphaned girls are sold for one or two silver dollars, but there are few buyers. In the Quanzhou area of Zhejiang, an eight-year-old girl sells for only twenty-two yuan, including the broker's fee, and a ten-year-old sells for only fifty yuan." In urban areas, the nascent industries are not immune to the blow of imperialism. The closure of silk mills, yarn mills, rubber factories, and match factories has left a large number of unemployed female workers with nowhere to go. In Shunde, Guangdong, the decline of the silk industry has led to more than 200,000 female workers wandering in Guangzhou,

living as maids or secretly engaging in prostitution, which is an example. "Even for women who can be employed in industry, commerce, or households, their wages are not high, and cannot be used to maintain a family's life. Thus, when the burden of life is too heavy, far exceeding what their meager wages can provide, their only way to cope with the difficulty is prostitution, in order to supplement their income." In this situation, there are a large number of women engaging in prostitution in various parts of China. In terms of the number of public and private prostitutes, there are more than 60,000 to 100,000 in Shanghai alone. In Nanjing, there are more than 3,000 private prostitutes. In Beiping, there are more than 2,000 public prostitutes. In Hankou, there are 1,735 public prostitutes, and the number of private prostitutes in these two places is several times that of public prostitutes, which is not included in the calculation. As for cities with around 1,000 public and private prostitutes, they are too numerous to count. How did this phenomenon occur? Isn't it caused by imperialism and feudal forces?

The contradictory social organization inevitably produces this dark phenomenon. With the premise of this contradictory social system, it is inevitable that there is no way to solve the problem. How can a piece of paper abolish trafficking in people? How can it abolish the prostitution system? In terms of the so-called post-event solutions, the more than 30 million unemployed workers and the tens of millions of hungry and cold people have already overwhelmed all capitalist countries. How can they find solutions for those women who have already fallen into the pit of fire? Hitler in Germany has already adopted the method of returning women from occupations to the family to solve the unemployment problem of male workers. How can he find proper occupations for prostitutes who live by prostitution? Therefore, the second method is also a dishonored check. Based on the above, this resolution of the League of Nations is just an empty theory that does not help the facts.

World's Great Thinkers' Opinions on Women's Issues (5) 218

— Hua

5. Schopenhauer

Arthur Schopenhauer was a German idealist philosopher and a pessimist. He was born in 1788 and died in 1860. The several British and French thinkers we discussed earlier were ardent advocates of women's equality, but Schopenhauer was an extremely abusive critic of women. His "On Women" (translated by Zhang Weici, Shenzhou Publishing) scolds women as worse than chickens and dogs. First, let's talk about his points against women's liberation, and then explore the reasons for his reactionary thoughts.

First, he fundamentally looked down on women, believing that women were not worthy of doing great things. He said, "You only need to look at the shape of women,

New Sorrow, Azure Distance 219

When women speak of the word "sorrow," people invariably think of Lin Daiyu, a beauty who is both talented and sickly, but that is not the point.

Just now, the landlord upstairs was scolding the nanny with authority, scolding her for sneaking out all day and not cooking. He was a cadre during the "May Eighth" Beijing student movement. How could he, on the anniversary of his glorious history, be alone in his room, starving? Anyone would feel anger rising from within.

The nanny was also a very capable nanny. She did not retreat at all in reason. Just listen to the back-and-forth arguments between the master and servant:

"You must have gone to that Wang Mazi's place again, you bastard!"

"Sir! If I could earn three more yuan a month here, I wouldn't go."

"Your conscience is so black! Other people's nannies get four yuan a month, and I've already paid that amount. You want me to pay seven yuan!"

"I didn't say I wanted you to pay seven yuan a month, but if I'm short three yuan and can't find a way, I'll naturally have to run out. Two boys at home, living with other people, cost six yuan a month. The remaining one yuan, I have to save in case I have another son. If it's a girl, it's fine to just kill her."

Hearing this, the landlord was stunned for a moment. But after a moment, another kind of frustrated hero's anger welled up in him. He said:

"Even if you're going to do bad things, you shouldn't not come back to cook! And you're really shameless, actually admitting to going to Wang Mazi's place! The Four-Horse Road prostitutes, sometimes if you pinch their face, they'll still say "I'm embarrassed," but you're even less afraid of embarrassment than them!"

"Sir! It was my fault for not coming back to cook, but please forgive me, my belly is too big. I originally wanted to rush back at noon, but I suddenly felt dizzy and fainted. But you say I'm not as good as the Four-Horse Road prostitutes, and I don't agree with that. They don't have any "embarrassment" at all. They deliberately say they're afraid of embarrassment, but in reality, they're even less afraid of embarrassment."

I didn't want to listen anymore and closed the door. This burst of noise stirred up every nerve in my body. This nanny seems to only understand the algebraic formula: negative plus positive still equals zero. People who are not afraid of embarrassment say they are embarrassed, but their skin is still thick: "The shame of having no shame is also shameless." This formula used in reverse, hatred plus no hatred, national shame plus shamelessness, still equals zero. So, after May 7th and May 9th, even though we lost the Northeast, lost Rehe, lost.... it still doesn't matter.

This statement is so comforting, everyone has lightened the burden of defending against foreign enemies. But "this also makes it impossible not to resent the predecessors: if a group of people hadn't shouted so loudly during the May Fourth Movement, China would not have had any national shame at all. And if China had signed the Treaty of Versailles at that time, Japan might have politely stopped asking for our Northeast after having the benefits of the Twenty-One Demands. Even if they wanted it, with fifteen years of recuperation, fifteen years of lessons, and a long-term resistance effort, we would have already succeeded halfway by now.

Let's not worry about old hatreds. In this annoying weather in May, the days are long and long. If you think about taking a walk in the streets and alleys, you will encounter many shameless child prostitutes, many pregnant servant women selling their bodies for money, many frustrated young men smelling of meat and wine, many foreign ships carrying guns, sailors, and foreign goods, many...... If you say to run to the countryside, you will accidentally step on a dead female baby in the grass, or a strange cannonball with the word "Taisho" on it, or crying and wailing poor people, or...... How can these not stir up people's infinite new sorrow?

You can see that women are inherently unfit to do any great work, whether in terms of intellect or material things... Women are only fit to be nannies and tutors for us in our childhood, because they are childlike, frivolous, and short-sighted themselves. In short, they are just big children for a lifetime, in an era between children and adults."

Second, he said that women's duty is to give birth to children, serve their husbands, and manage household affairs. "Women should pay attention to household affairs, eat their fill, and dress warmly, but they should not mix in society. Religious education should be available, but they cannot read poetry, prose, or politics. Except for religious or cooking books, all other books are forbidden to read."

Third, he opposed women's equality, his reason being: "In this world where monogamy prevails, after a person marries, his rights are reduced by half, and his obligations are doubled. Since the law gives women equal rights with men, the law must also give them a kind of masculine knowledge. But the honor and rights that the law gives to women exceed those that the creator gave to them. The more laws are made, the fewer women are able to enjoy these rights. All the natural rights of the rest of the women

are deprived by the few in the upper class."

Fourth, he argued that women should not have inheritance rights. The reason is: "Property is obtained by men through hard work over a very long period and suffering great pain. If this property later falls into the hands of women, they do not know the value of money and spend it all within a very short period in a muddleheaded way, which is extremely inappropriate, but such things often happen. To prevent such things from happening, women's right to inherit should be limited."

Fifth, he advocated polygamy, his reason being: in countries with polygamy, every woman has a master, but in countries with monogamy, the number of women who can marry is limited, leaving behind a large group of women who have no place to live and no one to support them. If these women belong to the upper class, they will live in comfort and become useless old maids. If they belong to the lower class, they will have to do hard work that they are not fit for, or become prostitutes, and their lives will be miserable, with no joy or dignity. "Therefore, from the perspective of women as a whole, polygamy is indeed a real benefit. And from that perspective, if a man's wife is old and sick, or cannot have children, or is too old, why can't he marry a second one?"

Schopenhauer's remarks can still find many, many sympathizers in our country today. However, the wheel of history is moving forward relentlessly. Each of the above opinions of Schopenhauer has now been overturned by facts, and there is no need for us to waste our ink here to refute him. What is worth our attention here is that the great British and French thinkers of Schopenhauer's time mostly advocated women's liberation. Why are Schopenhauer's views so conservative and reactionary?

People's will does not determine their lives, but rather their lives in society determine people's will. The root of Schopenhauer's reactionary and conservative thoughts should naturally be sought in the social and economic conditions of Germany at the time and in his personal living environment. At that time, Germany was still a completely feudal system, economic life was still滞留在serfdom, and male chauvinism and patriarchal ideas enveloped the entire society. Moreover, Schopenhauer grew up in a landlord's family, all of which could not but be reflected in Schopenhauer's thoughts.

Secondly, Schopenhauer's entire ideological system is reactionary, idealistic, and pessimistic. He believes that the world is just people's will and ideas; life is a vanity and chaos, in which living things struggle with each other and destroy each other; to escape the hell of existence, one can only overcome the will to live, only by suffering. This kind of thinking cannot but determine his conservative attitude towards women's issues.

Thirdly, his life was also very secluded and lonely. He did not have a single close friend in his life, whether male or female. He only had a dog, which never left him. This lonely life was also a major reason for him to despise women and oppose women's liberation.

Here, from the ideological systems of Schopenhauer and the several thinkers mentioned earlier and their opinions on women's issues, we can draw a conclusion in principle: those who are ideologically conservative are bound to oppose women's liberation. Conversely, those who advocate women's liberation, their entire ideology must also be progressive. We can get sufficient evidence of this conclusion later.

Women and the Law 220

— Bi Yun

-- Understanding the relationship between women and the law from a historical perspective

We must first ask: what exactly is the law? Most legal scholars or legal philosophers generally believe that law is a kind of "norm" that "regulates" the relationship between people, and an effective tool to protect the inherent rights of "the people" and to punish those who infringe on these rights. Therefore, they sing praises of the law as sacred, and the "equality" of the people before the law is true equality. But from the perspective of modern social science, the so-called law is, in fact, nothing more than a complex means used by a group of people who control the economy and politics in a certain society to protect their own special rights. Obviously, under this complex and sanctimonious means, countless people are being sacrificed. Needless to say, when those who are sacrificed rise up to protest or demand that the law pay attention to their rights, the law sometimes has to show them a little concession. That is to say, as history progresses, the law cannot but gradually want to broaden the scope it protects and narrow the limits of its sanctions. Therefore, historically speaking, the law itself is also an evolving thing, and can even accurately reflect the stage of social evolution and the depth of social relations.

When did the law first become related to women? To answer this question, we cannot but look back at history. We know that there was a period in human society, and a very long period, when there was no law. That is the primitive society and the clan commune society. At that time, people were jointly producing and jointly consuming, and the phenomenon of inequality between people had not yet occurred. People lived in the embrace of nature, and the relationship between them was extremely simple, so there was no need for that complex and sanctimonious "regulator" -- the law. But at that time, the people -- including women -- were truly equal to each other. Since the feudal demons changed the original social organization, they plundered the property of the majority of people by means of cruel force, and created

a kind of political power, for the first time dividing human beings into various classes of exploiters and the exploited, and oppressors and the oppressed. At the same time, women were also generally despised and oppressed. In order to prove the legitimacy of their special rights in front of the exploited and oppressed, the demons created the law for the first time, and the law took care of the heads of women for the first time. Naturally, the law in feudal society was only an extremely crude prototype, mostly mixed with the traditional customs of the time, the doctrines of religion, and the orders of feudalism, and was very far from modern law. Therefore, what the law at that time gave to women was not the protection of their rights, but cruel punishment and brutal insult. For example, the "seven grounds for divorce" for married women in our country in the old days was as brutal and cruel to women as a killing machine. I don't know how many women were sacrificed on this killing machine.

However, thanks to the unremitting progress of history! In the 18th century, the Industrial Revolution occurred in England, and at the same time, the Democratic Revolution broke out in France, which opened a new era in human history. On the one hand, the giant arm of the Industrial Revolution liberated women from the narrow and tragic shackles of the old family, sent them to work independently in various productive enterprises, and introduced them to

gradually enter various social occupations. In this way, a part of women gained considerable economic independence. On the other hand, the democratic bombs of the French Revolution fiercely bombed the centuries of barbaric despotism. Politically, the banner of "men are born with the right to freedom and equality" (Article 1 of the "Declaration of the Rights of Man") was also raised high, and the principle of "all people are equal before the law" was marked out. At this time, women were publicly recognized as equal to men for the first time, and were able to enjoy equal rights with men in law. This is a great progress after all! But since then, what exactly have women actually gained from the legal aspect? Have they really achieved complete liberation since then? This is a question worth studying. Due to the limited scope of this article, I can only end here!

Mother's Musings 221

— Zhan Quan

"Having been a mother for eight years now," due to a lack of good education, environment, and living conditions, our children have grown up in a precarious manner without proper upbringing. When the children's father was still alive, our life was entirely unstable. Amidst the tumultuous times, the children were deprived of the happiness and peace they deserved. In the past two years, since the burden of life fell upon my bare shoulders, I have been struggling to make ends meet under the lash of life, let alone any education or ideals. Yet, precisely because of this, the sensitive mother's heart is constantly surging with endless thoughts. If I were to put them to pen and paper, I might be able to produce a few seemingly ordinary yet meaningful pieces of writing. "Mother's Musings" is born out of this motivation.

XXXX

(1) On Stealing

The day before the start of spring break, I went to a small school to pick up my eldest son who was boarding there. During a conversation with the teachers, I learned that he had been behaving improperly lately (it is said that the teachers were reluctant to openly use the word "stealing" to the family. On the monthly school report, they only vaguely filled in "casually taking other people's belongings," but in reality, they wanted the family to understand the meaning of "stealing"). This news made me, who was struggling in poverty and trying to be an honest person, feel extremely ashamed and indignant. I really wanted to give him a good scolding upon returning home, but then I thought that a seven- or eight-year-old child does not understand the difference between right and wrong, and is born in an environment with strong material temptations, so threats are not as good as reasoning.

Starting with the "distinction between self and others," I extended it to "propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame," doing my best. But my child seemed to have a natural expression of half-knowing and half-believing. In order to satisfy his childish material desires, I automatically increased his daily allowance from six copper coins to nine, which was naturally the best I could do. But the child was not satisfied, grateful, or joyful, which started to surprise me. I repeatedly pressed him for the reason, and his clear answer made me suddenly understand the core of the problem. However, to eliminate his bad habit, I had to say sternly, "They are them, and we are not the same as them. They can be extravagant, but we shouldn't follow them. There are people who don't even have food to eat, and you're still not content!"

In the depths of my heart, I have a clear understanding of this problem: "What is nine copper coins? Others have two dimes! They buy cakes and pastries, and so much candy!" As the child said, there are many people in this society who enjoy absolute comfort, making the poor drool and their eyes burn with envy. The child, the child understands nothing of fate or destiny, such profound "worldly wisdom." If others have good enjoyment, why shouldn't they have it themselves? If they don't have good enjoyment like others, why shouldn't they use some means to get it? So-called stealing, so-called robbery, honestly speaking, would not arise without the unequal distribution of society. Then, if you want your son to stop committing crimes (?), first you have to find a way to make him not feel the lack of life, at least passively prevent those with money from having excessive enjoyment! Do you understand that these are impossible to do for a while? Then shouldn't you plant some clear and reasonable basic awareness in his mind? Due to the so-called combination of force and reason, making him distortedly understand some of the principles of being a loyal and weak class, making his spirit forever trapped in shackles, his life tolerantly tasting the bitter juice, does our society need such a child?

"Others have money, so they should live comfortably. We are not worthy to be compared with them. Others have money, so there is no need to talk about thrift, but we should be content. Even if we have no food to eat, it is destined by fate..." Ah! How ashamed! I taught my son such a great way of obeying fate, being content with one's lot, admiring the rich and despising the poor! (End of this section, the entire article is not finished.)

After Marriage (Continued) 222

— Lian Sheng

Even worse, he blames me for making the wrong decision. With my looks, I could have married a rich young man, then I could enjoy myself every day, how pleasant! How satisfying! I really wanted to slap him. He shouldn't say such things to me. But I just smiled. Endless pain, endless grievances, only to be endured in my heart. What else can I say? I don't want to say anything either.

I understand, I understand, I am just a weak person, the weakest of the weak.

Before, the ideal married life... Now, it's all turned into illusion! I only deeply feel the etherealness of life! Unrelated!

In this world, how many happy marriages are there? I am confident: I still love him, and he deeply loves me. Although, the time for us to separate is coming soon!

Here, there is no crying, no tears. Only picking up endless hidden pain to seek happiness for society, to serve society.

Marriage, how many people's youth has it buried? From my personal observation, I have lost courage, passion, and struggle because of marriage...

There is only seeking a way out in society. Marriage is a dead end for us women! I understand, I deeply understand -

Securities Chips Loose and Abundant

Yarn Market Slightly Declines After Rise; Daily Fluctuations Reach Over One Yuan 230

The yarn market remains firm, due to brisk sales of spot yarn. Demand for coarse yarn in North China is very strong, and stocks at various factories are dwindling daily. At the same time, the selling price of Japanese yarn is rising, which is driving up the price of Chinese yarn. Short covering is occurring. However, rumors circulated later in the market that the Shenxin factory was releasing 6,000 bales of "Red Man Bell" yarn, causing a softening trend at the third closing. It is said that the market will be closed on May 9th in commemoration of National Humiliation Day.

Golden Rooster Yarn: Near Month Rises, Distant Month Falls 231

At the opening of the forward yarn market, the lack of major sellers caused prices for all months to rise by about one yuan. As speculative buyers closed out their positions at the second and third sessions, prices fell again. As a result, prices for all months rose by only 1.2 or 3 dimes. The market remained tight after the afternoon opening, but factory rumors surfaced mid-session, causing a softer close. Prices for all months rose by 1.3 or 4 dimes, with the far month falling by one dime. Total daily trading volume was 57,600 bales. Sales included 1,150 bales from Tongfu, 1,000 bales from Tongji, 750 bales from Hengyi, 1,050 bales from Changji, 1,100 bales from Yuanda, 650 bales from Changyu, and 750 bales from Huikang. Purchases included 1,050 bales from Renfeng, 650 bales from Dafu, 3,250 bales from Dafeng, 1,050 bales from Mingde, 1,200 bales from Yuande, and 2,450 bales from Shenji. Cotton Market: Rising Trend Continues 234

The cotton market is rising sharply, due to the rebound in American cotton. Japanese merchants are purchasing heavily in the forward cotton market and also buying spot cotton outside the market. As a result, the supply side suddenly tightened and buying intensified. However, large short sellers still have no intention of covering.

Japanese Merchants Buy American Cotton on Dips 238

A New York dispatch on the 4th reports on the cotton market for the week: Last week, the cotton market fell due to long liquidation and manufacturer selling. Southern selling was not heavy. Selling pressure gradually decreased when prices fell below 11 cents, and industry participants also absorbed some supply. However, buyers failed to follow foreign cotton upward in the second half of the week, causing slight price discrepancies. The main buyers throughout the week were Japanese merchants who bought on small dips. Other factors await developments in Washington regarding the silver issue, as well as new crop harvests and the overall cotton industry situation. Cloth trading is sluggish, and talk of factory production cuts is increasing.

American Cotton Rises Over Thirty Points 239

Yesterday's American cotton market was firm due to good news from Liverpool, foreign buying, and a lack of sellers. Spot prices rose by 30 points and futures prices rose by 29 to 33 points. Liverpool spot cotton fell by 4 points and futures rose by 6-7 points. Egyptian cotton spot fell by 2 points. The Bombay cotton market rose due to European exporters buying old cotton, but this was offset by long profit-taking. As a result, Pinga fell by 2 rupees and 7.5 annas, Omra fell by 3 rupees, and White Row Creek fell by 3 rupees and 2.5 annas. (Telegraph Dispatch from the 4th).

Silk and Tea: Pessimism Mounts in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Regarding Spring Silkworms 240

Continuous Rain and Cold, Stuffy Weather Cause Changes

Lanxi: Lanxi in Jinhua, Zhejiang, has the earliest silkworm season. This year's silkworm farming is less successful. Native breeds account for 40-50% of hatching. Due to the lingering cold, ant collection was late. In addition, continuous rain and low temperatures caused early silkworms to develop diseases such as "yellow discharge," "black vomit," and "white muscardine" during the third sleep, peak leaf-eating stage. Losses reached 70-80%, so farmers supplemented with late silkworms and bred improved varieties. The silkworm season was later, but the weather was still unfavorable. High temperatures caused black and brown spots to appear on the bodies of 2nd and 3rd instar silkworms. They moved slowly and ate less. The stuffy weather caused many silkworms to stop eating and die. However, losses among late-stage (improved variety) young silkworms are still minimal.

Chongde: Farmers have suffered consecutive silkworm crop failures. The late sprouting of mulberry buds due to the spring cold delayed and unevened out hatching. Native breed silkworms are mostly turning yellow. In areas around Tujia Dam and Fujia Bridge, improved varieties are being bred to supplement. Ant emergence is also uneven. Early stage silkworms are starting their second sleep, while late stage silkworms have only been eating leaves for 6-7 days. Recently, prolonged rain has delayed silkworm dormancy and reduced appetite. There are occasional occurrences of "grasserie" disease, which spreads rapidly. Measures are being taken to isolate infected silkworms and thoroughly disinfect the silkworm rearing room and equipment to prevent further spread.

Yuyao: In areas such as Tianyuan City and Linxi Township, many farmers raise their own native breeds. After ant collection, the weather was abnormal, with fluctuating cold and warmth. During the second and third sleep, eating rain-soaked leaves caused diarrhea and foul-smelling deaths. Therefore, farmers in Henghe Town, Kan Town, and Xiaolu Town are supplementing with improved varieties. However, the cold and rainy weather is delaying development. Recently, the stuffy weather has caused black spots and brown patches to appear on the bodies of silkworms in the second sleep that have fully eaten their leaves. Third sleep silkworms are delaying molting and refusing to eat for a full day and night. The current situation is dire.

Zhenjiang: In the model sericulture area, farmers are raising silkworms later this year due to the cold weather. Hatching takes 14-15 days and silkworms have not yet emerged. Efforts have been made to increase temperature using fire, but ant collection is uneven. Early stage silkworms have fully eaten leaves in their first sleep, while late stage silkworms have just started eating. Mulberry trees in the four rural areas are not sprouting well and leaves are only the size of silver dollars. Recent continuous rain and cold weather have hindered silkworm rearing. Farmers are feeding chopped improved mulberry leaves to silkworms. However, early silkworms are showing signs of leaf stagnation and sleeplessness.

Wenzhou Black Tea Arrives But Not Yet Open for Sale 241

The Gong Sheng Yong Tea Firm in this city recently transported two boxes of new black tea from Wenzhou, totaling 121 cases. After extracting samples, many foreign firms made counter offers, but Chinese tea merchants refused to sell due to high transportation costs. The new offers have not yet been released.

Suian Rough Tea Slightly Declines 242

Since the opening of Suian's new green tea season last week, cold weather has hampered the flow of goods. Tea merchants from various regions, eager to get ahead of the competition, have been willing to pay higher prices to secure supplies. As a result, the price of rough tea rose to the 90 yuan mark. Upon learning of this market situation, Shanghai tea merchants immediately telegraphed to curb prices. It is now heard that tea prices in that region have fallen back by 10-20 yuan, and the situation is easing slightly.

Grain and Flour Merchants Continue to Sell Off Stock 243

Yesterday's flour market showed a stable trend for all months after the morning opening. The price of foreign wheat was about 5-6 dimes higher for Chicago wheat and about 3-4 dimes higher for Canadian wheat. Despite stable prices after the opening, market sentiment was difficult to stir. Domestic consumption was affected by the rural recession and the general decline in commodity prices. Although manufacturers requested the government to maintain the market, this has not been very effective. The actual difficulties are difficult to solve with simple words. By the afternoon opening, the near months showed a weak trend due to factory offerings. The distant months were absorbed by outsiders, showing initial signs of improvement. However, after the fourth session, prices declined due to continued selling by most manufacturers. It is unclear what motivated manufacturers to both request support and continue selling. However, their position is contradictory. As a result, the current month rose by 5 li, while June/July fell by 2.5 li, August fell by 7.5 li, September fell by 1.25 cents, and October fell by 1 cent.

Futures Wheat Rises in the Morning, Falls in the Afternoon 244

Yesterday's futures market initially showed a firm trend in all months after the morning opening. The price of foreign wheat rose by about 5-6 dimes for Chicago wheat and about 3-4 dimes for Canadian wheat. Coupled with continuous rain, market sentiment among both industry insiders and outsiders was relatively stable. As a result, the market was bullish after the opening, with prices rising by 2-3 cents. However, by the afternoon opening, the weather gradually cleared and the rain stopped, causing market sentiment to soften again. Current buyers seem powerless. Interior merchants are naturally inclined to sell as the new wheat crop is approaching the market. Longs are less attentive due to the influx of factories. Therefore, the future is still very concerning. As a result, June fell by 1 cent, July rose by 1 cent, August remained unchanged, and September/October did not open. The spot wheat market stagnated due to factory stoppages, with no activity. However, warehouse inventories are gradually increasing and are said to have reached about 100,000 bags.

Late Rice Sales Sluggish, Continuing Small Declines 245

(South Shanghai) Yesterday's supply included late rice of the 18th and 19th grades, thick japonica, and various colors of the 4th and 5th grades (totaling over 3,000 shi). Sales of late rice to both northern and southern merchants have stopped. Although there is some sporadic buying, the market is currently weak. At closing, southern merchants bought a small amount, about 200 bags, followed by northern merchants who bought 200-300 bags. Therefore, the price of Qingjiao, Sifeng, and Liantang etc. continues to decline slightly. Thick japonica remains stable due to limited supply. Duyangjian also saw no changes, and Yinbian Yuan remained unchanged.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday's shipments from Hexia were limited, about 30 boats. Sales of white japonica, foreign sharp rice, white yuan, Dujian, thin rice, and Shi Qiao were slightly active. The market lacked supply of early rice and Yin Yuan. High-grade white japonica was stable, but mid-grade and low-grade prices declined slightly. Sheep sharp rice also declined by 3-5 points. White Yuan and thin rice were firm. The price of Dujian increased by 3-5 points. Port and guest sharp rice remained stable.

Rough Foreign Rice Rises Another Half Dime 246

Mechanized rice is in short supply, soaring 3 dimes. Yesterday's supply of guest indica rice was limited and inventories are dwindling. Sellers are hoping for better prices and continue to raise prices. However, buyers, due to consecutive days of price increases, were hesitant. Merchants from Nan Shao and Quanzhou stopped buying immediately. Therefore, Fuzhou only handled about 400 bags of rough indica rice and 240 bags of mechanized rice yesterday. Local merchants in this city also slowed down purchasing due to high prices. However, merchants from Shantou, Wenzhou, and other inland regions, who had stopped buying for several days, saw the brisk sales in Fuzhou and this city and the soaring prices, and dared not inquire. After the local merchants in Fujian slowed down purchasing yesterday, they took the opportunity to buy. Merchants from Tianjin also purchased 200 bags of Wuxi mechanized rice. Mechanized rice is in short supply at both river factories and warehouses. The price opened at 9.5 yuan yesterday, a huge increase of 3 dimes compared to the previous day. Warehouse holders were slightly less interested, but local village sales remained active. Together, merchants from Wenzhou, Shantou, the interior, and the northern ocean bought about 3,000 bags. The market for guest indica and mechanized rice is temporarily stable. However, the price of reclaimed rough foreign rice opened at 5.4 yuan for 500 bags of Siamese rough rice, another increase of half a dime. There is a large inventory of small-kernel rice, so it is temporarily stable.

Sugar Market: Domestic Sliced Green Sugar Continues to Open with 300 Cases 247

In yesterday's sugar market, tariffs rendered Customs Gold without a market. Forward Gold remained flat with little change in trend. The association's price for No. 24 coarse sand white sugar remained unchanged with no transactions. The firm's stock of 21.2 yuan drew some offers. Eight and nine grade Dutch red sugar, Taikoo Sugar B mark, and domestic factory white sugar all saw little activity. Domestic Chaozhou green sugar opened with only 100+ bags for extraction at 11.8 yuan. A Guangzhou firm opened with 300 small cases of sliced green sugar at 9 yuan. A Huizhou white sugar opened with 100+ bags at 17 yuan.

Inventory of Dried Lily Flowers is Low in Both Northern Provinces 248

New crop not expected for two more months... Further price increases still expected.

Since the price increase, dried lily flowers have seen declining sales due to a lack of sustained demand. However, market supply is confirmed to be low, at no more than 800 bags. Based on past sales volume, a market price of 20 yuan should have been reached long ago. However, this year's demand has been intermittent, leading to irregular price fluctuations. Currently, only Guangdong merchants occasionally purchase small amounts, with little activity from other regions. The trend is toward stabilization due to low inventory. If sales pick up, the price of 20 yuan is still possible. The new crop is not expected for two more months, and the cost of new goods is estimated to be above 20 yuan.

Wang Jin Corrugated Iron Still Sees Strong Sales 249

Hardware trading was very quiet yesterday. The overall market was dull. However, sales of corrugated iron were relatively good. Trading was quite lively, with 700-800 dan offered. Buyers were Qingdao and Tianjin merchants, with little interest from the local market due to the abundance of Eastern goods. Prices were estimated at 13.85 yuan per box for 28-gauge, 13.3 yuan for 26-gauge, 12.4 yuan for 24-gauge, and 12.25 yuan for 22-gauge, a slight increase of 2-3 dimes compared to the previous standard. It is heard that the price of Eastern goods has also increased due to the Eastern exchange rate, resulting in limited trading.

Small Guangzhou Leather Enamelware Factory Purchases 200 Cases 250

Since northern merchants stopped buying, the small Guangzhou leather market has been quiet for a long time. Yesterday, a enamelware factory bought 200 cases, revitalizing the market. Prices were 10 yuan per dan.

Oil Market: It Remains Difficult to Expect Lower Prices for White Tung Oil 251

After the price of white tung oil in Hankou foreign firms rose to 28 yuan per picul last week, it quickly fell back to 28 yuan, then 27.8 yuan. Foreign firms, seeing the market trending downward, stopped purchasing in hopes of lower prices. However, after holding for a week, the situation remains unusually stable. Although foreign firms have stopped purchasing, the supply remains low, making it difficult for trading to slow down. Hankou's inventories remain low. Incoming goods are not willing to be sold at lower prices. The southern branch firms have raised their offers to 22.8 yuan for goods including tax, and 22.8 yuan for goods without tax. Xiang Tung is offered at 23 yuan, a buyer's price. Overall, the yield was only 50% last winter, leading to a large decrease in production. Therefore, sellers are very firm. As a result, the market is unlikely to see lower prices even if foreign firms continue to refrain from trading. If foreign trading resumes, the upward trend may continue unabated. Zhejiang tung oil has gradually risen due to the influence of the Hankou market. Recently, firms in this city have purchased several hundred piculs from Zedong, with prices ranging from 22.2 yuan to 22.5 yuan. The price of Jiangjia is heard to be 23 yuan.
