Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Chat

Exclusive Control, Joint Management, and the Way Out for the Nation 253

— Song Fen

Editor's Note: This piece was handed to the editor in person by a reader who said that he could no longer contain his indignation at the increasingly perilous situation in China recently. He said that this short essay was written with the utmost and purest patriotic fervor, and he hopes for the readers' earnest criticism, and even more hopes that it will resonate with the readers. We absolutely share Mr. Song's sentiments and firmly believe that readers will as well. However, at the same time, we must also consider, what use is merely impassioned indignation! What we need most is to find a way to encourage the people of the whole country to actively rise up and urge the government to act as a shield for the people and to break through this depressing predicament.

Opening the newspaper on May 1st, the eye is already filled with alarming news, as if unfolding a broken and tragic picture of China's current state.

Since September 18th, the policy of passively accepting aggression has resulted in not only what Mr. Pierson, a Far Eastern problem expert from the United States, stated in his official report to the Foreign Policy Association: "Japan's recent occupation of Manchuria and Jehol, the extent of the land, is equivalent to the 2.4 million square miles that China has lost in the ninety years since Britain annexed Hong Kong in 1842." This is still comforting our dear compatriots who cherish a false sense of pride! If we are unwilling to deceive ourselves and acknowledge the facts, consider Japan's actual control of North China, Britain's seizure of Xikang and Panhong, the Sino-British meddling and attempt to establish an independent Muslim state in Xinjiang, France's occupation of the nine islands of Qiongnan, as well as the strengthening of British influence in Sichuan and Guangdong, French influence in Yunnan and Guangxi, the United States' monopoly in national aviation and general transportation, especially the Japanese Foreign Ministry spokesperson's open declaration on April 17th of exclusively controlling China... If we temporarily close the book on all these facts and take stock, we will realize that the tragedy of national subjugation and the extinction of our race has long been a deeply felt pain for us for the past three years. Even before our children are born, their fate as slaves has already been arranged by the enemy.

Like today's special dispatch, Legislator So-and-so's observation that "China will definitely not be subjugated in the short term, because the country is too large, and Japan cannot swallow it in one gulp no matter what" is like a blind man fortune-telling; as for the argument that Japan's "increasing aggression can inspire national spirit," it is as if the tyrannical Japan's unbridled invasion and our own servile obedience have not yet reached the stage of perfect merit. This is simply the "sound of a dying nation"—

The dissemination of this kind of humiliating thought and the means of Japan's revised statement have the exact same purpose: to deceive us into bowing our heads and stepping into the colonial hell from which there is no return! Know that even if Japan's statement of revision is out of sincerity, it is also to alleviate the atmosphere in Europe and America, a way of peaceful partition of spoils. The British Foreign Secretary announced clearly in the House of Commons: "Equal rights and principles in China are guaranteed by the Nine-Power Treaty in extremely clear terms," except for "special rights possessed by Japan that are recognized by other countries," "Japan cannot be recognized as having the right to unilaterally decide on any special actions, such as a banking consortium." Here, the invocation of the Nine-Power Treaty is not to protect China's territorial integrity but to carve up China, this fat sheep, and everyone should have a share, and Japan should not swallow it alone. "The British government has resolved, to the greatest extent possible and in the spirit of international cooperation, to assist China's progress towards peace and prosperity and towards harmony and goodwill in the Far East," etc. This is the diplomatic language of Sir John Simon, which, translated into Japanese, means: Under Japan's exclusive control of China, the principle of the open door must be recognized, so that European and American powers have the opportunity to jointly manage China. Japan has special rights, and European and American powers have general rights; the ones who are always slaves are China and the Chinese people! Under Japan's exclusive control, China is subjugated and the Chinese people are slaves; under the joint management of the powers, China is still subjugated, and the Chinese people are still slaves. Which kind of slave do we, the Chinese people, want to be? Or, do we not want to be any kind of slave and seek our own path to survival?

If 400 million Chinese people are unwilling to be slaves, no matter how fierce the enemy in the world is, they have no way to force us to be slaves! The past policy of non-resistance has in fact led to exclusive control and joint management. We must wash away the "non-resistance doctrine" that leads to national subjugation. The only way out for the nation is "resistance." He comes with a punch, and I go with a kick. You cannot talk about morality and benevolence to jackals and wolves. We must recognize that the greatest enemy of the nation at present is tyrannical Japan. Resisting tyrannical Japan is the greatest task facing the nation. Revive the movement to boycott Japanese goods to stop the dumping of Japanese goods; develop the war of the volunteer army to drive out Japanese ruffians and retired officers in China; confiscate all Japanese enterprises in China to respond to Japan's seizure of Chinese land and property; mobilize the nation's military and financial resources to expel the Japanese army in China and recover all lost territories since September 18th. We use a sacred war of freedom to stop Japan's violent aggression. People across the country, regardless of each other, recognize the current national crisis, put aside everything, and work together wholeheartedly to complete one task: the cause of resisting Japan and saving the nation! Believe in one doctrine: the doctrine of resisting Japan and saving the nation! Those with money contribute money, those with strength contribute strength; the whole country, from top to bottom, men, women, old, and young, unite into a strong army to fight against Japan, with the spirit of disregarding one's own life, the determination to burn the boats, and extinguish the poisonous flames of tyrannical Japan. This is the only way out, the way to victory, for the Chinese nation! The people of the whole country must use the means of punishing tyrannical Japan to denounce the running dogs of tyrannical Japan!

Compatriots across the country, the beautiful mountains and rivers that our ancestors have painstakingly created over thousands of years have been passed down to us. We cannot let tyrannical Japan monopolize them, nor can we let international joint management take place! We must use a glorious, sacred, and righteous national war to extinguish tyrannical Japan, warn the powers, and open up a path to freedom and independence for the nation!

Life

Incense Making Lane 254

— Chen Zhemin

Spring is a season for burning incense. After the Qingming Festival, it is probably the time when incense is most popular in temples. Every year, a certain amount of money is spent on burning incense to worship Buddha, heaven, and ancestors. Although there are no precise statistics, it is undoubtedly a particularly huge number. Superstitious ideas have been slightly reduced due to the progress of material science, but on the contrary, due to the promotion of some powerful people, there seems to be a more rampant trend.

A superficial observation of incense shops and incense making in Shanghai. There are no less than 150 incense shops in Shanghai, and the most are in Nanshi and Zhabei. Pudong's Lanni Ferry, Yangjia Ferry, and Dongjia Ferry, and Huxi's Caojia Ferry, Zhoujia Bridge, and Beixinjing are also numerous. These are incense shops that have their own workshops. From here, we can easily understand the nature of China's semi-feudal society and the deeply rooted superstitious ideas.

I have visited several workshops, and I think that making incense is one of the most arduous and strenuous jobs in handicraft. It is almost unbelievable that their working hours start from one o'clock in the morning and last until five or six o'clock in the afternoon the next day, about sixteen hours a day. Because most stores employ them based on "piecework," calculated according to the piecework system. The more they make, the more they can earn. How can they not desperately sell their lives?

Sometimes, even if they are willing to sell their lives, they may not be able to. Making incense depends on the weather. If it rains and there is no sun, the incense cannot be dried, and they have to stop. During festivals such as New Year, Qingming, Dragon Boat Festival, and Mid-Autumn Festival, the demand for incense is high, and production can be increased; during the rest of the time, such as June, July, September, or October, the demand for incense is low, and they don't need to work hard. For these reasons, they only have about twenty days of work per month on average.

The working process of incense making is extremely unsanitary and very strenuous. The earliest step is mixing the incense. According to the type and fineness of the incense, the appropriate raw materials are mixed evenly. At this time, the mist of incense powder (not the incense powder used by young ladies and wives) will ruthlessly attack your nostrils, your mouth, and your eyes, making you unable to breathe, unable to open your mouth, and unable to open your eyes. They must be familiar with various raw materials and mixing methods. There are several types of raw materials. The most common ingredient is makko powder; the second is elm powder (which is about twice as expensive as makko powder), which is used to increase the viscosity of the incense. Cypress powder is used to make the incense look good and increase the fragrance. There are also joss powder and wood shavings, because wood shavings are cheap and can reduce costs—After becoming familiar with these, one can hope to do well. Otherwise, the incense made will not be good. The boss will not only haggle and deduct from the wages, but also destroy the bad incense and remake it, turning your hard work into nothing.

After the raw materials are mixed, they encounter one of the most serious tasks. That is the work of mixing evenly after adding water. They, like the master chefs who knead dough to make steamed buns, must knead various raw materials left and right; and the things in the incense trough that absorb their energy are so many that they must take off their shirts (even in winter) and use all their strength to continue working hard for more than three or four hours to succeed. You can see steam coming out of their entire bodies: although their strong muscles are full of power, as soon as you see them panting non-stop, you will know that this is not a job to be taken lightly.

This is often a task that should be done before noon. After kneading, put it in the open air to dry, and then they can go to have dinner and sleep. They go to bed at six or seven o'clock because the work of pulling incense at one o'clock in the morning is waiting for them. This job is less strenuous, just pulling the incense blocks into strips and placing them on the incense rack, waiting for the morning sun to dry them. However, doing this mechanical and monotonous thing for a long time will make your hands sore and your back ache!

Their skills are very related to their wages. Shanghai incense is much more exquisite than inland incense, and there are more types. Common ones include thread incense, stick incense, coil incense, longevity incense, mosquito incense... Each type has various differences. Not every incense maker knows and is proficient in these skills. For example, many people cannot make mosquito incense or do not make it well. Therefore, there are some levels in skills. The best craftsman is called "Shangzhuang" (top workshop), the slightly worse one is called "Erzhuang" (second workshop), and then there are apprentices. The daily income for hard work is about 50 cents for Shangzhuang, about 40 cents for Erzhuang, and apprentices are usually unpaid. Shangzhuang works an average of 20 days a month, earning about ten silver dollars.

In addition, there is also a type of incense packaging worker, who is hired by large incense shops to produce in large quantities for wholesale to cigarette paper shops and sundries shops. Their reward is one copper coin for packaging each incense stick. They can package five or six hundred incense sticks a day. Isn't that almost two silver dollars a day? Not really. There is not that much incense for them to pack. Incense shops will never leave their cashiers, clerks, and apprentices idle at the counter. This kind of incense packaging work is only available when demand exceeds supply.

Speaking of their diet, I must point out that yellow croaker, spinach, tofu, green vegetables, and pickles are the best. As for entertainment, they have nothing else besides playing cards for a few hundred coins on rainy days.

Current Affairs Research: What is Japan Intending? 255

— Shao

Since the "September 18th" Incident, although Japan has continued to plunder China's four northeastern provinces with bandit-like methods, and has seized many benefits in North China and even South China, at the same time, due to the development of domestic economic panic, political unrest, and the continuous resistance of the Chinese people in the Northeast, and the inability to stabilize the so-called "Manchukuo," Japan has become increasingly mired in a crisis from which it cannot extricate itself. In the conflict of interests between international imperialism in the Pacific and in China, because Japan's ambition to annex China and dominate East Asia has been fully exposed, it has become diplomatically isolated. Under this situation of "domestic and external troubles," Japan, in addition to actively embarking on the road of war to try a final gamble, is also trying its best to take advantage of the conflict between its two major enemies in the Pacific—Britain and the United States—to realize its ambition to dominate East Asia.

However, no matter what, Japan's excessive actions in China have caused great unease to both Britain and the United States. In order to ease its conflicts with Britain and the United States, and to increase the conflicts between Britain and the United States and profit from them, Japan does not hesitate to use flowery language to conduct friendly negotiations with Washington and commercial negotiations with Britain. After the British-Japanese and Japanese-American negotiations had results, and after the so-called diplomatic victory in Tokyo, Japan then proceeded to test whether the attitudes of Britain and the United States towards it were consistent. The League of Nations was at this time conducting "technical cooperation" with China, and banking groups from Britain, the United States, and other countries were planning a private silver company with China, discussing investment in China, "helping China build," and other issues, without inviting Japan to participate; this, of course, gave Japan an excuse. Thus, with a thunderclap, on April 17, the Japanese Foreign Ministry issued a "Declaration on China," stating its "special position" in East Asia and opposing the attempt by other powers to jointly manage or partition China.

This opposition to the so-called "special rights" in China threatens its actions, just as Britain and the United States are dissatisfied with Japan's plunder of the Northeast. This is a manifestation of the conflict of imperialist interests in China; at the same time, in the midst of this, Japan is using astonishing statements and harsh tones to test whether the attitudes of Britain and the United States towards it are consistent, and to determine its policies. At first, London seemed as if a huge bomb had fallen from the sky, expressing great astonishment at Japan's declaration on China, but the atmosphere in Washington was very calm: after Japan explained its declaration on China and superficially revoked its original position, British Foreign Secretary Simon felt that the "incident had come to an end," but the United States, on the contrary, expressed a serious attitude, formally lodging a protest with Japan, opposing the "East Asian Monroe Doctrine" and reiterating the Nine-Power Treaty. --This clearly shows the inconsistency of the attitudes of Britain and the United States towards Japan, indicating the initial success of Japan's trial. The reason why Japan is slow to issue its statement and not to respond to the US note is that it sees that the attitudes of Britain and the United States towards it have begun to show inconsistent situations, and it wants to wait quietly for the growth of the conflict between Britain and the United States, in order to profit from it.

If Britain and the United States cannot consistently maintain the same attitudes toward Japan, then Imperial Japan will use all means to launch a fierce attack on China, pressuring China to break away from the shackles of Britain and the United States, and be completely subject to Tokyo's control. Because although the cunning Japanese imperialism wants to expel British and American forces from China and dominate East Asia, it will never personally come forward to fight Britain and the United States with force unless it is absolutely necessary. It will inevitably pressure China not to accept the aggression policies of Britain and the United States, and even oppose Britain, the United States, and other imperialists, and be completely controlled by Japan. In this way, if it succeeds, it will, of course, be a complete victory for Japan. If it fails, it will be China that suffers, and it will have nothing to do with it. Recently, Japan's increasing troops to North China, putting forward direct negotiations to China, and opening fire in Changshu... all these are concrete manifestations of this conspiracy.

In this situation, what should China do? Seek help from Britain and the United States? They, like Japan, are imperialists, who are always trying to divide or jointly manage, or even exclusively control, China. Therefore, our only way out is in our own struggle. If we do not rise up ourselves, but rely on any imperialist to seek rescue, the result will be national subjugation!

The Effectiveness of Germany's Relief for the Unemployed 256

— Mengbai

Under the administration of the Nazi Party in Germany, great attention has also been paid to the issue of unemployment relief, and since the curtain on the unemployment relief movement has been drawn, considerable results have been achieved. Looking back, in January 1933, the total number of unemployed workers in Germany was 6,000,000, according to statistics. However, at present, there are only 3,250,000 people, and since the German government launched the second unemployment relief worker movement on March 21 of this year, it is expected that the number of unemployed workers can be further reduced by 2,000,000.

According to a report by the Nazi Party Propaganda Committee, since Germany held the unemployment relief worker movement, the record of industrial and commercial bankruptcies has decreased by 46 percent, and in 1933 alone, commodity sales in 1933 also exceeded those in 1932 by 12 percent; as for the turnaround in the factory sector, as of the end of 1933, there was an increase of 140,000,000 marks in capital compared to the end of 1932; the wool textile industry increased by 6.4 billion marks in 1932, and 7.1 billion in 1933.

As stated above, under the vigorous implementation of the unemployment relief worker movement in Germany, the extreme development of industry and commerce, directly and indirectly, has been sufficient to reduce the number of unemployed workers. Looking back at our China, rural bankruptcy, industrial and commercial depression, the number of unemployed people has exceeded that of any country in the world, and neither the government nor society has a way to provide relief to unemployed workers.

Compared with Germany, it is really regrettable!

The Soviet Union's Forest School 257

— Huangyin

At the gate of a shady garden, a rosy-cheeked little girl named Gelya is crying: "I don't want to leave here." Three months ago, a pale and weak girl cried at the same gate, and she refused to go in no matter what.

"Why can Lida, Valya, and Kolya stay in this forest school? I don't want to go home either!"

The crying child's mother was at a loss, but she was still happy because her six-year-old daughter had gained ten pounds in weight after living in this forest school sanatorium for three months.

She didn't want to go home because she had a lot of fun here. Those well-educated nannies gave her pencils and books and taught her to draw trains. Gelya could already recognize the slogan "Fresh air, sun, and drinks give us health" hanging in her bedroom. Every morning, Gelya gently climbed to the rabbit cage without waking others. These rabbits have white fur and red eyes, how cute!

Next to the forest school is a model farm, which supplies the school with milk and food, and also serves as an educational experiment for teachers and children. It was this farm and good nutrition that made Gelya gain ten pounds.

The children eat five meals a day. According to the needs of each child, the doctor prescribes the most appropriate food for them. When the children sleep, the windows are wide open, and even in winter, they have to sleep in a ventilated place for two or three hours during the day.

Because it is surrounded by forests, this school is called a forest school.

Each forest school has a special department on pedagogy, where doctors and educators study each child. They regularly report their observations to the children's parents. These parents are all kinds of people, some are skilled workers, some are cleaning the courtyard, unskilled workers, technicians, doctors, etc., most of them are workers, but the unemployed are not among them, because there has long been no unemployed in the Soviet Union.

The children's parents can come to see them once a month. Because it is a sanatorium, outsiders are not allowed to enter the inner rooms of the forest school. The parents gather in an isolated room. Doctors and educators tell them, and also teach them (the floor washers and unskilled workers) how to educate their children. Therefore, the Soviet Union's forest school is also a school for educating parents.

Fourteen such schools have been perfectly established near Moscow, with fifty to two hundred children each. These schools are kindergarten-like in nature, but the ages range from eight to seventeen.

In the sanatorium, older children study the courses of ordinary schools. The Second Five-Year Plan will greatly increase the number of these forest schools.

Spare Time Coffee Shop

On the Difficulty of Doing Business 258

— Lin Keren

Originally, engaging in commerce was a path to wealth; if business went well, one could become another Tao Zhugong. However, the current situation is somewhat peculiar. Many merchants well-versed in the art of business, many established stores, are not only failing to make money and become wealthy, but are also experiencing a daily decline, even heading towards bankruptcy. According to reports, after the lunar New Year, general stores in Shanghai are finding it difficult to sustain themselves. Not only have many less prominent stores announced their closure, but several large stores with significant influence are also struggling to stay afloat. If not for the court's consideration of the overall situation, they would likely have been declared insolvent due to debt. As for other cities, because their industry and commerce are not as developed as Shanghai's, and everything is less convenient, their commerce is even more desolate. In Xuzhou alone, the mass layoffs and closures of stores have resulted in the unemployment of three to four thousand shop assistants—what is the reason for this? In short, it is because we are currently in a year of panic. In this year of panic, even doing business is very difficult.

Let's discuss this in detail now.

First of all, business, that is, doing business, requires customers. The so-called "those who are skilled in business never lack customers" refers to those who are good at trading and dealing with customers. If a store has no business, it can only close down. In China today, due to the bankruptcy of the rural economy and the sharp decline in general purchasing power, the number of customers in various stores is decreasing day by day. In this situation, if a merchant still follows the usual business practices, demanding a large profit for each item sold, they will face the danger of an empty storefront. Once the storefront is empty and goods cannot be sold, they will face a shortage of cash, hindering economic circulation and leading to bankruptcy. Therefore, in order to boost their business and circulate cash, general merchants have no choice but to lower prices and engage in commercial competition. As a result, phenomena such as buying five feet of cloth for four copper coins, a pencil for two copper coins, and several catties of books for thirty cents have emerged. However, even in such commercial competition, business may not thrive. At the same time, merchants' goods are bought with money, and if they cannot make a profit in this competition, or even lose their capital, they will ultimately have to close down. This is the first reason why business is difficult to do under the current circumstances.

Secondly, because transportation in China is not convenient, the transportation of all goods is very difficult. Coupled with the heavy burden of miscellaneous taxes and duties in various regions and the immature methods of production, this constitutes the excessively high cost of all goods in China. With high costs and few buyers, and competition being so fierce, doing business under these circumstances would likely prevent even the most business-savvy commercial genius from becoming another Tao Zhugong.

At the same time, general merchants rely on loans from money houses and banks to maintain their cash flow. If money houses and banks adopt a particularly conservative policy, refusing to lend to those with less security, many merchants with limited capital will be doomed. Unfortunately, since this spring, money houses and banks, having seen the desolate state of commerce, have indeed adopted a particularly conservative policy, refusing to lend to merchants without special guarantees. As a result, the phenomenon of store closures has become increasingly common. This is the third reason why business is difficult to do under the current circumstances.

In addition, the exploitation of unequal treaties by imperialists, who dump their goods in our country without restriction, is a major cause of the decline of our industry and commerce and the difficulty of doing business.

The difficulty of business is a manifestation of commercial decline; commercial decline is, of course, closely related to the crisis in industry; the crisis in industry and commerce, and the bankruptcy of the rural economy, are the reality of our national economic bankruptcy. The so-called people's livelihood being desolate and social unrest are rooted here. But what is to be done? I have no concrete ideas about this; I only know that these are all the products of China under the current circumstances.

Commentary

After Reading the "Bank of China Business Report" 259

— Lu Yong

The Bank of China is one of the largest banks in the country. Its business report for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933) was published in newspapers a few days ago. In addition to containing a summary of the bank's business operations, it also details various sectors of the national economy. This not only allows us to see the abnormal development of the banking industry, but also reveals the general economic downturn. An analysis is as follows:

1. Abnormal development of the banking industry—At a time when all other industries are declining, the banking industry alone is able to profit. This is something we cannot ignore. Regarding the Bank of China's business overview for the 22nd year of the Republic, solely in terms of deposits and loans, the "total remaining balance of various deposits was 539,284,527.16, an increase of 62,736,473.73 compared to the 21st year of the Republic (1932); the total remaining balance of various loans was 351,388,609.15, an increase of 28,497,391.33 compared to the 21st year of the Republic (1932)." The extraordinary development of business is evident. Other Shanghai Chinese banks have also experienced similar development. According to the end of the report: "The amount of currency issued by Shanghai Chinese banks in the 20th year of the Republic (1931) was 454,143,165 yuan, an increase of over 23 million yuan compared to the 21st year (1932); the total amount of deposits was approximately 210 million yuan, an increase of approximately 100 million yuan compared to the 21st year (1932)." Furthermore, six new banks were established, and existing banks added sixteen branch offices. However, "due to a lack of high-quality and high-profit investments, they tend towards government bonds and real estate; those who pay attention to commerce also focus on the narrow channels of lending, discounting the credit collateral of debtors without careful selection; the unreasonable expansion of credit is increasing day by day." This truly reveals the abnormal development of the banking industry.

Everyone knows that in recent years, bank investment has regarded industry and commerce with fear, let alone agriculture. Therefore, "the only funds available in society are absorbed by high-profit government bonds, and everyone sighs and laments the lack of funds for construction and production." On the other hand, the abundance of floating capital does not indicate an increase in social wealth. This is due to the expansion of rural unrest. Wealthy natives are transferring large amounts of money to the cities, considering it safer to deposit in banks and earn meager interest. However, after this floating capital is concentrated in banks, it is reinvested in government bonds and real estate. Therefore, the profits of the banking industry come entirely from these two aspects. In other words, the issuance of government bonds and the concentration of floating capital are the sources of the abnormal development of the banking industry.

2. The general economic downturn—China is a country based on agriculture, so agriculture constitutes a major component of the national economy. In terms of agricultural production, the food harvest in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), according to various statistics, averaged 6% less nationwide than in the 11th year of the Republic (1922). Other crops such as cotton, tea, and tobacco varied in increase and decrease. Therefore, agricultural imports still reached a huge amount of 400 million yuan. So the rural areas declined to the extreme. However, the reasons for its decline are as follows: "1) the tragic fall of agricultural prices; 2) the increasing burden on farmers; 3) the repercussions of the fall in prices of foreign agricultural products; 4) the unfavorable harvest of agricultural products." However, the government and society did not take many measures to reduce agricultural costs and raise agricultural prices this year. This can be proved by the following facts: "1) the government issued orders to eliminate miscellaneous taxes; but the provinces have not yet taken concrete actions to reduce or eliminate them; 2) financial institutions promoted loans to farmers: each bank either set up agricultural granaries and piloted small loans, or promoted indirect loans through cooperatives; but the total amount was less than six or seven million yuan; 3) the government discussed levying import taxes on foreign rice, but Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian, which import the most foreign rice, have not yet implemented the levy." As for the central and provincial agencies that handle agricultural improvement, their numbers are as follows: 46 for administration and design; 161 for experimentation and research; 30 for promotion; and 58 for agricultural finance. However, all kinds of institutions are financially strapped, small in scale, limited in strength, and slow in progress. Such is the so-called achievement of rural revitalization.

Similarly, industry is also in decline. "Taking the industrial sector as a whole, the 22nd year of the Republic (1933) can be called the beginning of a difficult period for the industrial community. In fact, last year's industry, affected by the rural decline and the global economic panic, has already shown a rapid decline. We can see the extent of its decline simply by looking at the reduction in working hours in cotton mills and the closure of silk mills last year. As for other large and small industries, they are all implementing austerity measures in an attempt to overcome this difficulty. But this is just a dream. Moreover, China's industry has other obstacles and is constantly threatened by two forces: the competition from foreign factories set up in China and the dumping of the same imported goods. In short, the development of China's national industry will always be bound by the economics of imperialism until the forces of imperialism are eliminated.

In addition, in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), international trade: the total import amount was 134,500,000 yuan; the total export amount was 61,100,000 yuan, totaling 195,700,000 yuan, and the trade deficit was 73,300,000 yuan. Compared with the 21st year of the Republic (1932), imports decreased by 18%; exports decreased by 20%; and the trade deficit also decreased by 15%." This sharp decline clearly demonstrates the shrinking of purchasing power and the inadequacy of production. The inability to make up for the trade deficit can be proved by the export of silver.

In short, the abnormal development of the banking industry not only fails to remedy the national economy as a whole, but also contributes to social chaos. At the same time, the general economic depression causes production to be inadequate, unemployment to increase, and the lives of most people to be trapped in extreme poverty, so they have no power to buy their daily necessities. As a result, the sharp decline in international trade is promoted. This overall economic bankruptcy is undoubtedly a very serious problem. ▲Continued on page 5▲

Scientific Miscellany

Electrical Chicken Farming 260

— Yin Hua

Using electricity to incubate eggs and raise chicks is undoubtedly the best method. It allows us to obtain a high-quality and abundant supply of poultry in a very short time. Whether in terms of money or labor, this method is much more economical and efficient than any old-fashioned method. Chick mortality can also be reduced to a minimum.

Although the application of this new method is recent in the Soviet Union, as in other countries, the early research and experimental period has already passed, and it has now become an important sector of Soviet industry.

Until 1930, the Soviet Union had virtually no electrical chicken farms. From 1930 to 1931, several scientific and economic institutions conducted some experiments in this area. By 1932, this research had made great progress. Today, this industry is developing rapidly everywhere.

Experience indicates that the best results can be achieved only by entrusting this type of operation to specialized chicken-raising organizations in various regions. In North Caucasus, Crimea, Ukraine, and other places, egg production is very regular. It is very appropriate to treat these chicken farms as independently operated enterprises in various regions.

This type of important operation is particularly developed in North Caucasus, Armavir, Georgievsk, and other places. The average size of the electrical chicken farms here can raise 45,000 to 50,000 chicks. The largest chicken farms in Armavir and Georgievsk can each accommodate 85,000 chicks.

The Soviet Union now has two different methods of raising chickens. One method involves equipping a five-story chicken house according to the age of the chicks. The first floor houses chicks under twenty days old, the second and third floors house chicks over forty days old, and the fourth and fifth floors house chicks over sixty days old. An electrical pipe runs through the center of the five floors to warm each room. The other method involves installing electric wires on a wooden frame that can be freely moved. The entire frame is also heated by electricity. Comparatively, the latter is simpler and allows for larger-scale farming.

Although the chicken-raising business described above is very new in the Soviet Union, chicken farmers can proudly boast that their efforts have been quite successful. For example, in the North Caucasus chicken farm, out of 13,300 newly hatched chicks, only 800 died within sixty days, which is only 6% of the total.

In order to examine the results of the above-mentioned operations, find ways to eliminate various farming defects (such as chick protection and feed), further develop this business, and formulate some management rules for this business, several meetings have been convened by those in charge, farming workers, and representatives of various scientific research institutions.

In order to avoid farming difficulties, the discussion resulted in a more precise distribution of chick feed and attention to the different protection methods for chicks during each stage of their growth. These are all very scientific.

The Soviet Union's chicken-raising activities in 1932 have already gained valuable knowledge and experience. With broader and more detailed attention in 1933, there is no doubt that the problem of meat supply in the second five-year plan will be solved without difficulty.

Amateur Entertainment

Temple Stage Opera and Open Stage Opera 261

— Yu Si

When it comes to farmers' amateur entertainment, the community opera, which can accommodate hundreds to thousands of people at the same time, is the most popular. Community operas are mostly held in early spring before farming becomes busy, and at the end of autumn after farming is completed. "Grass stage troupes" travel from east village to west village along individual large villages or combined small villages. The villagers in the village where the opera is performed busily and politely invite their old relatives and new friends from various villages in advance. They also rush to the opera to find acquaintances and pull them home, taking out leftover preserved vegetables from the New Year or newly brewed rice wine from the wine jar to entertain guests, wishing them good harvests this year or celebrating the harvest of this season. The opera is crowded with people, with the young excitedly squeezing to the "front of the stage."

The youth eagerly push forward to the front of the stage.

Staring wide-eyed at the "actors" on the stage, those who are pushed aside retreat to the "back rows" and "edges," smiling and criticizing whose daughter is dressed fashionably. Old people with slightly blurred vision and impaired hearing have come, but they can't compete with the young people for watching the opera, so they simply sit under a tree or on a stone farther away from the "stage entrance" to chat with their old friends. Women, both pretty and ugly, except for the young widows who are more "private," mostly wear their most beloved clothes and shoes to show off. When they steal a glance at the "young men" looking at them on the "stage," they take out their handkerchiefs and twist them shyly. Children gather in groups, pushing past the waists of adults, rushing to the "small stalls under the stage." Everyone is so happy and energetic. From the "opening gong" to the "end of the show," it is late at night when they light their "lamps" and go home. The next afternoon, they follow the "opera troupe" to another neighboring village. Watching the opera so happily and energetically is their only entertainment! It is not until the "opera troupe" goes far away, fifteen or sixteen miles away, when they can't get home with a single candle after watching the opera, that they begin their field work or complete the winter storage as if nothing had happened.

Community opera was originally a ceremony to thank the gods and ancestors, but later it also became a kind of human affair. This meaning can be seen in the names "Temple Stage Opera" and "Open Stage Opera." The former is performed on a permanent or temporary stage in front of the main hall of a temple, while the latter is mostly performed in the open air in the wilderness. A shed is set up far in front of the stage to enshrine the gods, which is called "Shed Stage Opera," and the opera performed specifically for human affairs is called "Open Stage Opera."

Temple Stage Opera is performed regularly for the consecration of the Land God Hall, the City God Temple, and other temples, as well as the Wealth God Hall, Guan Yue Shrine, and other temples. Open Stage Opera is performed in early spring to pray for peace and prosperity, and in late autumn to thank the gods for a bountiful harvest, as well as to thank the gods for raising silkworms well, obtaining rain, and saving houses from burning down. More than ten years ago, when the rural economy was still relatively prosperous and farmers could still live in comfort, many human affairs operas were performed, such as when a certain clan's ancestral hall repaired its genealogy, or when a local gentry entered the ancestral hall, they performed operas to show their noble status and prosperous descendants. When someone had a son in old age or recovered from a serious illness, or on occasions such as longevity and promotion, they invited an opera troupe to sing a few operas to show their joy and generosity, and some were also sent as congratulatory performances by relatives and friends. A certain industry, such as plasterers, carpenters, tailors, and other groups, pooled their money to sing an opera, publicly set industry rules, and announced wage increases. Mountains, reed marshes, orchards, fruit orchards, etc., collected some money to sing an opera, publicly extended prohibitions, and agreed that "violators will be fined one opera and several seats of wine." The popularity of these Open Stage Operas not only paid tribute to gods and ancestors, but simply publicly called for entertainment from opera, and used it as a public gathering. Isn't that right, the farmers who work hard all year round need entertainment that can relax their muscles and spirits. As for whether this entertainment itself is toxic, or even after watching this opera, their spirit is oppressed by a certain surname or person, and their life is burdened, they have no time to consider these things.

An ordinary opera is eight acts, commonly known as the first four acts being the "main part" and the last four acts being the "addition." The main part is decided by the gentry and businessmen in the village and written on a water card hanging in front of the stage. The additions are decided by the youths of the village, who naturally choose what suits their tastes best. They don't like the gentlemen's love for the Romance of the Three Kingdoms and talented scholars and beauties. They love the battles and friendships of heroes and good men, and the flirtatious styles of men and women in "Little Cowherd" and "Drum Dance." The gentlemen pretend to be upright and don't watch the addition. A certain surname had a bit of a comical story about the opera when repairing their genealogy. Originally, the "team pullers" routinely took the opera list to ask the clan leader to choose the opera before the opening gong. However, the clan leader, who was older and of a higher generation, didn't know much about opera. Seeing "Cui Ping Mountain" on the opera list, he thought of the mountain directly opposite the ancestral hall, which was said to be related to feng shui, so he chose this opera to open the stage. Although someone discovered that this was problematic, they didn't dare to change it out of respect for the clan leader's face. When it came to the part where Pan Qiaoyun stole the monk Hai and teased Shi Xiu, the clan leader slipped away, and the youths chose obscene operas like Pan Jinlian. Afterwards, the surname was scolded for "performing an opera that shamed the ancestors" because they happened to be named Pan. Similar to this kind of performance related to surnames, it would often turn from a joke into a bloody tragedy. For example, the villages of the Qin, Luo, Cao, Yan, and Pan surnames each had agreements on which operas were allowed and not allowed. For example, Qin village would not perform "Luo Cheng Trapped in the Sand," but could only perform "Luo Tong Sweeping the North." Luo village would not choose "Qin Qiong Selling the Yellow Horse." If Pan village chose "Battle of Wancheng," "Slaying Cao Yi," or "Striking Yan Song," then the people of Cao and Yan villages would not only choose operas like "Capturing Pan Zhang Alive" or "Secret Trial of Pan Jiang" in retaliation, but would also make a ruckus in the opera, stop the performance, and beat anyone named Pan, thus forming a hereditary feud that would prevent intermarriage. This would turn from watching opera for entertainment to being angry and killing each other. However, the selection of operas for thanksgiving to the gods was much more solemn and rigid. For example, "Zhou Hu Achieving Enlightenment" and "Journey to the West" for consecration and temple fairs, "Wei River" and "Water Flooding Jinshan" for rain prayers, "Lady Leizu" for silkworm flower opera, and "Sitora献宝 [Siduoguo Xian Bao?]" for wealth god opera. As for human affairs operas, they mostly chose auspicious operas, such as "Nine Generations of Glory" for giving birth to a son and "killing a son" or "raccoon cat for a prince" for longevity, and avoided "Seven Stars Altar." After watching these old operas many times, the young audience would feel impatient and turn away to find opportunities to fight and make trouble to vent their anger.

Short-armor martial actors, clowns, dan (female) actors, and actors who did good work were the most popular. Everyone understood the mood of supporting an actor. When they were happy, they would throw fruit peels, sugar cane, and even stones onto the stage to express their dislike or appreciation for a certain character. Hua Xin and Cao Cao in "Xiaoyaojin" often got hit by stones.

Miscellaneous Writings

The Apathy of "Oblomov" 263

— Mori Hara

"The True Story of Ah Q," a Chinese novel, is very famous because the apathy of "Ah Q" is hidden in every corner of the Chinese people, from the court to the farmhouse, there is an Ah Q guarding the place. Therefore, when the Chinese are bullied, massacred, or have several provinces seized, they are just like Ah Q, saying "The son beats the father" with a self-satisfied air, while hiding away.

Ah Q is quite formidable in China, but unfortunately, he has Oblomov as his companion.

What kind of person is Oblomov? What are the differences between Oblomov's apathy and Ah Q's apathy? Now let's delve into history, invite Mr. Oblomov out, so we can get to know him, which is both interesting and meaningful. Goncharov, a Russian writer contemporary with Dostoevsky, wrote a novel called Oblomov.

Oblomov is a Russian nobleman with six or seven hundred serfs and moderate wealth. In his early childhood, his creative talents were completely destroyed, and he only dreamed of the vast and tranquil noble manor on the beautiful banks of the Volga River, where there were no railways to disturb the peace of the manor, and the local residents had no "problems" to worry about. Oblomov was provided for by nannies, attendants, maids, and servants. He himself said, "Since I was a small child, have I ever put on my own socks?" Lunch was prepared at breakfast time, and he slept very early after lunch. Later, Oblomov entered university, with a loyal servant following him, and an atmosphere of laziness and sleepiness followed him as well. After listening to a few lectures, the fervent talks with other young friends at night and the vague yearning for ideals often stirred the young man's heart, but the gentleness of the manor and the influence of sleep, laziness, and the feeling of a stable and completely guaranteed life completely extinguished these positive and beautiful impressions. Other classmates were heated in their debates and joined various groups, but Oblomov only watched and asked himself, "What is this all for?" "Why do you want to bother yourself with these things?"

The author's description opens like this: Oblomov had been sleeping in his apartment for a long time, and he was still in bed; several times he wanted to get up, and several times he had already put his slippers on his feet, but after stopping to think for a moment, he shrank back into the quilt. His old servant stood by the bed with tea in his hand, and visitors came to invite him to participate in the annual May Day ride, but he said, "Why? Why should I look for these troubles and run around so hard?"

The pleasure of noble feelings was very close to Oblomov. Sometimes, he hated human vices, deception, sin, and suffering so much that his blood boiled, and he sat up from the bed with excitement, immediately wanting to turn this excitement into heroic deeds. But when the sun was setting, he would turn over and lie on his back again, everything calmed down, and he sadly watched the setting sun.

Moving house, in Oblomov's eyes, was very terrifying and strange, and he always wanted to delay it. His old servant said: "Others also have to move when necessary!"

This "others" annoyed Oblomov very much, and he scolded the old servant, saying:

"Do you know the meaning of the word 'others'?"

"The so-called 'others' are wild, uneducated people; poor and dirty, living in the attic, they can sleep on a carpet, and live on sweet potatoes and herring. Poverty forces them to run around – such people can of course move to their new home at any time. For example, that 甲埃夫, carrying his two shirts wrapped in a handkerchief, can run away. If you ask him, "Where are you going?" He will say, "I'm moving!" The meaning of "others" is like this – do you think I am one of these others?"

Oblomov also said a lot: "'Another person' is someone who polishes their own shoes, puts on their own clothes, ... buys their own things, makes their own fire, sweeps their own floor, and never knows what it means to use servants..." "Yes," the old servant replied, "there are many such people."

"That's right, but me, look, am I one of them?"

"No, young master is not like that at all..."

"Yes, I am indeed not like that! Do I run around everywhere? Do I work? Am I thin? Do I lack anything? I have never suffered from the cold or from hunger, I have never known what it is to lack anything – I have never worked for my own bread, nor have I done dirty work... Good, why do you dare compare me with those "others"?..." The old servant shed tears, and Oblomov said;

"Pull down the curtains, cover me with the quilt, don't let anyone disturb me, I want to sleep for a while, call me back for dinner later!"

Oblomov met a young girl, Olga, because women often like to do rescue work, she decided to save him, but to succeed in love and reach the point of marriage, he must strive to improve himself, break the laziness and monotony of life, but he really couldn't bear these, and Oblomov was frightened back. He finally returned to his Oblomov kingdom, his sofa and his slippers, and Olga left him in disappointment.

After this novel was published in 1859, people all over Russia competed to read and discuss "Oblomovism". Everyone discovered that between himself and Oblomov, there were always some similar conditions. And thousands of young people loved Olga, and her favorite song "Casta Diva" also became their favorite tune.

In the current Soviet Union, especially during the implementation of the Five-Year Plan, in factories, collective farms, and schools, in addition to the Lenin Medal, a kind of "Oblomov Medal" is also popular.

Why is Oblomov still commemorated in the current Soviet Union? Are all the workers in the Five-Year Plan close to Oblomov?

That would be a joke, assuming that the implementers of the Five-Year Plan are close to Oblomov. It is definitely not like this, it is just a punishment, an insult, for a small number of those who do not work hard, just like drawing a turtle and pasting it in the position of a slow worker.

Oblomov represents the degeneration of will, laziness as morality, and conservatism, contempt for passionate activity, etc., a typical character produced under the serf system, but this kind of character has not completely died out in the big world even now. But the serf system is not the only reason for the production of this type; the era of affluence and capital production makes this type never disappear among us.

Oblomov is an ordinary type, a conservative and comfortable type. When a person's life is slightly affluent, he is unwilling to have any changes or to start new businesses, because that will only bring him a lot of unpleasantness and trouble.

He avoids the trouble of planning industries, he does not know what obligatory work is, what the labor of farmers is, when to plant, when to harvest. When thinking of rural life, he only thinks of beautiful gardens, picnics in the forest, and idyllic walks with a beautiful and plump wife; how and why property came into his hands, why so many people work hard for him alone, these have not bothered his mind.

Among intellectuals, in society, and in personal life, even now, there are still many, many Oblomovs. For example, in the intellectual world, when they encounter a new idea or proposition, they become uneasy, doubting the reform of society, and a slight mention of change frightens them, and love frightens them as well.

In great China, there are especially many Oblomovs, even to the point where a person possesses both Ah Q and Oblomov characteristics. However, there is a slight difference here. Oblomovs are all upper-class wealthy classes. The New Life Movement has no impact on the Oblomovs. They are fundamentally afraid of "new," afraid of "movement," and even more afraid of "exercise." If Ah Q changed his mind, and instead of offering his right cheek when someone slapped his left, he raised his fist, then the Oblomovs would disappear, right?

If a detailed statistic were to be made now, investigating all the Ah Qs and Oblomovs in the country, and then making an Ah Q medal and an Oblomov medal, and awarding them separately, this kind of New Life Movement would be very unique indeed.

Sowing Time 264

— Yu Ji

The wheat seedlings are gone, the willow branches are full of tender buds.

The bell in the bottom of the dipper rings busily in the fields, and people are sowing sorghum in a timely manner.

XXX

To buy fertilizer, one must skimp on cooking oil and salt,

To plant sorghum, one cannot vaccinate children; how dare one not plant when it's time to plant? – It is a difficult time, but also a rare time. XXX

People shake the 　, horses pull, the earth lies steadily beneath their feet, sowing the seeds of hope. Who knows what kind of sprouts will grow? XXX

Shaking the 　, talking about life, the thoughts in their minds sprout wildly like grass. "Maybe there won't be locusts this year?" "Can the price of grain still rise?" "The year before last, every liter of sorghum cost one thousand five," "Last year, it could still sell for a thousand," "Right now – spring is already deep," "One liter only sells for four hundred eight!" XXX

The earth lies quietly waiting for people to sow, the sun warmly watches the seeds sprout, but people sow the seeds with perplexity.
